b'Save It Print\nAir Fryer Chicken Wings Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 1 hourOptional Refrigeration time: 6 hours\nThe baking powder trick yields super-crispy wings and is worth planning ahead. But you\xe2\x80\x99ll still have delicious wings without it: Omit the baking powder, but still season the wings with the kosher salt before air-frying them.\nIf you can\xe2\x80\x99t find gochujang, try another favorite sauce for chicken wings and use the same air fryer method.\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the wings:\n3 pounds chicken wing drumettes and flats\n3 teaspoons baking powder\n2 teaspoons kosher salt\nFor the sauce:\n2 tablespoons gochujang\n2 tablespoons soy sauce\n1 tablespoon rice wine vinegar\n2 teaspoons sesame oil\n1 teaspoon sugar\n3 tablespoons butter, melted and kept warm\nFor the sesame mayonnaise dipping sauce:\n1 cup mayonnaise\n1 tablespoon toasted sesame oil\n3/4 teaspoon sugar\n1/8 teaspoon sriracha\nTo garnish:\nThinly sliced scallions, for garnish\nToasted sesame seeds, for garnish\nThin spears of cucumber\nThin slices of radish\nSpecial equipment:\nAir Fryer\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Season and rest the wings: Pat the wings dry, if needed. In a large bowl, add the wings and toss them with the baking powder and salt until evenly coated.\nSpread the wings around the bowl so they are in a single layer and refrigerate them, uncovered, for at least 6 hours and up to 24 hours.\n2 Air fry the wings: Heat the air fryer to 380\xc2\xb0F. Open the drawer and fit as many wings as you can in it without crowding them (for my 4.4-quart air fryer, this was 1-1/2 pounds of wings, or half the batch). Close the drawer. Cook for 25 minutes, shaking the drawer every 5 minutes to shuffle the wings around.\n3 Make the sauce: As the wings cook, make the sauce. In a medium bowl, whisk together the gochujang, soy sauce, rice wine vinegar, sesame oil, and sugar. Set aside.\n4 Make the sesame mayonnaise: In a small bowl, whisk together the mayonnaise, sesame oil, sugar, and sriracha until smooth. Set aside.\n5 Increase the air fryer temp: Once the wings have cooked for 25 minutes, increase the temperature of the air fryer to 400\xc2\xb0F. Cook the wings for another 5 minutes. This gets them nice and brown and especially crispy.\n6 Sauce and serve the wings: Mix the melted butter with the sauce (it might solidify a bit, but the heat of the wings will re-melt it). Add the wings to a large bowl, pour over half the sauce and toss the wings in the sauce.\n7 Serve and eat: Transfer to a serving platter and sprinkle with scallions and sesame seeds, if you like. Serve immediately, accompanied by the cucumbers, radishes, and sesame mayonnaise for dipping.\n8 Cook the remaining wings: Reduce the temperature of your air fryer back to 380\xc2\xb0F. Repeat steps 2 and 4. Toss them with the remaining sauce.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'
b'Save It Print\nAir Fryer Fried Chicken Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 45 minutesMarinating time: 1 hourYield: 10 pieces of fried chicken\nAlternative Pan Fry Method: If you don\xe2\x80\x99t have access to an air fryer, you can make this fried chicken using a traditional pan fry method. Add enough oil to a cast iron skillet so the oil is about 1 1/2 inches up the side of the skillet. Heat oil until it reaches 350\xc2\xb0F. Add chicken pieces and fry for 8 minutes. Flip, and fry for another 8 minutes until golden brown. Test temperature; you might need a few more minutes for the dark meat pieces (thighs and legs).\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the chicken: \n1 4-pound fryer chicken, cut into 10 pieces (2 breasts cut in half, 2 wings, 2 legs, 2 thighs)\n1 teaspoon kosher salt\n1 teaspoon ground black pepper\n2 cups buttermilk\nFor the coating:\n2 cups all-purpose flour\n1 tablespoon seasoned salt\n1 teaspoon kosher salt\n1 teaspoon ground black pepper\n1 tablespoon garlic powder\n1 tablespoon paprika\nSpray olive oil for cooking\nSpecial equipment:\nKrups Air Fryer\nThermapen Instant Read Thermometer\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Marinate the chicken: Season the chicken well with salt and pepper and then add it to a bowl with buttermilk. Chicken pieces should be covered with the buttermilk. Let it sit for at least an hour or up to overnight.\n2 Bread the chicken: To prepare the breading mixture, stir together flour, seasoned salt, salt, pepper, garlic powder, and paprika.\nRemove chicken pieces from buttermilk and shake off any excess; then dip in the flour mix and coat well. Transfer breaded chicken pieces to a clean plate or wire rack to rest.\n3 Air-fry the chicken: You will need to work in two batches if you are doing a full chicken. Spray the basket of your air fryer with nonstick spray. Place half of the pieces in the basket of your air fryer. Try to ensure the pieces don\xe2\x80\x99t touch. Air needs to circulate around them.\nSpray the chicken pieces lightly with spray oil. Place the basket in the air fryer and turn the air fryer to 350\xc2\xb0F. Cook for 14 minutes, then flip the fried chicken with tongs, spray lightly with oil a second time on the bottom side of the chicken, and cook for another 8 to 10 minutes.\nThe half-breast pieces and the wings will be done on the low end of that time range, and the dark meat pieces will need a full 24 to 26 minutes of time to be cooked through. The dark meat pieces should reach 175\xcb\x9aF.\n(NOTE: My method photo here only shows the temp at 148\xcb\x9aF to illustrate that the chicken can LOOK cooked but is actually not cooked through. A meat thermometer is vital.)\nDuring the air frying process, if you pull out the chicken and notice any dry flour spots on the chicken, spray those spots lightly with oil. The breading will never crisp up if it doesn\xe2\x80\x99t have a tiny bit of oil to hydrate it. It will just burn.\n4 Serve: When the fried chicken is ready, let it rest on a plate for a few minutes before serving. Serve immediately with salad, coleslaw, mashed potatoes, or your favorite fried chicken sides!\nCooked fried chicken can be stored in the fridge for 5 days and reheated in a 300\xc2\xb0F oven for 8 to 10 minutes.\nHello! b"Save It Print\nAir Fryer Cranberry Brie Canap\xc3\xa9s Recipe\nCranberries are widely available this time of year, and you can use fresh or frozen for this recipe. And brie is mild in flavor, but when served with foods that are tart (such as cranberries), the creaminess is amplified. Don\xe2\x80\x99t concern yourself with removing the rind from your wheel of brie: it\xe2\x80\x99s completely edible!\nINGREDIENTS\nSpiced Cranberry Sauce\n1-inch piece of ginger, or 1/4 teaspoon ground ginger\n1 vanilla bean, or 1 1/2 teaspoons vanilla extract\n1 (12-ounce) bag (about 3 1/2 cups) fresh or frozen cranberries, rinsed\n1 3-inch cinnamon stick (or 1/2 teaspoon ground cinnamon)\n3 sprigs of fresh rosemary, divided\nJuice of 1 naval orange (about 1 /2 cup)\n1 tablespoon of orange zest\n1/4 cup maple syrup\nPinch of kosher salt\n1/2 cup packed light brown sugar\nCanap\xc3\xa9s\n8 ounces brie cheese, cut into 1\xe2\x80\x9d cubes\n2 (1.9 ounce) boxes fully baked phyllo shells (30)\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1. Prep the ginger and vanilla: Peel and then thinly slice the ginger (using the edge of a spoon is the easiest way). Use a sharp paring knife to split the vanilla bean down its length.\nOpen the vanilla bean slightly to ensure the seeds are extracted during cooking.\n2. Make the Cranberry Topping: In a 3-quart saucepan, combine the ginger, vanilla bean, cranberries, cinnamon stick, 1 sprig of rosemary, orange juice and zest, maple syrup, and the salt.\nStir the ingredients together and heat over medium-high heat for 3 minutes, or until the mixture starts to boil.\n3. Reduce the topping: Reduce the heat to low, and allow the cranberries to cook until they begin to split open. Stirring frequently, cook the cranberries for 8 to 10 minutes, or until they've reduced a bit and thickened to a jelly-like consistency.\nRemove the pan from the stove and add the light brown sugar. Stir constantly to dissolve the sugar and coat the cranberries in a thick glaze.\nAllow the cranberries to cool to room temperature, leaving the spices in it.\n4. Prep your Air Fryer: Set your Cuisinart\xc2\xae Air Fryer Toaster Oven\xe2\x80\x99s function dial to Air Fry and the temperature dial to 300\xc2\xb0F. Remove both the Air Fryer basket and the baking pan from the oven, then turn the on/oven dial to 10 minutes to preheat the oven.\n5. Fill the phyllo cups: While your Air Fryer is heating, fill your phyllo shells with the pieces of brie. It\xe2\x80\x99s easier to leave the shells in the packaging while you\xe2\x80\x99re trying to fill them. Remove the shells from the plastic packaging and arrange them, a dozen at a time, in the Air Fryer basket.\n6. Bake the shells: Place the baking pan, with the Air Fryer basket nestled inside, into the oven in position 1. Bake the shells for five minutes.\nOnce the shells have finished baking, remove them from the Air Fryer Toaster Oven and carefully remove them from the basket. Repeat this step, baking the shells by the dozen, until they are all baked.\n7. Prep the rosemary topping: While the shells are baking, pick off the remaining rosemary leaves in clusters of two or three leaves. Set aside to garnish the canap\xc3\xa9s when you\xe2\x80\x99re done topping them with the sauce.\n8. Top with cranberry sauce and garnish: Once you have baked all of the brie-filled shells, top each with a teaspoon of cranberry sauce, leaving the cinnamon stick, vanilla bean (if you used one), rosemary sprigs and slices of ginger in the pan. Pull out any pieces of rosemary orAny remaining cranberry sauce may be stored in the refrigerator for up to one week.\nGarnish the top of each canap\xc3\xa9 with the sprigs of rosemary leaves you picked earlier.\n9. Serve! These canap\xc3\xa9s are best served immediately, but can be held at room temperature for up to 2 hours.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. b'Save It Print\nHow to Make Crispy Air Fryer French Fries\nPrep time: 1 hour, 10 minutesCook time: 20 minutesYield: 2 to 4 servings\nIf you want to soak these in the morning and air fry them for dinner, you can refrigerate the potatoes in the interim once they\xe2\x80\x99ve been soaked in cold water. Or soak them in the fridge all day in cold water.\nINGREDIENTS\n1 1/2 pounds russet potatoes (peeled if you want)\n2 teaspoons canola oil or other vegetable oil\n1 tablespoon chopped fresh rosemary or 1 teaspoon dried rosemary\n1/2 teaspoon fine sea salt (or regular salt)\n1/4 teaspoon freshly cracked black pepper\nSpecial equipment:\nAir fryer\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Soak the potatoes. Scrub the potatoes clean and slice them long ways, 1/4 to 1/2-inch thick. Soak them in a bowl of ice water for at least an hour, or up to 24 hours (in the fridge) if need be.\n2 Preheat the air fryer: Preheat the air fryer to 390\xc2\xb0F for about 15 minutes.\n3 Dry and season potatoes: Remove the potatoes from the bowl and lay them out on a paper towel or clean kitchen towel. Dry them thoroughly, and then transfer them to a medium bowl and toss them with the oil, rosemary, salt, and pepper.\n4 Air fry the potatoes: Remove the air fryer basket and add the potatoes, positioning them as evenly as you can. Set the timer for 10 minutes and fry the potatoes.\nSlide the basket out, toss the potatoes to redistribute them\xe2\x80\x94you may notice some spots look more air fried than others.\nFry for another 10 to 12 minutes, until they start to look dry and crispy. (If any pieces seem excessively brown, remove them before you turn the fryer back on.)\n5 Serve: Remove from the fryer and place in a serving bowl. Let them cool for a few minutes (I know it\xe2\x80\x99s hard, they\xe2\x80\x99re French fries!) and taste. They should crisp up a little bit as they cool. Toss with additional rosemary, salt, and/or pepper if desired.\nIf for some reason you find yourself in a situation with leftovers, you can refrigerate them, covered for a few days. Simply reheat them in a little oil in a hot cast iron pan or skillet and they\xe2\x80\x99ll perk right back up.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'

b'Save It Print\nAir Fryer Tostones Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 25 minutesSoaking time: 20 minutesYield: About 20 Tostones\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the dipping sauce:\n1 cup mayonnaise\n1/4 cup ketchup\n1/4 teaspoon garlic powder\nFor the tostones:\n3 green plantains\n4 cups cold water\n1 tablespoon kosher salt\n3 tablespoons neutral cooking oil (vegetable, peanut, or coconut oil)\ncoarse salt for sprinkling\nSpecial equipment:\nTostonera, optional\nAir fryer\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Prepare dipping sauce: Whisk together the mayonnaise, ketchup, and garlic powder. Organize in a single layer, leaving a 1/2 inch of space on all sides of the slices to allow the air to circulate properly. The plantain should be a flat 1/4-inch thick disc that holds together.\n7 Air fry the smashed plantains: Return the smashed plantains to the air fryer basket (you may have to work in batches depending on the size of your basket).\nBrush a light layer of oil onto the top side of the tostones and fry for 3 minutes on the first side. Flip the tostones and brush once more with a light layer of oil, then fry for the final time for 4 minutes instead of 3 minutes.\n8 Season the tostones: Immediately after removing them from the air fryer. Serve the tostones with the mayo-ketch sauce while still hot.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. b"Save It Print\nMexican Wedding Cookies Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 18 minutesChilling time: 1 hourYield: 24 to 30 cookies\nYou can substitute any other nut in place of the pecans. Times for toasting in Step 1 will vary based on the size of the nut you use.\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the cookie dough:\n1 cup (115 g) pecan pieces\n1 cup (225 g or 2 sticks) unsalted butter at room temperature\n3/4 cup (85 g) powdered sugar, sifted\n2 teaspoons vanilla extract\n2 cups (280 g) all-purpose flour\n1/2 teaspoon kosher salt\nTo roll the cookies:\n1 1/4 cup (145 g) powdered sugar\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Toast the nuts on the stovetop: Place the nuts in a medium skillet and place over medium heat. Toast the nuts, stirring frequently, until they darken slightly and smell fragrant and nutty, about 5 minutes.\nRemove the pan from heat and let the nuts cool in the pan.\n2 Crush the nuts: Once the toasted nuts are warm to the touch, but not hot, pour them into a quart-size sealable freezer bag. Seal the bag, and then use a rolling pin to roll and crush the nuts until they are crushed into a chunky powder. Set aside until needed.\n(Alternatively, pulse in a food processor until powdery. Be careful of over-processing or the nuts will turn into nut butter!)\n3 Mix the butter and sugar: Place the butter and 3/4 cup powdered sugar in the bowl of stand mixer fitted with a paddle attachment. Beat together on medium speed until the sugar is absorbed into the butter and the buttery paste clings to the side of the bowl. Add the vanilla and beat for an additional 30 seconds to incorporate.\n4 Add the flour and salt: Mix on low speed. As the dry ingredients start to absorb into the butter-sugar mixture, you can increase the speed back to medium. Once all the flour is mixed in and a dough has formed, stop the mixer.\n5 Empty the crushed nuts into the bowl with the dough: Mix on low speed to incorporate.\n6 Chill the dough: Scrape the dough onto a piece of plastic wrap and flatten into a disk about 1-inch thick. Wrap tightly with the plastic wrap and place in the refrigerator for at least 1 hour or until the dough is firm.\n7 About 10 minutes before you're ready to bake, preheat the oven to 350F. Line 2 baking sheet with parchment paper or a silicon baking mat.\n8 Roll the cookies: Place the 1 1/4 cups of powdered sugar for coating the cookies into a shallow bowl. Remove the chilled dough out of the refrigerator and form into 1-inch balls of dough. (If your dough chilled longer than 1 hour, you may need to let it soften for a few minutes at room temperature.)\nRoll the balls of dough in powdered sugar and place on the baking mat, spaced slightly apart.\n9 Bake for 17 to 19 minutes, or until the cookies start to brown slightly on top and are golden brown on the bottoms. Let the cookies cool on the baking sheet for 10 minutes after baking.\n10 While the cookies are still warm, roll each cookie in the powdered sugar again. Return the cookies to the cooling rack and let cool completely before serving.\nStore at room temperature in an airtight container. They will keep well for at least a week.\nHello! b'Save It Print\nAlmond Crescent Cookies Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 20 minutesYield: Makes 2 1/2 dozen cookies\nINGREDIENTS\n1 cup of butter, room temperature\n2/3 cup of sugar\n1 teaspoon of vanilla extract\n1 teaspoon of almond extract\n2 1/2 cups of flour\n1 cup of almond flour (can substitute ground almonds*)\n1/4 cup of powdered sugar for sprinkling\n*You can use slivered, blanched almonds and grind them up, but you will have a very crumbly, hard to work with dough. It\xe2\x80\x99ll still taste good though.\nMETHOD\n1 Beat the butter and the sugar together until light and fluffy. Add the vanilla and almond extracts and mix.\n2 Add the flour and almond flour. Mix thoroughly.\n3 Take generous tablespoons of the dough (it will be slightly crumbly) and roll it into a small ball, about an inch in diameter, and then shape into a crescent shape. Place onto a parchment paper lined baking sheet.\n4 Bake at 350\xc2\xb0F for 15-20 minutes or until a light golden brown.\n5 Dust with powdered sugar.\nFor added decadence let the cookies cool and dip one end of them into some melted chocolate, then let the chocolate harden.\nHello! b'Print\nChocolate Florentine Cookies Recipe\nPrep time: 30 minutesBake time: 8 minutes per batchYield: 30 florentine cookies\nFlorentine cookies are crisp almond toffee-like cookies that are sandwiched with a layer of chocolate and then drizzled with more chocolate. They have a reputation for being difficult to make but I\xe2\x80\x99ve given some hints and tips on making them easier for you. Just make sure to watch them bake, as they can go from done to burnt fairly quickly.\nMaking these cookies goes more quickly if you have at least two baking sheets so that you can prep the next batch while the previous batch is in the oven.\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the cookies:\n2 1/2 cups (290 g) slivered almonds\n1/4 cup (35 g) all-purpose flour\n2 tablespoons natural cocoa powder (not Dutch-process)\n1/4 teaspoon ground nutmeg (optional but recommended)\n3/4 cup (150 g) white granulated sugar\n1/2 cup (1 stick or 115 g) unsalted butter\n1/4 cup heavy cream\n2 tablespoon honey\n1 teaspoon vanilla extract\nTo finish:\n8 to 10 ounces of dark chocolate, chopped\nSpecial equipment:\nFood processor\nSilpat or other silicon baking mat\nThin, flat spatula\nWire cooling rack\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Chop the almonds: Place the slivered almonds in a food processor. Pulse until the almonds are broken down into smaller bits, about 1/4 inch in size. They should be the size of the chopped nuts you would sprinkle over an ice cream sundae.\nIf you don\xe2\x80\x99t have a food processor, you can chop the nuts by hand or place them in a ziplock bag and crush them with a wooden rolling pin until they are the right size.\n2 Add the flour and cocoa powder to the food processor bowl. Pulse a couple of times to blend together.\n3 Make the cookie "batter" on the stovetop: In a medium-sized saucepan, place the sugar, butter, cream, and honey. Heat until the sugar is dissolved and the butter has melted. Remove from heat and stir in the vanilla extract.\nAdd the dry almond mixture and stir until incorporated. Set aside to cool for 20 minutes.\n4 Preheat the oven to 325\xc2\xbaF. Line a baking sheet with parchment paper or a silicon baking mat.\n5 Spoon out the cookies: Once the batter has cooled (it will still be warm), use a teaspoon measure to spoon out the cookies onto the prepared baking sheet (1 teaspoon per cookie). Space the cookies about 3 inches apart; they will spread a lot during baking. (On a 12 x 18 sheet, I found 6 cookies fit comfortably.)\n6 Flatten the cookies: Dip your finger in some water, then use it to spread the batter into a round circle, with the nuts in a single layer on the pan. This will encourage the batter to spread evenly in a circle.\n7 Bake the cookies: Bake the cookies in the oven for 6 to 8 minutes. If you are using parchment paper, the cookies will bake faster. If you are using a silicon baking sheet, the silicon insulates the heat and it takes a little long to bake (but they will bake more evenly).\nRemove the pan from the oven once the edges of the cookies start to darken and brown and transfer to a cooling rack. Be careful as the cookies go from done to burnt fairly fast.\nWhile the cookies are still warm from the oven, take a look at them and see if any of them are not quite round. If they are not as nicely shaped as you would like, use a spatula to carefully nudge the sides of the cookie into a round circle. You will have to work fairly quickly as the cookies firm up as they cool.\n8 Cool the cookies: Let the cookies cool on the pan for 10 to 20 minutes, until they are set. It\'s fine if they\'re still a little soft, but they should be able to be transferred in one piece without tearing or creating ripples in the cookie.\nIt helps to use a very thin, flat spatula so you can easily slide under each cookie. Also, if you have a wire rack that has crisscross wires, this is ideal for cookies like this since any under-baked cookie will slump a little bit on racks with more widely-spaced wires. Let the cookies cool completely.\n9 Continue baking the cookies in batches until all the batter has been used.\n10 Sandwich the cookies with chocolate: Once the cookies have all been baked and cooled, melt dark chocolate by placing it in a microwave-safe bowl and cooking it in 30 second increments, stirring between each increment. (You can also melt the chocolate on a double boiler, if you prefer.)\nOnce the chocolate has melted, pick two cookies that are roughly the same size and smear a thin layer of chocolate on the bottom of one of them. Place the matching cookie bottom on top and set the cookie sandwich on a baking sheet lined with parchment paper or a wire rack.\nRepeat with the remaining cookies. Drizzle any remaining chocolate over the Florentines.\n11 Wait for the chocolate to firm up and harden before serving or packaging. Stored in an airtight container, these cookies will keep at room temperature for 3 days, or in the fridge for about 2 weeks.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'
b"Save It Print\nFlourless Lemon Almond Cake Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 40 minutesYield: Serves 8\nIt helps to separate the eggs first, while they are cold, and then let them sit to come to room temperature as you prep the other ingredients.  Eggs are easier to separate when cold, and they perform better as leavening agents when at room temperature.\nWhen whipping egg whites, make sure your equipment is perfectly clean. Any fat (or even bits of egg yolk in the whites) can keep the egg whites from properly whipping up.\nIf almond flour is not available at your market, you can grind up blanched, slivered almonds in a food processor until very finely ground.  I would start with a little more than 1 1/3 cups. Our local Whole Foods carries a Bob's Red Mill brand of finely ground blanched almond flour which is what we used for this recipe.\nINGREDIENTS\n4 eggs (large), separated into 4 egg yolks and 4 egg whites, room temperature (see how to separate eggs)\n2 Tbsp lemon zest, packed\n1/2 cup (100 g) white sugar, divided 1/4 cup (50 g) and 1/4 cup (50 g)\n1 1/2 cup lightly scooped (144 g) finely ground blanched almond flour\n1 teaspoon baking powder (make sure your baking powder is fresh!)\n1/4 teaspoon ground cardamom\n1 teaspoon white or cider vinegar\nPinch of salt\nPowdered sugar for sprinkling\nSpecial equipment:\n8 or 9-inch springform pan\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Preheat oven, prepare pan: Preheat the oven to 350\xc2\xb0F (175 \xc2\xb0C).  Place a round of parchment paper on the bottom of a 8 or 9-inch springform pan, and grease it and the sides of the pan with butter or cooking spray.\n2 Beat egg yolks, lemon zest, 1/4 cup sugar: In a large bowl, beat together with a wooden spoon the egg yolks, lemon zest, and 1/4 cup sugar until smooth.\n3 Whisk almond flour, baking powder, cardamom, beat into egg yolk mixture: In a separate bowl, whisk together the almond flour, ground cardamom, and baking powder. Add the flour mixture to the egg yolk mixture and beat until well combined. The mixture should resemble a thick paste.\n4 Whip egg whites to soft peaks: With an electric mixer with a very clean bowl and clean whisk attachment, beat the egg whites, starting on low speed and gradually increasing the speed.\nWhen bubbles start to form, add a pinch of salt and the teaspoon of vinegar (both the salt and the vinegar will help the beaten egg whites maintain better structure, as will the sugar in the next step).\nAs the egg whites begin to increase in volume, sprinkle in the remaining 1/4 cup of sugar, a little at a time, as you continue to beat the egg whites. Beat until soft peaks form.\n5 Fold beaten egg whites into almond mixture: Stir a third to a half of the beaten egg whites into the almond mixture to loosen it and make it lighter.\nThen gently fold the remaining whipped egg whites into the batter, a large scoopful at a time.\n6 Scoop batter into pan, bake: Gently scoop the batter into the prepared springform pan and place in the oven. Bake at 350\xc2\xb0F (175 \xc2\xb0C) for 30 minutes.\nRemove from the oven and let cool. Run a sharp knife around the edge of the cake helping it to separate from the side of the pan.\nRelease the springform pan sides, and gently move the cake (on parchment) to a cake serving plate. Sprinkle with a little powdered sugar before serving.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"

b'Print\nCaramel Nut Tart Recipe\nYield: Serves 10\nINGREDIENTS\nCrust Ingredients:\n1 1/2 cups (200 g) all purpose flour\n2 tablespoons sugar\n1/4 teaspoon ground cinnamon\n1/4 teaspoon ground nutmeg\n1/4 teaspoon salt\n1/2 cup (1 stick, 112 g) chilled unsalted butter, cut into 1/2-inch pieces\n1 teaspoon vanilla extract\n3-4 tablespoons ice water\nFilling Ingredients:\n1 1/4 cups (250 g) sugar\n1/4 cup (60 ml) water\n2/3 cup (160 ml) heavy whipping cream\n2 tablespoons unsalted butter, cut into small pieces\n1 tablespoon honey\n1 teaspoon vanilla extract\n1 cup (125 g) walnuts, coarsely chopped\n1/2 cup (62 g) pecans, coarsely chopped\n1/2 cup (55 g) slivered blanched almonds\nWhipped cream (optional)\nSpecial equipment:\n9 1/2 inch (24 cm) tart pan with removable bottom\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Make the tart dough: Whisk together the flour, sugar, cinnamon, nutmeg and salt. Add the cut up pieces of butter and use a pastry cutter to cut into the flour mixture until the butter pieces are no bigger than a pea. (You can use a food processor for this if you want.)\nSprinkle with vanilla and add 3 tablespoons of ice water. Use a fork to work the water and vanilla into the dough. (You can use a food processor.) Add up to a tablespoon more of ice water, just enough so that the dough easily sticks together when you pinch it with your fingers.\nForm the dough into a ball, kneading once or twice if necessary, and flatten into a disk. Wrap the dough disk in plastic and chill for 1 hour.\n2 Roll out the dough, place in tart pan, freeze: Preheat oven to 375\xc2\xb0F (190\xc2\xb0C). Remove dough from refrigerator and let sit for 10 minutes. Place the dough on a lightly floured clean surface. Roll out the dough to a 12-inch round. Place the dough in a 9 1/2-inch-diameter tart pan with a removable bottom.\nPress the dough down and into the sides. Roll the rolling pin over the top of the tart pan to even off the top edges.\nPierce the bottom of the dough in the tart pan all over with fork. Freeze for 30 minutes.\n3 Pre-bake the crust: Bake the crust at 375\xc2\xb0F for 20 minutes, piercing the bottom with fork if bubbles form. Transfer to a rack to cool.\n4 Make the caramel nut filling: Put sugar and 1/4 cup water in heavy medium saucepan with high sides. Heat on medium-low heat and stir until sugar dissolves.\nOnce the sugar has dissolved, increase the heat to medium high. Boil without stirring until caramel is deep amber color, occasionally swirling the pan, about 10 minutes. Reduce heat to medium.\nSlowly stir in the cream. Be careful as the mixture will bubble up significantly (this is why we are using a high sided pot). Stir until the caramel is smooth.\nAdd the butter, honey and vanilla. Stir until the butter has all melted.\nStir in all of the nuts.\n5 Bake: Pour caramel mixture into the pre-baked crust. Bake at 400\xc2\xb0F (205\xc2\xb0C) 20 minutes. Remove from oven to cool completely on rack.\nServe with whipped cream or vanilla ice cream (optional).\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'
b"Save It Print\nHomemade Almond Roca Recipe\nPrep time: 5 minutesCook time: 20 minutes\nUse an inexpensive chocolate such as Hershey's. It has low cocoa butter content. If you use a premium chocolate with a high cocoa butter content, unless you temper the chocolate first (look up directions online), the cocoa butter may separate into white streaks as the melted chocolate cools.\nYou can use other kinds of nuts such as pecans or macadamia and white chocolate.\nDo not attempt to make this on a humid or rainy day. Do not double the recipe, make one batch at a time.\nINGREDIENTS\n1 cup sugar\n1/4 cup water\n1 Tbsp light corn syrup\n1/2 lb butter (2 sticks - NO substitutes!)\n1/2 lb. slivered almonds (2 cups)\n1/2 lb. bar of regular Hershey's dark chocolate (7 oz okay)\nMETHOD\n1 Melt butter with sugar, syrup and water in a pan (such as a large non-stick frying pan) on medium to medium-high temperature. Stir continuously with a wooden spoon.\nWhen butter is melted, add the almonds.\n2 Cook until the mixture turns a warm amber color, and the boiling sounds like a crackle: When mixture comes to a rolling boil, set your timer for a minimum of 10 minutes and keep stirring (no more than 15 minutes). The mixture will thicken and turn darker in color. The almonds will roast.\nKeep stirring and cooking until you hear it crackle. If you don't cook it long enough it will not harden, so keep stirring and listen for the crackling sound.\nElise's note: I have found it very hard to distinguish between the boiling sound and the crackling sound in this recipe. A better guideline for me is by color. When the mixture turns a warm amber color, at about 11 or 12 minutes into the boiling, that's the time to pour it out. Wait too long and it will burn.\nIf you try to make this, please read all the comments listed below. It's actually trickier than one would think.\n3 Pour mixture out onto a large cookie sheet: When the mixture crackles, pour the mixture out onto a large sheet pan or cookie sheet and spread it as thin as possible with a fork.\n4 Spread chocolate over the top: While the almond mixture is still hot, break up the chocolate into chunks and distribute it over the almond mixture and let it melt. Spread it evenly on the top.\n5 Cool to room temp: Let the almond roca cool to room temperature. When cool you can lift the whole thing off the pan and break into small pieces.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b"Save It Print\nAlmond Shortbread Cookies Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 40 minutesChilling time: 30 minutesYield: 12 to 16 cookies\nThis recipe makes 12 large or 16 small wedges\xe2\x80\x94the cookies are rich, so the small wedges are not too small if you want to have a greater yield.\nINGREDIENTS\nButter, for the baking pan\n1 stick (4 ounces, 8 tablespoons) unsalted butter, cut into 1-inch slices, at room temperature\n3/4 cup (148g) sugar\n1 cup (120g) flour\n1/2 cup (56g) cornstarch\n1/2 cup (48g) almond flour\n1/2 teaspoon salt\n1 teaspoon vanilla extract\n1 tablespoon milk\n1/3 cup sliced almonds\nPowdered sugar (for sprinkling)\nSpecial equipment:\n9-inch pie pan, or tart pan\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Preheat the oven to 350\xc2\xbaF. While the shortbread is still awrm, carefully cut the wedges again to make sure they're separated. b"Print\nAlmond Pound Cake with Orange Glaze Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 1 hour, 15 minutesYield: Makes one loaf\nWhenever baking with eggs, you'll get more rise if you start with eggs that are at room temperature. If you want to quickly bring chilled eggs up to room temp, place them in a bowl of warm (not hot) water for 10 minutes.\nTip on using Odense almond paste\xe2\x80\x94grate it using the large holes of a box grater.\nThis recipe makes enough batter for one 5x9x3 inch loaf pan, which is a rather large loaf pan. If you have a 4x8x2 1/2 inch loaf pan, either make two loaves, or cut the recipe in half.\nINGREDIENTS\nCake:\n5 ounces (140 g) almond paste (we recommend Odense almond paste), grated\n1 1/2 cups (300 g) white granulated sugar\n4 ounces (1/2 cup or 1 stick) butter, room temperature\n4 large eggs\n1 teaspoon orange zest\n1 teaspoon vanilla\n1/2 cup (120 g) plain (full fat) Greek yogurt (or sour cream)\n1 1/2 cups (200 g) all purpose flour\n1 teaspoon baking powder\n1/2 teaspoon salt (if using unsalted butter)\nGlaze:\n1/3 cup (43 g) powdered sugar\n2 teaspoons orange juice\n1/2 teaspoon lemon juice\n1/2 teaspoon orange zest\nSpecial equipment:\n5x9x3-inch loaf pan\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Preheat oven, prepare loaf pan: Preheat oven to 325\xc2\xb0F. Place on lower middle rack of your oven.\nBake at 325\xc2\xb0F for 50-55 minutes, until golden brown, and if you press down lightly on the top it springs back at you, and a tester inserted into the center comes out clean. While it's baking, if you notice it getting too browned, tent it lightly with aluminum foil.\n6 Cool on a rack: Remove from oven and let cool on a rack for 5 to 10 minutes. Then carefully remove from the pan to cool completely on a rack.\n7 Make orange glaze: While the cake is cooling, make the glaze. Sift the powdered sugar through a sieve to remove any lumps and place in a medium bowl. Whisk in the orange juice and lemon juice. Stir in the the zest. Add more sugar if the glaze is too runny, add more juice if it is too thick for your taste.\n8 Drizzle cake with glaze: When the cake has cooled, place it on a serving plate and use a spoon to drizzle the glaze all over it.\nHello! b'Save It Print\nGinger Chicken with Almonds Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 15 minutesYield: Serves 4-6\nIncluding a little cornstarch in the chicken marinade is traditional in many asian dishes. b'Save It Print\nPeach Frangipane Puff Pastry Tarts Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 35 minutesYield: 9 tarts\nPackage sizes of puff pastry vary but are usually in the 14- to 16-ounce range. Depending on the original size of the sheet, you will cut it into squares or rectangles. Remember, this is fancy but rustic, so the exact size of the tarts is flexible!\nINGREDIENTS\n1 sheet all-butter puff pastry (14 to 16 ounces), thawed\n1 cup almond flour\n1/2 cup sugar\n1/8 teaspoon salt\n5 tablespoons unsalted butter, at room temperature, cut into slices\n1 large egg\n2 tablespoons all-purpose flour\n1 tablespoon amaretto or 1 teaspoon pure almond extract\n1 teaspoon vanilla\n1 1/2 pounds (about 4 medium) ripe peaches, cut into 1-inch wedges\n2 tablespoons turbinado sugar\n3 tablespoons apple jelly or apricot jam\n1 tablespoon water\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Preheat the oven: Line a baking sheet with parchment and preheat the oven to 375\xc2\xbaF.\n2 Prepare the dough: On a lightly floured work surface, unfold the puff pastry. Lightly roll it with a rolling pin to even it out if there are any gaps or wrinkles. Transfer the dough to the parchment-lined baking sheet.\nWith a pizza cutter or knife, cut the dough into 9 pieces to make four-inch squares or similar size rectangles. The exact size depends upon the original shape of the dough. Spread them apart on the baking sheet. Refrigerate while you make the filling.\n3 Make the frangipane: In a food processor fitted with the metal blade, pulse the almond flour, sugar, and salt for a few seconds to mix. Add the butter pieces and pulse until the butter is incorporated with no large visible pieces.\nAdd the egg, all-purpose flour, amaretto (or almond extract), and vanilla and process until the frangipane is smooth. It should have the consistency of natural almond butter, thick but runny.\n4 Assemble the tarts: On each square of pastry, spoon about 1 tablespoon of the frangipane. It will spread out naturally on the pastry, and even further once you add peaches. If some spills over the edges that\xe2\x80\x99s fine. If your frangipane doesn\xe2\x80\x99t spread, feel free to push it around the tart with the back of your spoon. You may have some frangipane left over, depending on the size of your pastry squares.\nSet 5 to 6 wedges of fruit on top of each tart\xe2\x80\x94no need to be too fussy about their arrangement. Sprinkle each with the turbinado sugar.\n5 Bake the tarts: Bake for 35 to 40 minutes, or until the peaches are soft and the frangipane and pastry are golden.\n6 Glaze the tarts: In a small microwave-safe bowl, heat the jelly or jam and water for 30 seconds, or until liquefied. Brush the warm glaze over the peaches. Serve the tarts on the same day that they are made.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. b"Print\nAlmond Butter Date Balls Recipe\nPrep time: 5 minutesChill time: 30 minutesYield: 15 to 16 date balls\nI sometimes like to add a tablespoon or so of dried cranberries to give this a bit of a tart twist.\nINGREDIENTS\n1/2 cup walnuts\n1/2 cup pitted dates (about 4 to 5), cut into quarters\n1/2 cup cocoa powder, any kind (I usually use Hershey\xe2\x80\x99s Special Dark)\nScant 1/2 cup maple syrup\n1/2 cup almond butter\n1/2 teaspoon vanilla extract\n1/4 teaspoon fine sea salt\n1/2 cup whole almonds\nCooking spray (optional)\nFor topping/rolling the balls:\n1/2 cup unsweetened shredded coconut\n1/2 cup cocoa powder\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Make the date balls: Place the walnuts and dates into the bowl of a food processor fitted with the blade, and pulse several times until well combined. The pieces should look like a rough crumble.\nAdd the cocoa powder, maple syrup, almond butter, vanilla extract, and sea salt and pulse until the mixture is smooth and thick; it will start to peel away from the edge of the bowl.\nWhen this happens, stop the food processor; if it keeps whirring away, it may get stuck because these ingredients are, well, sticky! Keep a close eye on this, as it will come together quickly.\n2 Add the almonds: Add the almonds and pulse a few times to incorporate them. You want them sort of irregularly sized, so that some pieces are still pretty crunchy and offer a variety of textures.\n3 Roll the date balls: Line a rimmed baking sheet with parchment or wax paper. Place the coconut in a small bowl and the cocoa powder in another bowl.\nUsing a cookie scoop measuring about 1 1/2 tablespoons (like this one) and sprayed with cooking spray for easy release, scoop out the mixture, roll it into golf-ball shapes, and roll in the shredded coconut or the cocoa powder. (I usually do some in coconut and some in cocoa powder, and leave some plain.)\n4 Chill and store the date balls: Transfer the date balls to the baking sheet and chill them for a few hours or overnight, if needed. Once they've firmed up, transfer to a plastic lidded container and keep in the fridge for several weeks, but I've never, ever, had them last that long. They are usually consumed too quickly.\nHello! b'Print\nGrain-Free Apple Honey Cake Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 30 minutesCooling time: 45 minutesYield: 8 to 10 servings\nThis cake can be made up to a day ahead. Or, if you\xe2\x80\x99re in a big hurry to serve it, you can serve the cake warm, too.\nFor a more rustic cake, use almond meal instead of almond flour, and leave the apple unpeeled.\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the cake:\n1 1/2 cups (6 ounces) almond flour\n1 teaspoon ground cinnamon\n1/4 teaspoon ground nutmeg\n3/4 teaspoon salt\n3 large eggs\n1/4 cup honey\n2 tablespoons neutral-tasting oil (I use avocado oil)\n1 medium (7-ounce) Granny Smith apple, peeled and cut into thin matchsticks, or grated coarsely\nFor the glaze and topping:\n1/2 cup powdered sugar\n2 tablespoons honey\n1 tablespoon almond milk or water\n1/4 cup sliced almonds\nSpecial equipment:\n8-inch cake pan\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Preheat the oven and prepare a cake pan: Preheat the oven to 325\xc2\xbaF. Grease an 8-inch cake pan and place a round of parchment in the bottom of the pan.\n2 Make the cake batter: In a medium mixing bowl, whisk together the almond flour, cinnamon, nutmeg, and salt. Make a well in the center of the flour, then add in the eggs, honey, and oil. Whisk wet ingredients together in the middle, then gradually whisk in the flour from the sides of the bowl. Continue whisking until the batter is smooth. Stir in the julienned or grated apple.\n3 Pour the batter into the pan and bake the cake: Pour the batter into the cake pan, taking care not to move the parchment around. Spread out the batter in an even layer using an offset spatula or butter knife, then tap the cake pan against the countertop to remove any air bubbles.\n4 Bake the cake: Bake the cake for 30 minutes, until it is browned around the edges and a toothpick inserted in the middle comes out clean. You may also use a probe thermometer to test for doneness\xe2\x80\x94the center of the cake should be 210\xc2\xbaF.\n5 While the cake is baking, make the glaze and toast the almonds: In a small bowl, stir together the sugar, honey, and almond milk. Cover the bowl and set it aside until needed.\nToast the sliced almonds in a skillet over medium heat until they are lightly browned, about five minutes. Shake the pan often so that the almonds are browned evenly. When they are done, immediately transfer to bowl to cool.\n6 Transfer the cake to a cooling rack: Allow the finished cake rest for 5 minutes, then run a knife around the edge of the pan to and invert the cake to a cooling rack. Peel the parchment off the bottom of the cake and flip it right side up.\n7 While the cake is still warm, pour the glaze over the top. Spread the glaze so that it drips over the edges of the cake. While the glaze is still wet, sprinkle the almonds on top.\n8 Let the cake cool to room temperature and serve. The cake can also be made and glazed up to a day ahead.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'
b'Save It Print\nSpicy Paleo Pumpkin Muffins Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 20 minutesYield: 12\nYou can substitute any hard winter squash or carrots for the pumpkin.\nTo grate the pumpkin, cut it into large pieces, scoop out the seeds, and grate the flesh on a box grater until you hit the skin. Alternatively, you can cut away the skin and grate in a food processor.\nINGREDIENTS\n2 1/2 cups almond flour\n3/4 cup tapioca starch\n1 1/2 tablespoons coconut flour\n1 teaspoon baking soda\n1 1/2 teaspoons baking powder\n1/2 tablespoon smoked paprika\n1 teaspoon crushed chili flakes (I used chipotle chili flakes)\n1 1/2 teaspoons ground cumin\n1/2 teaspoon salt\n4 large eggs\n1/2 cup olive oil, melted ghee, or melted butter\n2 tablespoons honey\n1 tablespoon red wine vinegar\n1 packed cup grated raw sugar or pie pumpkin (avoid jack-o-lantern pumpkins)\n1/2 cup diced red bell pepper\n1/2 cup diced onion\n3/4 cups toasted pepitas or pumpkin seeds (divided)\nSpecial equipment:\n12-cup muffin tin\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Preheat oven to 350F. Line a muffin tin with muffin papers\n2 Sift together the dry ingredients: Sift together the almond flour, tapioca starch, coconut flour, baking soda, baking powder, spices, and salt. I like to sift at least twice with Paleo baked goods to make sure there are no clumps and everything is well-mixed.\n3 Mix together the wet ingredients: In a separate bowl, beat the eggs, then whisk in the oil, honey, and vinegar.\n4 Pour the wet ingredients into the dry and mix gently until combined.\n5 Gently stir in the grated pumpkin, bell pepper, onion, and 1/2 cup of pepitas. Save the rest of the pepitas for topping. Rest the batter for at least 10 minutes so that the flours can hydrate.\n6 Fill each muffin wells up to the top. Top each muffin with a few of the remaining 1/4 cup of pepitas.\n7 Bake for 18 to 20 minutes. When done, the muffins should look toasted around the edges, be dry on top, and a toothpick inserted in the middle will come out clean.\n8 Cool and serve (or store): Transfer the muffins to a cooling rack. Cool briefly before serving, or cool completely and store in an airtight container at room temperature for 3 days (or refrigerate for up to a week).\nHello! b'Print\nClassic Pasta Primavera Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 10 minutesYield: Serves 4\nINGREDIENTS\n1/2 pound angel hair pasta or spaghetti\n1 small bunch broccoli, about 1 heaping cup of florets\n1 small zucchini, diced\n4 asparagus spears\n1/2 cup peas, fresh or frozen\n1/2 cup snow peas\n3 minced garlic cloves\n3 Roma or other paste tomatoes, seeded and diced\n12 basil leaves, chopped\n4 tablespoons butter\n1/4 cup chicken broth (use vegetable broth for vegetarian option)\n1/2 cup heavy cream\n1/2 cup grated parmesan cheese\nSalt\nMETHOD\n1 Blanch the broccoli, asparagus, snow peas: Get a large pot of water boiling. Salt it well. It should taste like the sea. Fill a large bowl with ice water. Boil the broccoli for 1 minute.\nAdd the asparagus and boil another minute. Add the snow peas and boil for 30 more seconds.\nRemove all the vegetables and plunge them into the ice water. Once they\xe2\x80\x99re cool, drain in a colander.\nIf you want, you can boil your pasta in the same pot you boiled the vegetables in, or you can start over and boil new water; I use the same water.\n2 Saut\xc3\xa9 zucchini and garlic, then add tomatoes: In a large saut\xc3\xa9 pan, heat the butter over medium-high heat. When the butter is hot, add the garlic and zucchini and saut\xc3\xa9 1 minute.\nAdd the diced tomatoes and saut\xc3\xa9 another 2 minutes, stirring often.\n3 Add broth, cream, blanched vegetables, peas: Pour in the chicken or vegetable broth and turn the heat to high to bring it to a boil.\nAdd the cream and toss in all the vegetables you boiled, plus the peas. Stir to combine.\nTurn the heat down until the cream-chicken broth mixture is just simmering, not boiling.\n4 Add Parmesan: Add the Parmesan cheese and stir to combine. If the sauce seems too thick \xe2\x80\x93 it should be pretty thick, but not gloppy \xe2\x80\x93 add some more chicken broth, cream or water.\n5 Boil the angel hair pasta: If you are using spaghetti, you will want to start cooking it before you begin saut\xc3\xa9ing the garlic and zucchini. Angel hair will only need 1-2 minutes to cook, vermicelli or spaghetti can take 8-12 minutes.\n6 Transfer cooked pasta to sauce and vegetables: As soon as the pasta is done, transfer it with tongs into the sauce and stir to combine.\nAdd the basil now, and taste for salt. Add salt if needed. Grind some black pepper over everything and serve immediately.\nYou will want a dry white wine with this, ideally a dry French white.\nHello! b'Print\nAngel Hair Pasta with Garlic, Herbs, and Parmesan Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 10 minutesYield: Serves 4 as a side\nThis recipe can easily be doubled. If you use delicate herbs such as basil or tarragon, toss them in at the end with the Parmesan.\nINGREDIENTS\n8 ounces angel hair pasta\nSalt\n1/4 cup extra virgin olive oil\n2 Tbsp finely chopped fresh herbs such as rosemary, thyme, oregano\n1/4 cup chopped fresh parsley\n3 cloves of garlic, sliced\n1/8 teaspoon chili pepper flakes (or more to taste)\n1/2 to 1 teaspoon of freshly ground black pepper (to taste)\n1/2 cup grated Parmesan cheese\nMETHOD\n1 Prepare boiling water for pasta: Bring a large pot of salted water to a boil. Add the sliced garlic, chili pepper flakes, finely chopped herbs, and chopped parsley to the oil.  Cook for one minute or until the parsley has wilted and the garlic is emitting a strong fragrance.  Remove from heat.\n3 Cook the pasta: The angel hair past will cook in about 2 minutes once it starts, so get everything ready. Once the water is at a rolling boil, add the pasta.  Cook at a rolling boil until al dente. Remove 1/2 a cup of the pasta cooking water and set aside. Drain the pasta and rinse briefly with cold water, just enough to stop the cooking, but not so much as to make the pasta cold. The pasta should still be quite warm.\n4 Combine pasta and herbs: Place pasta in a large bowl. Pour herbed garlic sauce over the pasta and gently toss to combine. Sprinkle Parmesan cheese  and freshly ground black pepper over the pasta and gently toss to combine. If the pasta is a little sticky, add back a little of the pasta cooking water to loosen.\nServe immediately as a side dish. Reheats well if you make ahead.\nHello! b"Print\nAngel Hair Pasta with Shrimp and Parmesan Lemon Cream Sauce Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 15 minutesYield: Serves 4\nWe used medium shrimp (41-50 per pound) for this recipe, but little cocktail shrimp would also work. b"Save It Print\nAngel Hair Pasta with Salmon, Arugula, and Creamy Lemon-Parmesan Sauce Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 25 minutesYield: 6 servings\nINGREDIENTS\n2 tablespoons extra virgin olive oil, separated\n6 salmon fillets (2 1/2 to 3 ounces each, about 1 to 1 1/4 pounds total), preferably wild-caught King or Sockeye salmon\n2 1/4 teaspoon kosher salt, divided\n1 teaspoon ground black pepper, divided\n1 pound angel hair pasta\n4 tablespoons unsalted butter, separated\n1 tablespoon minced shallot\n4 garlic cloves, minced\n1 cup dry white wine or seafood stock\nJuice and rinds of 2 lemons (1/3 to 1/2 cup juice)\n2 cups heavy cream\n5 ounces arugula (4 packed cups)\n1 cup freshly grated Parmesan cheese\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Warm your oven: Set the oven to its lowest setting (mine is 150\xc2\xb0F) to keep the salmon warm once it's cooked.\n2 Start the water for pasta. Bring a large pot of salted water to boil.\n3 Season the salmon fillets: Rub both sides of the fillets with 1 teaspoon of the kosher salt and a 1/2 teaspoon of the black pepper.\n4 Sear the salmon: Heat 1 tablespoon of the olive oil over medium-high heat in a large saut\xc3\xa9 pan (preferably nonstick). Once the oil starts to ripple in the pan, place the salmon fillets into the pan, skin-side up.\nPress the fillets down gently to make sure the entire surface makes contact with the pan. Sear the salmon fillets for 3 minutes, or until the flesh turns an opaque pink 1/4 of the way up the sides of the fillets.\n5 Flip the salmon and keep it hot: Use a spatula to flip the salmon and sear it, skin-side down, for an additional 3 minutes.\nTransfer the fillets to a sheet pan and place them in the heated oven while you finish the dish. It\xe2\x80\x99s okay if the salmon is not cooked completely through just yet\xe2\x80\x94it will continue to cook in the oven.\n6 Cook the shallot and deglaze the pan: In the same pan you used to sear the salmon, heat the remaining tablespoon of olive oil and 2 tablespoons of the butter over medium-high heat. Add the shallot and the garlic to the pan and saut\xc3\xa9 for 3 minutes, or until glossy and fragrant.\nPour the white wine and lemon juice into the pan and use a wooden spoon to scrape up any bits of food that have stuck to the bottom of the pan. Add the lemon halves and bring the mixture to a boil.\n7 Reduce the sauce and cook the pasta: Reduce the sauce in the pan by half by maintaining a boil. This should take 3 to 4 minutes.\n8 Cook the pasta: By now, your pasta water should be at a rolling boil. Add generous tablespoon of salt to the boiling water and drop the pasta into the middle of the pot. Stir the pasta immediately to separate the noodles.\nLower the temperature slightly to prevent the water from boiling over and cook the pasta for 4 to 5 minutes, until al dente (or according to package directions). Drain the pasta.\n9 Finish the sauce:  Once the liquid in the pan has reduced by half, reduce the heat to medium-low. Remove the lemon halves. Slowly stir in the heavy cream and the remaining butter.\nAllow the sauce to come to a simmer, then add the arugula. Stir to coat the arugula in the sauce and allow it to wilt slightly\xe2\x80\x94this should only take a minute or so. Add the Parmesan, along with the remaining salt and pepper. Taste and adjust the seasoning, if necessary, by adding a bit more salt or pepper.\n10 Combine the pasta and sauce: Add the pasta to the pan with the sauce. Using tongs, toss in the pasta in the sauce until it is evenly coated.\n11 Serve the pasta with the salmon: Remove the warm salmon fillets from the oven and arrange on top of the pasta. Serve immediately. While this dish is best enjoyed the same day it\xe2\x80\x99s made, we have had success with reheating the leftovers in the microwave the next day.\nHello! b'Print\nQuick and Easy Shrimp with Angel Hair Pasta Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 15 minutesYield: Serves 4\nIf you are working with frozen shrimp, to defrost place in a large bowl, cover with an inch or two of cold water, stir a couple teaspoons of salt into the water, add a few ice cubes. Let sit until defrosted.\nINGREDIENTS\n1/2 cup extra virgin olive olive\n2 cups finely diced red and green bell peppers (3 to 4 bell peppers)\n2 Tbsp grated fresh ginger root\n2 cloves garlic, minced (about 2 teaspoons)\nSalt\n1 pound peeled and deveined medium sized shrimp (31-40 count)\n4 Tbsp fresh lime juice (can sub lemon juice)\n1/2 teaspoon black pepper\n3 Tbsp chopped chives (or green onion greens)\n3/4 pound angel hair pasta\nMETHOD\n1 Heat salted water for pasta: Put a large pot of salted water (4 quarts of water, 2 Tbsp salt) on high heat. While the water is heating, continue with the recipe.\n2 Saut\xc3\xa9 bell peppers, ginger, garlic: Heat 3 Tbsp olive oil in a large saut\xc3\xa9 pan on medium high heat. Add the diced bell peppers and cook until softened, about 4 to 5 minutes. Add the grated ginger and minced garlic, and cook for 1 to 2 minutes more.\n3 Add shrimp: Add the shrimp and cook until just cooked through and no longer translucent, about 2 to 3 minutes. Sprinkle with lime juice, the remaining olive oil, and black pepper. Remove from heat.\n4 Cook pasta: When the pasta water is boiling, add the angel hair pasta and cook for 2 minutes or until cooked through, but still slightly al dente. Drain, reserving 1/2 cup of the pasta water.\n5 Add pasta to shrimp: Add the drained pasta back to the pan with the shrimp. Add the reserved pasta cooking water to the pot. Stir to combine all of the ingredients. Sprinkle with chopped chives to serve.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'
b"Print\nSopa Seca de Fideo (Mexican-style Angel Hair Nests) Recipe\nPrep time: 5 minutesCook time: 25 minutesYield: Serves 4\nIf you can't find angel hair nests at the market, you can make fideo with straight vermicelli pasta. Just break up the pasta in 3 to 4 inch long segments and cook the same way as you would the nests, browning them first in hot oil.\nINGREDIENTS\n1/2 pound angel hair nests or vermicelli (vermicelli usually comes in 1 pound packages, so about 1/2 a package)\n1/4 cup extra virgin olive oil\n1/2 yellow onion, chopped (about 3/4 cup)\n2 fresh tomatoes, peeled and chopped, or 1/2 cup crushed canned tomatoes\n2 cups chicken broth or stock\nSalt and pepper\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Brown the angle hair nests: Choose a frying pan with a lid in which the angel hair nests will all tightly fit in a single layer (about 9 or 10-inches wide, depending on the brand of angel hair nests you use). In the pan, heat the oil until shimmering hot.\nWorking in batches, fry the vermicelli angel hair nests on both sides in the hot oil until golden brown in color. Remove from pan.\n2 Saut\xc3\xa9 tomatoes and onion, add broth: Add the chopped onions to the pan and saut\xc3\xa9 until lightly browned, about 5 minutes. Add the chopped tomatoes. Add the chicken broth. Season with salt and pepper to taste.\n3 Cook angel hair nests in simmering broth: Bring the broth mixture to a simmer. When broth is simmering, place the browned angel hair nests or vermicelli in a single layer in the pan, nestled into the broth. The nests should cover the whole pan. Turn them over in the broth so that they get moistened on all sides.\nCover and cook until the vermicelli has soaked up the liquid, about 5 minutes. If after 5 minutes the top of the vermicelli is dry, flip over the individual angel hair nests and cook a minute longer.\n4 Serve: Remove from heat and let sit for 5 minutes before serving.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint"
b'Print\nRoast Chicken on Angel Hair Pasta Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 50 minutesYield: 4 servings\nAt my grocery store, I can buy nests of fresh angel hair pasta, which I love for this dish. If you find something similar at your grocery store, give it a try! The cooking times will be the same.\nAnother name for angel hair pasta is capellini; either is fine in this recipe.\nLook for chicken legs (thigh and drumstick attached) at the meat counter at your grocery store. If you can\'t find them, then buy two bone-in, skin-on thighs and two drumsticks, or buy a whole chicken and spatchcock it before roasting.\nINGREDIENTS\n1 pound angel hair pasta\n6 tablespoons olive oil, divided\n1 (15-ounce) can diced tomatoes with their juices\n1 teaspoon salt, divided\n1/2 teaspoon black pepper\n1/4 teaspoon crushed red pepper\n2 tablespoons chopped fresh oregano, divided\n2 whole chicken legs (thighs and drumsticks attached), on the bone (1 1/2 pounds total)\n2 large chicken breast halves, on the bone (1 1/2 pounds total)\n1 sprig fresh oregano, leaves removed, for garnish\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Cook the angel hair: Bring a pot of salted water to a rapid boil over high heat and cook the angel hair until al dente, about 4 minutes. Drain the pasta.\n2 Transfer the pasta to the baking dish: Use 1 tablespoon of olive oil to coat the bottom and sides of a 9-by-13-inch baking dish. Using tongs, transfer the pasta to the baking dish.\nIf you like, twirl the pasta into several small "nests" within the dish. Drizzle 1 tablespoon of olive oil evenly over top of the pasta and set the dish aside.\n3 Heat the oven to 400\xc2\xb0F.\n4 Cook the tomatoes: Warm 2 tablespoons of the olive oil in a skillet over medium high heat. Add the tomatoes and their juices, 1/2 teaspoon salt, 1/4 teaspoon black pepper, red pepper, and 1 tablespoon of the oregano.\nCook, stirring occasionally, for 3 minutes. Spoon the tomato mixture evenly over the nests; they will not be covered completely.\n5 Add the chicken: Rub the chicken skin with the remaining 2 tablespoons of olive oil. Sprinkle with the remaining 1/2 teaspoon salt and 1/4 teaspoon black pepper.\nSet the chicken on the nests, skin side up. Sprinkle with the remaining tablespoon of oregano.\n6 Roast the chicken: Transfer the dish to the oven and roast the chicken for 45 to 60 minutes, or until a meat thermometer inserted into the thickest part of a breasts and thighs registers 165\xc2\xb0F. Remove from the oven and rest for 10 minutes.\n7 Cut and serve the chicken: Cut the legs in half to make 2 thighs and 2 drumsticks (you can do this right in the dish). Cut the breasts in half horizontally. Break up the angel hair with a metal spoon or knife. Serve the chicken pieces with some of the pasta from underneath.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'
b"Save It Print\nAngel Hair Pasta with Quick Cherry Tomato Sauce Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 10 minutesYield: 4 to 6 servings\nIf you're good at multitasking, start the sauce as soon as the pasta goes into the pot so everything comes together at about the same time. If this feels stressful, cook the pasta first and then start the sauce. Either way, dinner is ready fast!\nFor a fancier presentation, if serving this at a dinner party, remove half of the tomatoes before tossing with the pasta. Plate the pasta, then top with the reserved tomatoes.\nINGREDIENTS\n2 1/2 teaspoons salt\n1 pounds angel hair pasta (capellini or capelli d\xe2\x80\x99Angelo), or another thin spaghetti\n4 tablespoons olive oil\n2 pints red and yellow cherry tomatoes\n1/2 teaspoon crushed red pepper\n1/4 teaspoon ground black pepper\n2 cloves garlic, very thinly sliced\n1 cup fresh basil leaves, removed from the stems\n1 cup grated Parmesan cheese\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Cook the pasta: Bring a large pot of water with 2 teaspoons of salt to a boil. Add the pasta and stir well until the water returns to a boil.\nCook for 3 to 4 minutes, stirring occasionally, or until the pasta is tender. With a ladle or a heat-proof liquid measuring cup, remove about 1/2 cup of the pasta cooking water and set aside.\nDrain the pasta but do not rinse it; transfer to a bowl. Sprinkle with 1 tablespoon of the oil and toss well.\n2 Prep the tomatoes: Pierce small whole tomatoes with a skewer or the tip of a paring knife. Halve the tomatoes if they\xe2\x80\x99re large.\n3 Make the sauce: In a deep skillet over medium-high heat, heat the remaining 3 tablespoons of oil. Add the cherry tomatoes \xe2\x80\x93 they will splutter \xe2\x80\x93 along with the remaining 1/2 teaspoon salt, red pepper, and black pepper.\nCook, shaking the pan, for 2 to 3 minutes, or until the tomatoes start to collapse and form juices. Add the garlic and continue cooking for 2 minutes more.\n4 Toss the pasta with the sauce: Add the pasta and 1/4 cup of the pasta water to the skillet with the tomato sauce. Toss well.\nAdd more pasta water if needed, a tablespoon at a time, to thin the mixture so the sauce coats the pasta. Add half the basil leaves and toss again.\n5 Serve: Divide the pasta among 4 to 6 large bowls. Add a few basil leaves on top of the pasta and sprinkle generously with Parmesan.\nHello! b'Print\nAngel Hair Pasta with Clams, Cherry Tomatoes, and Basil Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 15 minutesYield: Serves 2 to 3\nSave time by prepping the shallots, garlic, tomatoes, and basil while the water for the pasta is heating up.\nINGREDIENTS\n30 cherry tomatoes, sliced in half\n1/4 teaspoon salt\n4 Tbsp chopped fresh basil, divided\n1/4 cup extra virgin olive oil\n1/2 cup sliced shallots\n2 cloves minced garlic\n2 6-ounce cans chopped clams (and their juices)\n8 ounces capellini or angel hair pasta\nSalt for the pasta water\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Toss cherries with salt and basil: Place sliced cherry tomatoes in a bowl. Toss with 1/4 teaspoon of salt and 2 Tbsp of the chopped fresh basil. Set aside.\n2 Boil salted water, prep shallots and garlic: Bring a large pot of salted water to a boil (4 quarts of water, 2 Tbsp salt). While the water is coming to a boil, prep the shallots and garlic and start the sauce.\n3 Make tomato clam sauce: Heat the olive oil in a large saut\xc3\xa9 pan on medium heat. Add the sliced shallots and cook until translucent, stirring often. Add the garlic and cook for 30 seconds more.\nAdd the tomatoes and cook for 2 minutes. Add the chopped clams with their juices.\nReduce the heat to low and let simmer at a low temperature while the pasta is cooking in the next step.\n4 Cook the pasta: Once the salted pasta water comes to a rolling boil, add pasta and cook, uncovered at high heat until al dente, no more than 2 minutes.\nDrain the pasta, reserving 1/4 cup of the pasta water. Add the 1/4 cup of pasta water to the sauce in the saut\xc3\xa9 pan.\n5 Combine pasta and sauce: Add the pasta to the cherry tomato mixture and toss to combine. Stir in the remaining 2 Tbsp chopped fresh basil.\nServe immediately.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'
b'Print\nSopa Seca de Fideo with Tomatillos Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 1 hourYield: Serves 4\nIf you want, you can substitute a cup of prepared tomatillo salsa verde for the sauce you make in step one. The original recipe calls for using Hoja Santa cheese, which is goat cheese wrapped in aromatic Hoja Santa leaves. It\'s a lovely cheese to use if you can find it, otherwise regular goat cheese will do.\nINGREDIENTS\n3/4 pound tomatillos (about 6 medium sized), husks removed\n1 to 2 serrano chiles\n1/4 medium onion\n1 clove garlic\n2 tablespoons chopped fresh cilantro, plus extra for garnish\n4 tablespoons extra virgin olive oil, divided\n4 ounces fresh Mexican chorizo, casing removed, crumbled\n8 ounces capellini, or angel hair pasta, broken into 1 to 1 1/2-inch pieces\n1 teaspoon sea salt\nFreshly ground black pepper\n2 1/2 cups chicken stock\n4 ounces goat cheese, crumbled\n1 avocado, seeded, peeled, diced\nCrema fresca or sour cream\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Broil tomatillos, chiles, onion: Place the tomatillos, serrano chiles, an quarter onion on a baking sheet lightly greased with olive oil. Broil for about 15 minutes until somewhat charred and blistered. Remove the stems from the serranos.\n2 Make tomatillo sauce: Working in batches if necessary, pur\xc3\xa9e the chiles, tomatillos, onion, a clove of garlic, and 2 tablespoons of the chopped cilantro in a blender, making sure not to fill the blender more than halfway. Once blended you should have about a cup of sauce.\n3 Cook the chorizo: Heat 2 Tbsp of oil in a large saucepan on medium heat. Add the chorizo and cook 3 to 4 minutes until cooked through and crispy. Use a wooden spoon to crumble up the chorizo as it cooks.\nUse a slotted spoon to remove the chorizo to a paper-towel lined plate, keeping the fat and oil in the pan.\n4 Brown the dry noodles: Place the broken up dry pasta into the pan and increase the heat to medium high. Lightly brown the dry noodles in the chorizo oil. Remove the pasta from the pan and set aside.\n5 Cook the tomatillo sauce: Add the remaining 2 Tbsp of oil to the pan and heat on medium high heat. Add the tomatillo sauce and the salt. The sauce should bubble up from the heat of the pan. Cook for about a minute, allowing the sauce to reduce by about a quarter cup. Dragging your spoon through the sauce should leave a trail for a second or two.\n6 Add pasta: Add the pasta back to the pan with the tomatillo sauce and cook it until it has absorbed the liquid.\n7 Add stock, simmer and cook: Add the chicken stock. Bring to a boil and reduce to a simmer. Let cook undisturbed for about 15 minutes, or until the pasta is soft and the stock absorbed. The pasta will be past "al dente" but shouldn\'t be cooked to a mush.\n8 Serve: Place in serving bowls and garnish with crumbled chorizo, goat cheese, avocado, cilantro, and crema fresca or sour cream.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'
b"Save It Print\nHow to Make Perfect Guacamole Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesYield: Serves 2-4\nBe careful handling chiles if using. Wash your hands thoroughly after handling and do not touch your eyes or the area near your eyes with your hands for several hours.\nINGREDIENTS\n2 ripe avocados\n1/4 teaspoon of salt, more to taste\n1 tablespoon fresh lime juice or lemon juice\n2 tablespoons to 1/4 cup of minced red onion or thinly sliced green onion\n1-2 serrano chiles, stems and seeds removed, minced\n2 tablespoons cilantro (leaves and tender stems), finely chopped\nA dash of freshly grated black pepper\n1/2 ripe tomato, seeds and pulp removed, chopped\nRed radishes or jicama, to garnish\nTortilla chips, to serve\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Cut the avocado, remove flesh: Cut the avocados in half. Remove the pit. Score the inside of the avocado with a blunt knife and scoop out the flesh with a spoon. (See How to Cut and Peel an Avocado.) Place in a bowl.\n2 Mash with a fork: Using a fork, roughly mash the avocado. (Don't overdo it! The guacamole should be a little chunky.)\n3 Add salt, lime juice, and the rest: Sprinkle with salt and lime (or lemon) juice. The acid in the lime juice will provide some balance to the richness of the avocado and will help delay the avocados from turning brown.\nAdd the chopped onion, cilantro, black pepper, and chiles. Chili peppers vary individually in their hotness. So, start with a half of one chili pepper and add to the guacamole to your desired degree of hotness.\nRemember that much of this is done to taste because of the variability in the fresh ingredients. Start with this recipe and adjust to your taste.\nChilling tomatoes hurts their flavor, so if you want to add chopped tomato to your guacamole, add it just before serving.\n4 Serve: Serve immediately, or if making a few hours ahead, place plastic wrap on the surface of the guacamole and press down to cover it and to prevent air reaching it. (The oxygen in the air causes oxidation which will turn the guacamole brown.) Refrigerate until ready to serve.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b"Save It Print\nFresh Tomato Salsa (Pico de Gallo) Recipe\nPrep time: 6 minutesYield: Makes 3 to 4 cups of salsa\nWhen using fresh chile peppers always taste first before adding! Some peppers are hotter than others and you really can't tell unless you taste them. Just take a very small taste. You'll be able to gauge the heat of the pepper and will be better able to judge how much you need.\nINGREDIENTS\n2 to 3 medium sized fresh tomatoes (1 to 1 1/2 pounds), stems removed\n1/2 red onion\n2 serrano chiles or 1 jalape\xc3\xb1o chile (stems, ribs, seeds removed), less or more to taste\nJuice of one lime\n1/2 cup chopped cilantro\nSalt and pepper to taste\nPinch dried oregano (crumble in your fingers before adding), more to taste\nPinch ground cumin, more to taste\nMETHOD\n1 Prep the ingredients: Roughly chop the tomatoes, chiles, and onions. Be careful while handling the chile peppers. Use a plastic baggie or disposable gloves to handle them, or wash your hands thoroughly with soap and hot water after handling and avoid touching your eyes for several hours.\nSet aside some of the seeds from the peppers. If the salsa isn't hot enough, you can add a few for more heat.\n2 Make the salsa: Place all of the ingredients in the bowl of a food processor fitted with the blade. Pulse only a few times, just enough to finely dice the ingredients and not enough to pur\xc3\xa9e. If you don't have a food processor, you can finely dice by hand.\n3 Adjust seasonings: Place in a serving bowl. Add salt and pepper to taste. If the chilies make the salsa too hot, add some more chopped tomato. If it's not hot enough, carefully add a few of the seeds from the chilies, or add a little more ground cumin.\nLet the salsa sit for an hour (room temperature or chilled) for the flavors to combine.\n4 Serve: Serve with chips, tortillas, tacos, burritos, tostadas, quesadillas, pinto or black beans. The salsa will keep refrigerated for up to 5 days.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b'Print\nMozzarella and Basil Stuffed Tomatoes Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 15 minutesYield: Makes 8 stuffed tomato cups, 4 servings\nIf preparing gluten-free, use gluten-free bread or bread crumbs.\nINGREDIENTS\n4 medium tomatoes with firm, fleshy walls, 2 1/2 inches wide\n1 cup shredded mozzarella cheese\n1/3 cup grated parmesan cheese, divided\n1/4 cup packed fresh basil, chopped, plus more for garnish\n1 slice of bread (enough to make 1/4 cup breadcrumbs)\n1 tablespoon melted salted butter\n1 teaspoon minced garlic\n1/4 teaspoon salt\n1/8 teaspoon pepper\nOlive oil for drizzling\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Preheat oven to 400\xc2\xb0F.\n2 Make the soft breadcrumbs: To make the 1/4 cup soft breadcrumbs, remove the crust from 1 slice of bread (preferably stale) and either pulse in a small food processor or shred with a fork until the bread resembles fine, sand-like crumbs.\n3 Prepare the tomatoes: Slice the tomatoes in half horizontally around the equator and use a spoon to scoop out the flesh. Be careful not to puncture the walls of the tomato, but if you do, the filling will plug the hole. Place empty tomato halves in a casserole dish and season with salt and pepper.\nUsing your hands or a spoon, separate the seeds from the scooped out tomato flesh and transfer the flesh to a cutting board. Discard the seeds and the tomato water. Chop the flesh and set aside for the stuffing.\n4 Make the stuffing: In a medium bowl, add the mozzarella cheese, 1/4 cup of the parmesan cheese, basil, breadcrumbs, butter, garlic, salt, and pepper and stir to thoroughly combine.\n5 Bake: Using two spoons, fill the tomato halves with the stuffing. Sprinkle filled tomatoes with the remaining parmesan cheese and drizzle with olive oil. Bake for 15 minutes, or until tomatoes are tender, then broil on high for 1 minute until the filling begins to bubble and brown.\n6 Serve: Garnish with a few torn basil leaves and serve hot.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'
b'Save It Print\nBlistered Shishito Peppers Recipe\nPrep time: 3 minutesCook time: 6 minutesYield: serves 2-4\nRecipe is easily doubled, but cook in batches so as not to crowd the pan.\nINGREDIENTS\n1 teaspoon extra virgin olive oil\n20 or so shishito peppers (about 4 or 5 ounces, 1 small basket)\nSprinkle of kosher salt\n2 tablespoons balsamic vinegar (optional)\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Toss peppers with oil: Toss shishito peppers with extra virgin olive oil in a bowl, so the peppers are well coated.\n2 Sear in frying pan: Heat a well seasoned cast iron (or a pan that can take high heat) on high heat. When the pan is hot, add the peppers to the pan in a single layer. Let the peppers sear and blister on one side, then use tongs to turn them over individually to sear on the other side.\n3 Salt: Remove to a bowl and sprinkle the shishito peppers with salt.\n4 Make balsamic glaze (Optional):  Add a couple tablespoons of balsamic vinegar* to the pan. Remove from heat, and let bubble until the vinegar reduces to a glaze, which should be very quickly. Pour over the blistered shishito peppers.\n*Balsamic vinegar can be syrupy and sweet, or thin and acidic. Use the syrupy kind. If what you have is thin and very acidic, stir with a half teaspoon of sugar or honey before adding to the hot pan.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'
b"Save It Print\nBaba Ganoush (Eggplant Dip) Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 1 hourYield: Serves 4-8 as an appetizer\nINGREDIENTS\n1-2 globe eggplants (totaling 2 pounds or 900 g)\n3 tablespoons extra virgin olive oil\n2-3 tablespoons roasted tahini (sesame paste)\n1-2 garlic cloves (more or less depending on how garlicky you want your baba ghanouj to be), finely chopped\n1/2 teaspoon ground cumin\nJuice of one lemon (about 2 1/2 tablespoons)\nSalt and cayenne pepper to taste\n1 tablespoon chopped parsley\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Roast the eggplants: Preheat oven to 400\xc2\xb0F. Poke the eggplants in several places with the tines of a fork. Cut the eggplants in half lengthwise and brush the cut sides lightly with olive oil (about 1 tablespoon).\nPlace on a baking sheet, cut side down, and roast until very tender, about 35-40 minutes. Remove from oven and allow to cool for 15 minutes.\nAlternate Grilling Instructions: Preheat grill. Poke the eggplants in a few places with a fork, then rub the eggplants with 1 tablespoon of the olive oil.\nGrill over high heat, turning as each side blackens. Put the charred eggplants in a paper bag, close the bag and let the eggplants steam in their skins for 15-20 minutes.\n2 Scoop the eggplant flesh into a large bowl and mash well with a fork.\n3 Add garlic, olive oil, tahini, cumin, lemon juice, salt, cayenne: Combine the eggplant, minced garlic, remaining olive oil (about 2 tablespoons), tahini, cumin, 2 tablespoons of the lemon juice, the salt, and a pinch of cayenne.\nMash well. You want the mixture to be somewhat smooth but still retaining some of the eggplant's texture.\n4 Cool and season to taste: Allow the baba ganoush to cool to room temperature, then season to taste with additional lemon juice, salt, and cayenne.\nIf you want, swirl a little olive oil on the top. Sprinkle with fresh chopped parsley.\nServe with pita bread, crackers, toast, sliced baguette, celery, or cucumber slices.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
