b'Save It Print\nThe Best Nachos Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 15 minutesYield: Serves 6\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the spice mix:\n2 tablespoons chili powder\n1 1/2 teaspoons kosher salt\n1 teaspoon granulated garlic\n1 teaspoon granulated onion\n1 teaspoon ground cumin\n1/2 teaspoon dried oregano\n1/4 teaspoon black pepper\nPinch of cayenne pepper (optional)\nFor the nachos:\n1 teaspoon vegetable oil\n1 pound ground beef (80:20 lean-to-fat ratio)\n16 ounces (2 cups) refried beans, canned or homemade\n1/4 cup water\n1 large bag of tortilla chips\n4 ounces cheddar cheese, grated (about 2 cups), plus more for topping\n4 ounces Colby Jack cheese, grated (about 2 cups), plus more for topping\n1 cup pico de gallo, store-bought or homemade, plus more for topping\n1/4 cup chopped cilantro\n1 sliced jalape\xc3\xb1o (pickled or fresh)\nOptional toppings:\nGuacamole\nSalsa\nSour cream\nCanned black olives\nSliced green onions\nShredded lettuce\nCorn\nHot sauce\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Preheat the oven to 350\xc2\xb0F.\n2 Make the taco spice blend: Combine all of the spices (chili powder through cayenne) together in a small bowl.\n3 Make the beef and bean topping: Heat the vegetable oil on medium high heat until it begins to shimmer. Add the ground beef to the pan and season it with all of the taco spice blend. As the meat cooks, use a spoon to break the meat up into crumbles.\nCook for about 8 minutes until the meat has browned and drain the fat using a colander.\nReturn the meat to the pan and add the refried beans and the water. Heat the mixture until the beans are smooth and warmed through. Reduce the heat to low and keep the beef-bean mixture warm while you prepare the chips.\n4 Toast the chips: On a 13x18-inch oven-safe platter or sheet pan, arrange the tortilla chips in a single layer, overlapping them slightly. Toast the chips in the preheated oven for 5 minutes, or just until you begin to smell their aroma.\n5 Assemble and bake the nachos: Carefully remove the pan from the oven and top with one half of the shredded cheeses. Allow the heat from the chips to melt the cheese slightly before topping the chips with the beef and bean mixture.\nSprinkle the remaining cheese over the beef and return the pan to the oven for 5 minutes, or until the cheese has fully melted.\n6 Top and serve: Top the nachos with the pico de gallo, chopped cilantro, jalape\xc3\xb1o slices, or any of your preferred toppings. Serve hot.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'

If you use cherry tomatoes, just quarter them, don't bother blanching or peeling them.\nINGREDIENTS\n6 or 7 ripe tomatoes (about 1 1/2 lbs)\n2 cloves garlic, minced (about 2 teaspoons)\n1 Tbsp extra virgin olive oil\n1 teaspoon balsamic vinegar\n6-8 fresh basil leaves, thinly sliced* or chopped\n3/4 teaspoon sea salt, more or less to taste\n1/2 teaspoon freshly ground black pepper, more or less to taste\n1 baguette French bread or similar Italian bread\n1/4 cup (60 ml) olive oil\n*To thinly slice basil leaves, stack the leaves on top of each other and roll up like a cigar. As the water is heating make shallow cuts in a cross pattern at the tip ends of the tomatoes (this will make the tomatoes easier to peel).\nOnce the water is boiling, remove the pot from the heat. Put the tomatoes in the hot water and blanch for 1 minute.\nRemove with a slotted spoon and let sit until cool enough to handle. Then gently peel off the tomato skins. Note, tomatoes love salt; you may need to add more than you expect.\n4 Toast the baguette slices: Use a bread knife to slice the baguette on the diagonal making half-inch thick slices. Brush one side of each slice with olive oil (a pastry brush helps here) and place olive oil-side down on a baking sheet or roasting pan.\nThe baguette slices will toast best in the top rack of your oven, so you may need to work in batches to toast them all.\nWhen the oven has reached 450\xc2\xb0F (230\xc2\xb0C) place the slices in the oven on the top rack and toast for 5 to 6 minutes until lightly browned around the edges.\nIf you want you can toast the bread slices without coating them first in olive oil. Toast them until lightly browned on both sides. Then cut a clove of garlic in half and rub over one side of the toast. Then brush with olive oil. (See Easiest Ever Garlic Bread.)\n5 Serve toasted bread with tomato mixture: Arrange the toasted bread on a platter, olive oil side facing up (the olive oil will help create a temporary barrier keeping the bread from getting soggy from the chopped tomatoes).\nEither serve the toasts plain with a bowl of the tomato bruschetta mixture on the side for people to top their own, or use a spoon to gently top each toasted bread slice with some of the tomato mixture. If you top each slice individually, do it right before serving.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. b"Save It Print\nSwedish Meatballs Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 1 hourYield: Serves 4 to 6 as a main, 8 to 12 as an appetizer\nLingonberry jelly is traditionally used with Swedish meatballs; you can substitute cranberry, red currant or raspberry jelly if you can't find lingonberry jelly.\nThis recipe serves 4 to 6 people and can easily be doubled for serving a party.\nINGREDIENTS\nMeatballs:\n1 Tbsp butter\n1/2 large yellow or white onion, peeled, grated (use the large holes of a box cheese grater)\n1/4 cup milk\n3 slices of bread, crusts removed, bread cut into cubes (2 cups of cubed bread)\n1 large egg\n3/4 pound ground beef\n1/2 pound ground pork\n1 teaspoon kosher salt\n1 teaspoon black pepper\n1/2 teaspoon freshly ground nutmeg\n1/2 teaspoon ground cardamom\nSauce:\n3 Tbsp butter\n3 Tbsp flour\n2 cups beef stock\n1/4 cup sour cream (use full-fat sour cream or the sauce may curdle)\nSalt and pepper\n2 Tbsp of Lingonberry, red currant, raspberry or cranberry jelly, less or more to taste (optional)\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Soak bread in milk, shred: Place the cubed bread in a large bowl and mix with the milk. Let sit for 5 to 10 minutes for the bread to absorb all of the milk. Once the bread has soaked up the milk, shred with the tines of a fork or by hand.\n2 Saut\xc3\xa9 grated onion: Melt the butter in a saut\xc3\xa9 pan on medium-high heat. Stir in the grated onion and cook until translucent and softened, 3-4 minutes. Remove from heat and let cool for a minute.\n3 Make meatball mixture with bread, onions, eggs, meat, spices: Stir the cooled onions into the milk bread mixture. Add the eggs, ground pork and beef, salt, pepper, nutmeg, and cardamom. Use your (clean) hands to mix everything together until well combined.\n(If you have extra time, chilling the mixture for 20 minutes or so will make it easier to roll out the meatballs.)\n4 Form meatballs: Use your hands to form the mixture into meatballs about 1 1/4-inch to 1 1/2-inch wide and place them on a plate or sheet pan. This recipe should make about 40 meatballs. Note that the meatballs will be a bit on the wet side.\n5 Brown meatballs on all sides: Heat 3 Tbsp of butter in a large saut\xc3\xa9 pan on medium heat. When the butter is melted and foamy, start adding some meatballs to the pan.\nWorking in batches as to not crowd the pan, slowly brown the meatballs on all sides. Use a spoon or tongs to turn them. Handle the meatballs gently so they do not break apart as you turn them.\n   Once the meatballs have browned on all sides and are just cooked through, remove them from the pan to a bowl. You'll warm the meatballs in the sauce later.\nOnce you have removed the meatballs from the pan, wipe out the butter and browned and blackened bits with a paper towel and rinse out the pan.\nWe'll want to start with fresh butter because that way we won't pick up any burnt bits from the pan, and we will be able to more accurately gauge the amount of fat in the pan for making the meatball sauce in the next step.\n6 Make a roux: To make the sauce, first make the roux. Add 3 Tbsp of fresh butter to the pan. Heat the butter in the pan on medium heat until it melts and starts to bubble up.\nSlowly whisk in 3 Tbsp of flour. Stir until smooth. Continue to stir, allowing the flour mixture to cook, several minutes, until the roux is the color of coffee-with-cream.\n   7 Add stock to roux to make sauce: When the roux has cooked to a lovely shade of light brown, slowly add the stock to the roux, stirring as you add the stock.\nThe stock will sputter at first and the roux may seize up, but keep adding the stock slowly and keep stirring. Eventually the sauce will loosen and become silky.\n8 Stir in sour cream and jelly if using: Remove the pan from heat and stir in the sour cream. If you are including jelly, either stir it in now or serve it on the side. Taste for seasonings and add more salt and pepper to taste (I use about 1/2 teaspoon of kosher salt, and 1/4 teaspoon of pepper.)\n9 Add meatballs to sauce: Return the meatballs to the pan with the sauce and cook on low heat to warm the meatballs through for a few minutes.\n10 Serve: Serve over mashed potatoes or egg noodles. Or serve individual Swedish meatballs dipped in gravy as an appetizer.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"

b'Save It Print\nHow to Make Naan\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 10 minutesRise time: 6 hoursYield: 16 naan\nINGREDIENTS\n1 cup lukewarm milk\n1 1/2 teaspoons active dry yeast\n2 teaspoons sugar\n4 cups all-purpose flour + extra for dusting\n2 teaspoons kosher salt\n2 tablespoons olive oil or canola oil + extra for greasing the bowl\n1/2 cup plain yogurt\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Prepare a bowl: Lightly grease a large bowl with a little bit of oil. You will put your dough in this bowl to let it rise. Set the bowl aside.\n2 Prepare the dough: In a Pyrex liquid measuring cup or a small mixing bowl, combine the lukewarm milk, sugar, and active dry yeast. The milk should be just warm to the touch. If it\xe2\x80\x99s too hot you can kill the yeast. Let it sit for 5 minutes.\nIn another large mixing bowl, whisk the flour and salt together. Add yogurt, oil and milk-yeast mixture. Use a wooden spoon or your hands to combine the dough. The dough should be soft and sticky at this point.\n3 Knead the dough: Dust your countertop with flour. Transfer the dough to the counter. Knead together until a soft dough forms, about 5 minutes. If the dough feels dry and is too tough to knead, add about 1-2 tablespoons of water, a little bit at a time, until the dough is easier to work with.\n4 Let the dough rise: Transfer the dough to the greased bowl. Cover the bowl with plastic wrap or a damp towel. Place in a dark, warm, dry place. I place it in my oven (it\xe2\x80\x99s not on) to let it rise, but your countertop is fine. Let the dough rise for 3-4 hours or until it more than doubles in size.\n5 Punch down the dough and let it rise again: Punch the risen dough down. Knead for another minute. Return the dough to the bowl, cover it again and let it rise for another 45 minutes to 1 hour.\n6 Divide the dough: Dust your countertop with flour. Turn the dough out onto the counter and knead it for another minute or two until its smooth. Divide the dough into 16 smaller balls of equal size (about 2 ounces each).\nUsing a rolling pin, roll the balls into a teardrop shape. About 2-3 inches wide, 6-7 inches long, and about 1/8 inch thick. They don\xe2\x80\x99t have to be perfectly uniform.\n7 Cook the naan: If using herbs or spices, sprinkle one side of the bread with those now. Brush the other side with water. Set a medium-sized heavy pan or cast iron skillet with a lid over medium-high heat.\nCheck the heat of the pan by flicking water on it. If it evaporates on contact, it\xe2\x80\x99s ready. Once the pan is hot, place the naan wet side down into the skillet.\nCover it with a lid. Let it cook for about 30 seconds or until you see bubbles on it. Flip the naan, brush it with butter or ghee, and cook it uncovered for another 10 seconds. Serve it hot.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'

b"Save It Print\nMussels in White Wine Sauce Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 15 minutesYield: Serves 2 as a meal, 4 as an appetizer or side dish\nWhen purchasing mussels be sure they smell like the ocean, not fishy.\nDon't buy any whose shells are cracked or open or any that refuse to close their shells when you handle or tap them, those are likely dying or dead.\nTry to cook the mussels immediately (unwrap them as soon as you get home), but if you have to wait place them in a bowl and cover them with a damp towel so they can breathe.\nINGREDIENTS\n2 pounds mussels, scrubbed clean under running water\n1/2 cup dry white wine\n2 tablespoons butter\n1/4 cup minced shallots\n1 tablespoon minced garlic\n2 teaspoons flour (optional, omit for gluten-free version)\n1/4 cup minced parsley\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Clean and prep mussels: Put the mussels in a bowl of salted water (1 Tbsp salt per quart of water) for 10-15 minutes. Throw out any that are wide open or refuse to close when you handle them as these ones are likely dead.\nLooking over the closed mussels, see if any still have their beards (long hairy byssal threads which help anchor the mussel to surfaces) and pull them out, pulling slowly and strongly towards the hinge of the shell.\n2 Put wine, mussels in bottom of large pot, steam until mussels open: Put 1/2 cup of dry white wine in the bottom of a large pot (at least 4-quart). Add the mussels to the pot. Cover and bring to a boil and then reduce the heat to low. As the mussels cook, they will release their highly flavored water into the pot.\nCook until shells have opened, and the mussels are just cooked, looking steamed and soft, 5 to 7 minutes. Take care not to overcook, or the mussels will be rubbery and hard.\n3 Remove cooked mussels, save the cooking liquid: Once the mussels are cooked, carefully remove them from the pot to a bowl, one-by-one using tongs, including those that have broken loose from their shells. Do not discard the liquid in the pot!\nLet the water in the pot settle for a minute. Any grit will settle to the bottom. Gently pour out the cooking water into a measuring cup, leaving the grit in the pot to discard of later. If the water you've measured out is still a little gritty, filter out the grit using a sieve.\n4 Saut\xc3\xa9 shallots and garlic in butter, add flour: Melt the butter in a medium-sized saucepan. Add the shallots and cook a couple minutes until translucent. Add the garlic and cook a minute more. If you want your sauce to be a little thick, add a teaspoon or two of flour to the pan, stir to combine. (Otherwise skip the flour.)\n5 Add mussel cooking water to create sauce: Slowly add about a cup of the filtered mussel cooking water to the saucepan, stirring to create a smooth sauce. Add the minced parsley to the sauce.\n6 Pour sauce over mussels to serve: Place mussels in serving bowls. Pour some sauce over each bowl of mussels.\nServe immediately. Serve with crusty bread for dipping in the sauce.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b"Save It Print\nCranberry Glazed Meatballs Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 40 minutesYield: Makes about 30 meatballs\nINGREDIENTS\nCranberry Glaze\n1 cup sugar\n1 cup water\n1 12-ounce bag of cranberries, fresh or frozen (no need to defrost)\nA pinch of salt\n1 teaspoon orange zest\n1 teaspoon minced ginger\n2 teaspoons apple cider vinegar or white vinegar\n1/8 to 1/4 teaspoon cayenne, to taste\nMeatballs\n2 large slices white bread, crusts removed, bread torn into small pieces (approximately one cup, packed, or 2 ounces of bread, can sub 1/2 cup of plain breadcrumbs)\n2 Tbsp milk\nA generous 1/4 cup ricotta cheese\n1 egg\n1 1/4 pounds ground turkey\n1 teaspoon kosher salt\n1 1/2 teaspoons dried thyme\n1 scant teaspoon fennel seeds\nFlour for dusting (optional)\nVegetable oil\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Make the cranberry glaze by mixing all the glaze ingredients except the cayenne in a small pot. (Be sure to scrape the outside of the sieve with the spatula.) Add cayenne to taste.\n2 Prepare the meatballs: While the cranberries are cooking, prepare the meatballs. Add the ground turkey, salt, thyme, fennel seeds and milk-sprinkled bread.\nGently mix with your (clean) hands until the ingredients are all incorporated. Don't overwork the meatball mixture or the meatballs will become too dense.\n3 Gently roll out small meatballs about an 1 inch wide with the palms of your hands and set them on a baking sheet or large plate.\n4 Brown the meatballs: Heat 2 Tbsp vegetable oil in a wide saut\xc3\xa9 pan on medium heat. Working in batches, add the meatballs, taking care not to crowd the pan, and brown all over. Use a fork to gentle nudge the meatballs, turning them.\nNote that the meatballs will probably be a bit on the wet side, which may cause some splattering as you cook them in the oil. To reduce that, you may want to sprinkle some flour on the meatballs, or roll them in flour, before they go in the pan. Add more oil to the pan as needed.\n5 Add glaze and simmer: Once the meatballs are browned and the glaze has been strained, add the glaze to the pan with the meatballs. Let simmer, uncovered, until the glaze reduces a bit and the meatballs cook through, about 5 minutes.\nRemove the meatballs to a serving dish. Pour over remaining cranberry glaze. b"Save It Print\nBacon-Wrapped Shrimp Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 10 minutesBrining time (optional) time: 30 minutesYield: Makes 12 pieces\nYou'll need about 1 strip of bacon for every 2 shrimp.\nI highly recommend brining the shrimp first. The brine will help keep the shrimp from drying out in the time it takes for the bacon to cook.\nIf grilling, I recommend using long, flat skewers which make turning the shrimp on the grill easier. If you don't have flat skewers, I've used two thin bamboo skewers (soaked in water for 30 minutes beforehand) to the same effect.\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the brine (optional, but recommended):\n1/4 cup (Diamond Crystal) kosher salt (if using Morton's kosher salt, use only 3 tablespoons)\n1/4 cup sugar\n4 cups water\n1 cup ice\nFor the bacon-wrapped shrimp:\n1 pound (12 to 20 count), raw, peeled and deveined shrimp (tail on)\n2 tablespoons extra virgin olive oil\nZest from 1 lime\n2 tablespoons lime juice\n1/2 teaspoon chipotle powder or chili powder (less or more to taste)\n6 to 10 strips thin bacon, cut in half (half as many pieces of bacon as there are shrimp)\nSpecial equipment:\nSkewers (for grilling) or toothpicks (for oven)\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Brine the shrimp (optional, but recommended): Whisk the salt, sugar, and water until the salt and sugar dissolve. Add the ice and the shrimp, and let sit for 30 minutes (no longer). Remove the shrimp from the brine.\n2 Prepare grill or preheat oven: Prepare grill on high, direct heat (if grilling) or preheat the oven to 400\xc2\xb0F. If grilling and using thin bamboo or wood skewers, soak them in water first for 30 minutes.\n3 Season the shrimp: Mix together in a small bowl the lime zest, lime juice, olive oil, and chipotle powder. Stir the shrimp into the lime chipotle mixture; make sure each piece is well coated.\n4 Partially cook the bacon: Spread the bacon pieces out over several layers of paper towels on a microwave-safe plate. Cover with another layer of paper towel. Microwave on high until the bacon fat begins to melt but the bacon is still somewhat pliable, about 1 1/2 to 2 minutes.\n5 Wrap the shrimp with bacon: Working one at a time, wrap a half piece of partially cooked bacon around each piece of shrimp.\n6 Prep the shrimp for cooking: If you are grilling, thread the shrimp onto skewers.\nIf you are using the oven, secure each the bacon onto the shrimp with toothpicks. Place the bacon-wrapped shrimp on a foil-lined baking pan. Brush remaining lime chipotle mixture on the outside of the bacon-wrapped shrimp.\n7 Grill or bake the shrimp: Grill uncovered for 3 minutes on each side (less or more time depending on the heat of your grill), or bake in the 400\xc2\xb0F oven for 8 to 11 minutes, or until the bacon is lightly browned and the shrimp is cooked through.\nHello! b"Save It Print\nAir Fryer Cranberry Brie Canap\xc3\xa9s Recipe\nCranberries are widely available this time of year, and you can use fresh or frozen for this recipe. And brie is mild in flavor, but when served with foods that are tart (such as cranberries), the creaminess is amplified. Don\xe2\x80\x99t concern yourself with removing the rind from your wheel of brie: it\xe2\x80\x99s completely edible!\nINGREDIENTS\nSpiced Cranberry Sauce\n1-inch piece of ginger, or 1/4 teaspoon ground ginger\n1 vanilla bean, or 1 1/2 teaspoons vanilla extract\n1 (12-ounce) bag (about 3 1/2 cups) fresh or frozen cranberries, rinsed\n1 3-inch cinnamon stick (or 1/2 teaspoon ground cinnamon)\n3 sprigs of fresh rosemary, divided\nJuice of 1 naval orange (about 1 /2 cup)\n1 tablespoon of orange zest\n1/4 cup maple syrup\nPinch of kosher salt\n1/2 cup packed light brown sugar\nCanap\xc3\xa9s\n8 ounces brie cheese, cut into 1\xe2\x80\x9d cubes\n2 (1.9 ounce) boxes fully baked phyllo shells (30)\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1. Prep the ginger and vanilla: Peel and then thinly slice the ginger (using the edge of a spoon is the easiest way). Use a sharp paring knife to split the vanilla bean down its length.\nOpen the vanilla bean slightly to ensure the seeds are extracted during cooking.\n2. Make the Cranberry Topping: In a 3-quart saucepan, combine the ginger, vanilla bean, cranberries, cinnamon stick, 1 sprig of rosemary, orange juice and zest, maple syrup, and the salt.\nStir the ingredients together and heat over medium-high heat for 3 minutes, or until the mixture starts to boil.\n3. Reduce the topping: Reduce the heat to low, and allow the cranberries to cook until they begin to split open. Stirring frequently, cook the cranberries for 8 to 10 minutes, or until they've reduced a bit and thickened to a jelly-like consistency.\nRemove the pan from the stove and add the light brown sugar. Stir constantly to dissolve the sugar and coat the cranberries in a thick glaze.\nAllow the cranberries to cool to room temperature, leaving the spices in it.\n4. Prep your Air Fryer: Set your Cuisinart\xc2\xae Air Fryer Toaster Oven\xe2\x80\x99s function dial to Air Fry and the temperature dial to 300\xc2\xb0F. Remove both the Air Fryer basket and the baking pan from the oven, then turn the on/oven dial to 10 minutes to preheat the oven.\n5. Fill the phyllo cups: While your Air Fryer is heating, fill your phyllo shells with the pieces of brie. It\xe2\x80\x99s easier to leave the shells in the packaging while you\xe2\x80\x99re trying to fill them. Remove the shells from the plastic packaging and arrange them, a dozen at a time, in the Air Fryer basket.\n6. Bake the shells: Place the baking pan, with the Air Fryer basket nestled inside, into the oven in position 1. Bake the shells for five minutes.\nOnce the shells have finished baking, remove them from the Air Fryer Toaster Oven and carefully remove them from the basket. Repeat this step, baking the shells by the dozen, until they are all baked.\n7. Prep the rosemary topping: While the shells are baking, pick off the remaining rosemary leaves in clusters of two or three leaves. Set aside to garnish the canap\xc3\xa9s when you\xe2\x80\x99re done topping them with the sauce.\n8. Top with cranberry sauce and garnish: Once you have baked all of the brie-filled shells, top each with a teaspoon of cranberry sauce, leaving the cinnamon stick, vanilla bean (if you used one), rosemary sprigs and slices of ginger in the pan. Pull out any pieces of rosemary orAny remaining cranberry sauce may be stored in the refrigerator for up to one week.\nGarnish the top of each canap\xc3\xa9 with the sprigs of rosemary leaves you picked earlier.\n9. Serve! These canap\xc3\xa9s are best served immediately, but can be held at room temperature for up to 2 hours.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"

b'Save It Print\nGrilled Artichokes Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 45 minutesYield: Serves 4\nINGREDIENTS\n1 tablespoon chopped fresh herbs such as rosemary, oregano, thyme\n1/3 cup extra virgin olive oil\n2 cloves garlic, cut in half (no need to peel)\n1 bay leaf\n1 lemon, cut into wedges\n2 to 4 large globe artichokes\nSalt\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Steep herbs in warm olive oil: Place chopped fresh herbs in a small bowl (not the bay leaf), cover with olive oil. Microwave on high heat for 30 seconds (or heat oil and herbs on the stovetop until warm). Let the herbs steep in the warm olive oil while you prepare the artichokes.\n2 Prep the artichokes: Prepare a large pot with an inch of water at the bottom. Add the cut cloves of garlic and the bay leaf, and place a steamer rack in the pot.\nTo prepare the artichokes, have lemon wedges ready. If you want a nice presentation, use scissors to snip away the pointy tips of the artichoke leaves. As you trim the artichokes, rub the cut areas with juice from the lemon wedges to prevent the artichokes from turning brown from oxidation.\nUse a vegetable peeler to cut away the thick outer layer of the artichoke stems. Trim the stems to 2 inches from the base of the artichoke. Cut off and discard the top 1/2 inch of the artichokes. Cut the artichokes in half.\nUse a strong metal spoon to scoop out the fuzzy chokes and the small inner artichoke leaves. Rub lemon juice all over the inside and exposed cut areas of the artichokes.\n\n3 Steam the artichokes: Heat the water in the large pot with a steamer rack on high. When it comes to a boil, reduce the heat to medium high and place the artichoke halves, cut side down on the steam rack.\nCover. Steam for 20 minutes (less or more, depending on the size of the artichokes), until you can easily pull off the outer leaves, and you can pierce the heart easily with a knife.\nThe artichokes can be just a tiny bit less cooked than would be typically perfect for steamed artichokes, as you will be cooking them further on the grill.\n4 Grill the artichokes: Prepare your grill for direct, high heat. Use a pastry brush to brush the artichoke all over with the herb infused oil. Sprinkle all over with salt.\nPlace the artichoke halves cut-side-down on the grill grates. Cover, and grill for 5 to 10 minutes, until you have nice grill mark on the cut sides of the artichokes.\nTo serve, sprinkle the cut sides with more lemon juice. Serve alone or with mayonnaise, remoulade, or aioli.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'
b'Print\nSpanish Roasted Potatoes with Tomato Sauce (Patatas Bravas) Recipe\nPrep time: 5 minutesCook time: 1 hourYield: Serves 4 as a side dish\nThis recipe makes more than enough sauce for the potatoes, so you can double the amount of potatoes for more servings, or save the extra sauce for later. It will keep a week in the refrigerator.\nINGREDIENTS\n2 pounds Yukon gold potatoes, or other waxy potato (peeled or un-peeled, your choice), cut into 1 to 1 1/2-inch chunks\nExtra virgin olive oil\nSalt\n1/2 medium yellow onion, chopped\n3 garlic cloves, chopped\n1/2 cup white wine (can substitute stock)\n2 tablespoons tomato paste\nA 14-ounce can of crushed tomatoes\n2 teaspoons Tabasco or other hot sauce\n1 teaspoon smoked paprika\n1 teaspoon salt\n1 teaspoon sugar\nMETHOD\n1 Roast the potatoes: Preheat oven to 375\xc2\xb0F. Toss the potatoes with 3 tablespoons of olive oil and salt well. Arrange in one layer in a casserole pan or rimmed baking tray and roast until browned, about 50 minutes.\n2 Saut\xc3\xa9 onions and garlic: While the potatoes are roasting, make the sauce. Heat 2 tablespoons of olive oil in a medium pot set over medium-high heat. Saut\xc3\xa9 the chopped onions, stirring occasionally, for 4-5 minutes, or until they begin to brown on the edges. Add the garlic and saut\xc3\xa9 another 2 minutes.\n3 Make the sauce: Add the white wine to the pan and turn the heat to high. Boil on a high boil until the wine is reduced by half, then add the tomato paste and stir to combine. Add the crushed tomatoes, Tabasco sauce, salt, sugar and smoked paprika. Stir well and reduce the heat to a bare simmer. Let the sauce cook slowly while the potatoes roast. If you want, you can use a blender or an immersion blender to pur\xc3\xa9e the sauce until smooth.\n4 Toss potatoes with sauce, continue to roast: When the potatoes are well browned, toss with the tomato sauce and return to the casserole pan. Continue to roast until the tomato sauce dries out a bit on the potatoes and caramelizes, about 10 minutes.\nServe with the remaining tomato sauce as an appetizer or side dish.\nHello! b"Save It Print\nSpicy Turkey and Zucchini Burger Recipe\nPrep time: 25 minutesCook time: 25 minutesYield: Serves 4-6\nRecipe adapted from the cookbook Jerusalem by Yotam Ottolenghi and Sami Tamimi.\nINGREDIENTS\n1 pound ground turkey meat\nJust under 2 cups, lightly packed, coarsely grated zucchini (from about 2 to 3 small zucchinis or one medium zucchini)\n3 green onions, thinly sliced, onion greens included\n2 tablespoons chopped fresh mint (spearmint)\n2 tablespoons chopped fresh cilantro (tender stems included)\n1 clove garlic, crushed and minced\n1 teaspoon ground cumin\n1 teaspoon Kosher salt\n1/2 teaspoon freshly ground black pepper\n1/2 teaspoon cayenne\n3 tablespoons extra virgin olive oil\nSour cream sauce:\n1/4 cup sour cream\n1/3 cup plain Greek yogurt\n1 teaspoon grated lemon zest\n1 tablespoon lemon juice\n1/2 teaspoon minced garlic\n2 teaspoons extra virgin olive oil\n1/4 teaspoon salt\nPinch of freshly ground black pepper\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Make the sour cream sauce by placing all of the sauce ingredients in a bowl and stirring until combined. Stir to combine.\nWith your hands, mix in the ground turkey until the zucchini mixture is well distributed through the ground turkey.\n3 Form patties: Use your hands to form 3 to 4 inch wide patties, placing them on a baking sheet. Note that the patties will be rather wet, so they may be a little tricky to handle.\n4 Fry gently: Heat 3 Tbsp of olive oil in a large frying pan on medium high heat. Once the oil is hot, lower the heat to medium.\nWorking in batches, place the patties in the pan. Let cook for about 5 minutes, then flip the patties over and cook for another 5 to 6 minutes.\nYou want them to brown and to gently cook all the way through. If the temperature is too high, they'll get browned on the outside but the inside will still be raw. So, cook them gently.\nIf the outsides are browned and the insides still aren't done, lower the heat and cook longer.\n5 Remove to paper-towel lined plate: Once the first batch of patties are done, remove to a paper towel-lined plate while you cook the second batch. b'Save It Print\nGrilled Skirt Steak Skewers Recipe\nPrep time: 1 hourCook time: 20 minutesYield: Serves 6 to 8\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the marinade:\n1/3 cup extra virgin olive oil\n1/3 cup soy sauce\n1/4 cup honey\n2 cloves garlic, minced\n1 tablespoon red wine vinegar\n1-inch piece of ginger, sliced\n1/2 teaspoon red chili pepper flakes\n1/2 teaspoon freshly ground black pepper\nOther ingredients:\n1 1/2 to 2 pounds skirt steak, trimmed of membranes and silver skin\nOlive oil for grill grates\nSpecial equipment:\n25-30 bamboo or wooden skewers for grilling\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Soak the skewers in water: If using bamboo or wooden skewers, place them in a dish and cover with water to soak.\n2 Make marinade: Place all marinade ingredients in a small bowl and stir to combine. Set aside.\n3 Cut skirt steak in strips across the grain: Lay the skirt steak horizontally out on a cutting board. Notice the grain of the steak that goes up and down.\nCut the steak into segments (along the grain of the meat), about 6 to 8-inches long.\nThen, with each segment, turn the segment so the grain of the meat runs in a line from left to right, and cut thin strips (1/4 to 1/3-inch thick, 1 1/2-inch wide, 6 to 8-inches long), angling the knife, cutting across the grain.\n4 Marinate the steak slices: Place the steak slices in a non-reactive bowl or casserole dish. Toss with the marinade to coat. Chill and marinate for at least 30 minutes or up to 2 hours.\n5 Preheat grill, thread skewers: Preheat your grill, whether charcoal or gas, for high-direct heat. While the grill is preheating, thread the marinated skirt steak strips onto your pre-soaked skewers.\n6 Grill over high direct heat: When ready to grill, brush the grill grates with olive oil (helps to fold a paper towel, soak the towel in olive oil, and use long handled tongs to hold the soaked paper towel and spread oil on the grates).\nYou know your grill is hot enough when you can only stand to hold your hand 1 inch above the grill grates for one second.\nWorking in batches if necessary, lay the skirt steak skewers on the hot grill grates, perpendicular to the grates. Grill for 3 to 4 minutes per side, until cooked through.\nRemove from grill and let sit for a few minutes before serving.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. b"Save It Print\nGolden Cheddar Cheese Crisps Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 10 minutesYield: About 2 dozen crisps\nIf you'd like, you can substitute another semi-hard cheese for the cheddar, like Swiss or Gruyere.\nThe crisps are best the day they are made. If they've gone a little soft, just pop them back in the oven for a few minutes to warm them up before serving. They will re-crisp as they cool.\nINGREDIENTS\n6 ounces sharp cheddar (about 2 cups grated)\n1/4 cup all-purpose flour\n1 teaspoon paprika\n1/8 teaspoon baking powder\nPinch of cayenne pepper, to taste (optional)\n1 tablespoon unsalted butter, at room temperature\n1 tablespoon black sesame, poppy, coriander, or cumin seed\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Heat the oven to 350F. Line two baking sheets with parchment paper. Using the large holes of a grater, grate the cheese.\n2 Make the crisp mix: In a bowl, combine the flour, paprika, baking powder, and cayenne. Add the butter, and mix with a fork or your fingers until blended in. Stir in the seeds. Add the grated cheese and toss with your hands to combine.\n3 Form and bake the crisps: Mound tablespoon-size portions of the cheese mixture on the baking sheets, spaced 2 inches apart. Flatten them slightly with the back of the spoon.\nIt's not absolutely necessary, but you can also use a 2-inch round cookie cutter as a mold to keep the cheese tidy if you like. Place the cutter on the baking sheet and drop a spoonful of cheese mix into it. Lift the cutter, level the cheese, and repeat until you have made all the crisps.\n4 Bake for 9 to 12 minutes, or until golden. Let the crisps cool completely on the baking sheets. Lift the edge of the parchment to lift the crisps off the baking sheet, then peel them off. Store in an airtight container.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b'Save It Print\nSpinach Artichoke Dip with Bacon Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 20 minutesYield: 3 cups\nMy Italian cheese blend used mozzarella, Parmesan, Asiago, Provolone, and Romano cheeses, but any blend of Italian cheeses is fine.\nINGREDIENTS\n6 slices bacon (about 1/3 pound), chopped\n2 cloves garlic, minced\n1 14-ounce can artichoke hearts, drained and chopped\n1 10-ounce package frozen spinach, thawed, drained, and chopped, or 1 12-ounce bunch fresh spinach, finely chopped\n1/4 teaspoon crushed red pepper flakes\n1/2 teaspoon kosher salt (or slightly less table salt)\n1 8-ounce package cream cheese, at room temperature\n8 ounces shredded Italian cheese blend\n1/2 cup sour cream\nPita chips, tortilla chips, crackers, or celery sticks, for serving\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Preheat the oven to 400\xcb\x9aF.\n2 Cook the bacon: Place the chopped bacon in a skillet and cook over medium heat until crispy, 7 to 10 minutes. Transfer the bacon to a plate lined with paper towels to drain, leaving the rendered bacon fat in the skillet. Set some of the bacon aside for sprinkling over top the dip.\n3 Cook the vegetables: Add the garlic to the pan and cook until fragrant, about 30 seconds. Add the artichoke hearts, spinach, red pepper flakes, and salt. Cook, stirring occasionally, until artichokes are warmed through and the spinach has wilted, about 5 minutes.\n4 Combine with the cheeses: In a medium bowl, mix the cream cheese, shredded Italian cheese blend, sour cream, reserved bacon, and spinach-artichoke mixture until thoroughly combined.\n5 Bake and serve: Transfer the mixture to a 1- to 2-quart baking dish and bake until bubbling around the edges, about 20 minutes. Let cool slightly, then sprinkle with reserved bacon and serve with pita chips.\nThis dip is best eaten right away while hot. If it cools a bit and starts to firm up, microwave it for a minute or two to melt the cheese again.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'
b"Save It Print\nShrimp Quesadilla Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 10 minutesYield: Serves one\nIf you are starting with frozen raw shrimp, put them in a bowl of ice water to defrost.\nIf you are starting with cooked shrimp, just toss them with some salt, pepper, chipotle chile powder and lime juice and let them sit while you heat the tortillas.\nINGREDIENTS\n1/4 pound of medium-small raw shrimp, peeled and deveined\n1/4 teaspoon chipotle powder or chili powder\nPinch of salt\nPinch of pepper\n1 Tbsp of lime or lemon juice\n2 1/2 teaspoons extra virgin olive oil (divided, 2 teaspoons and 1/2 teaspoon)\n1 Tbsp chopped red onion\n1 Tbsp chopped fresh cilantro, plus more for garnish\nSalt and pepper\n2 medium-sized flour tortillas\n1/2 cup shredded Monterey Jack cheese\n1/4 avocado, sliced\nDollop of sour cream or crema fresca\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Marinate the shrimp: Toss the shrimp in a small bowl with 1/4 teaspoon of chipotle powder or chile powder, a pinch of salt, pinch of pepper, and a tablespoon of lime or lemon juice. Let sit for 10 minutes. Then drain out the juice.\n2 Cook the shrimp: Heat a couple teaspoons of olive oil in a relatively stick-free skillet (a cast iron skillet works well for this) on medium high heat.\nAdd the shrimp and cook for half a minute on each side, and remove to a bowl.\nThe shrimp shouldn't be completely cooked through; they will continue to cook during the next step.\n3 Heat the tortillas: Wipe out the skillet with paper towels. Add a small amount of olive oil (about 1/2 a teaspoon, you could use butter as well) and heat the pan on medium high.\nPlace one flour tortilla on the skillet. Flip the tortilla over a few times, 10 seconds between flips. Air pockets should begin to form within the tortilla.\nRemove the tortilla and repeat with the second tortilla. Leave the second tortilla in the pan and reduce the heat to medium.\n4 Build the quesadilla: Sprinkle the tortilla with the grated cheese. Distribute the shrimp on top of the cheese. Add chopped onion and cilantro. Place the other tortilla on top.\nFlip the quesadilla over when the bottom tortilla is nicely toasted and the cheese has begun to melt. Remove the quesadilla from the pan when the now bottom tortilla has toasted sufficiently.\nYou can also use just one tortilla instead of two, and fold the tortilla over itself like an omelette.\n5 Cut the quesadilla into triangles: Cut like a pie into six pieces (a pizza wheel works well for this). Place on a serving plate. Serve with avocado slices and sour cream. Garnish with chopped fresh cilantro. Squeeze a little lime juice over everything.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b"Save It Print\nArizona Cheese Crisp Recipe\nPrep time: 5 minutesCook time: 15 minutesYield: Makes one large Sonoran quesadilla\nIf you want to have green chiles on your quesadilla (they are optional), you can either roast your own (use Anaheims, Hatch, or Poblano) or use canned whole green chiles.\nTo roast your own, blacken them over a gas stove, on a grill, or under a broiler, then put the chiles in a covered bowl for a few minutes, then rub off the blackened skin.\n(See How to Roast Chiles over a Gas Flame video.) Then de-seed them and cut them into strips.\nINGREDIENTS\nOne large, burrito-size (13-inch diameter or larger) flour tortilla\n1 Tbsp butter\n1/2 cup of grated cheddar cheese\n1 or 2 roasted green chiles, peeled, seeded, cut into strips (optional)\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Preheat your oven to 350\xc2\xb0F with a rack in the middle.\n2 Butter a flour tortilla all the way to the edges: Place the flour tortilla on a large baking sheet (a dark baking sheet or cookie sheet will work best. Spread the butter all over the top of the tortilla, all the way to the edges. The butter is important for the flavor of a cheese crisp, so don't leave it out!\n3 Bake the tortilla until lightly toasted: Bake the plain buttered tortilla for about 6 minutes or until it begins to get lightly toasted. (Check on the timing for your particular oven.)\n4 Sprinkle with cheese, add green chile strips, return to oven: Remove the tortilla from the oven and sprinkle with the cheddar cheese, leaving about 1/2-inch from the edges. Add strips of green chiles in a star pattern if you want.\nReturn the tortilla to the oven and cook for 2 more minutes, or until all of the cheese has melted. Remove from oven and eat!\nMy mother will use her oven's convection setting when she makes these cheese crisps. For convection, she'll put the buttered tortilla into a cold oven and heat on convection at 375\xc2\xb0F for 7 to 10 minutes. Then she'll sprinkle the cheese and return the quesadilla to the oven for a couple more minutes.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b'Save It Print\nHoney Hazelnut Baked Brie Recipe\nPrep time: 5 minutesCook time: 20 minutesYield: Serves 6\nIf starting with raw hazelnuts, toast them by spreading them out on a sheet pan and roasting them in a 350\xc2\xb0F for 15 minutes, or until the skins start to split. Remove from oven and place in a clean dish towel, rub to remove the outer skins.\nINGREDIENTS\n1 (8-ounce, 225 g) round of brie (we recommend President brand, it melts well)\n1/4 cup toasted hazelnuts (skins removed), lightly chopped\n1/2 cup (120 ml) sherry vinegar or apple cider vinegar\n5 Tbsp honey\nPinch of salt\n1 small sprig rosemary\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Make the sauce: Place the vinegar, honey, salt, and 5 or 6 needles from the rosemary sprig into a small saucepan. Stir to combine. Heat on medium high heat until simmering. Then lower the heat to low and simmer until the mixture starts to darken in color and the consistency thickens to a thin syrup, about 5 to 10 minutes. (Note if you find that you have over-reduced the sauce, resulting in hard candy not syrup, you can add water to it and heat it again.)\nRemove from heat and stir in the hazelnuts.\n2 Bake the brie: While the sauce is simmering, start on the brie. Preheat the oven to 350\xc2\xb0F (175\xc2\xb0C). Use a serrated knife to slice off the very top of the brie round, exposing the cheese on one side. Place on a parchment paper or Silpat lined baking sheet (cut side up). Bake until just soft and bubbly, about 15 minutes. (Jiggle the pan to see if the cheese has melted all the way through.)\n3 Drizzle the brie with sauce: Remove the brie from the oven and let it cool for a minute or two. Use a metal spatula (or two) to carefully transfer it to a serving dish. Drizzle the honey vinegar hazelnut sauce over the brie. Garnish with the sprig of rosemary.\nServe with sliced tart apples.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'
b'Save It Print\nSpanish Roasted Potatoes with Tomato Sauce (Patatas Bravas) Recipe\nPrep time: 5 minutesCook time: 1 hourYield: Serves 4 as a side dish\nThis recipe makes more than enough sauce for the potatoes, so you can double the amount of potatoes for more servings, or save the extra sauce for later. It will keep a week in the refrigerator.\nINGREDIENTS\n2 pounds Yukon gold potatoes, or other waxy potato (peeled or un-peeled, your choice), cut into 1 to 1 1/2-inch chunks\nExtra virgin olive oil\nSalt\n1/2 medium yellow onion, chopped\n3 garlic cloves, chopped\n1/2 cup white wine (can substitute stock)\n2 tablespoons tomato paste\nA 14-ounce can of crushed tomatoes\n2 teaspoons Tabasco or other hot sauce\n1 teaspoon smoked paprika\n1 teaspoon salt\n1 teaspoon sugar\nMETHOD\n1 Roast the potatoes: Preheat oven to 375\xc2\xb0F. Toss the potatoes with 3 tablespoons of olive oil and salt well. Arrange in one layer in a casserole pan or rimmed baking tray and roast until browned, about 50 minutes.\n2 Saut\xc3\xa9 onions and garlic: While the potatoes are roasting, make the sauce. Heat 2 tablespoons of olive oil in a medium pot set over medium-high heat. Saut\xc3\xa9 the chopped onions, stirring occasionally, for 4-5 minutes, or until they begin to brown on the edges. Add the garlic and saut\xc3\xa9 another 2 minutes.\n3 Make the sauce: Add the white wine to the pan and turn the heat to high. Boil on a high boil until the wine is reduced by half, then add the tomato paste and stir to combine. Add the crushed tomatoes, Tabasco sauce, salt, sugar and smoked paprika. Stir well and reduce the heat to a bare simmer. Let the sauce cook slowly while the potatoes roast. If you want, you can use a blender or an immersion blender to pur\xc3\xa9e the sauce until smooth.\n4 Toss potatoes with sauce, continue to roast: When the potatoes are well browned, toss with the tomato sauce and return to the casserole pan. Continue to roast until the tomato sauce dries out a bit on the potatoes and caramelizes, about 10 minutes.\nServe with the remaining tomato sauce as an appetizer or side dish.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'
b'Save It Print\nHoney Mustard Chicken Wings Recipe\nPrep time: 7 minutesCook time: 30 minutesMarinating time: 1 hour to overnightYield: Makes 20 chicken wings\nRecipe adapted from Petaluma Poultry, providers of Rocky Range and Rocky Jr. chickens.\nINGREDIENTS\n8 cloves garlic, peeled and crushed\n2 tablespoons honey\n2 tablespoons Dijon mustard\n1 tablespoon tamari soy sauce (or 1 1/2 Tbsp regular soy sauce, use gluten-free soy sauce or tamari for gluten-free version)\n2 tablespoons lemon juice\n1/4 cup extra virgin olive oil\n2 teaspoons salt\n1 teaspoon freshly ground pepper\n20 chicken wing drummettes\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Marinate the chicken wings: Rinse and pat dry the chicken wings. Line a roasting pan with foil and place a baking rack over it.\nPlace the chicken wings in on the rack in a single layer with some space between the wings.\nBake for 25-35 minutes, depending on the size of the chicken wings, until cooked through and well browned.\n  Hello! b'Save It Print\nAngels on Horseback Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 20 minutesYield: Serves 4\nCanned shucked oysters can be found in the refrigerated section of the grocery store and work well in this recipe.\nINGREDIENTS\n16-32 small oysters (or scallops), or larger ones cut in half, shucked\n8-16 slices of thin-cut bacon\n16-32 wooden toothpicks\n3-4 limes or lemons\nMETHOD\n1 Pre-cook the bacon slices: Working in batches if necessary, cook the bacon slices on medium low heat in a large frying pan, until only about halfway cooked, but not crispy.\nYou need to pre-cook the bacon a bit or else when you cook them with the oysters the oysters will be overcooked by the time the bacon is crispy. Set the bacon aside to cool.\n2 Heat the grill: Get a grill or broiler good and hot while you wrap the oysters.\n3 Wrap bacon around oysters: To make an angel on horseback, you wrap 1/2 a piece of bacon around the small oyster and secure it with the toothpick. Overlap the edges of the bacon by about an inch if you can.\n4 Grill or broil: Grill or broil over high heat to cook the oyster and crisp the bacon, about 5-6 minutes on the first side, another 2-4 once you turn them over. You will need to turn them once or twice to get a good crispiness on all sides.\n5 Sprinkle with lemon or lime juice: As soon as they come off the heat, squirt with the lemon or lime juice and serve hot.\nHello! b"Save It Print\nSpicy Turkey and Zucchini Burger Recipe\nPrep time: 25 minutesCook time: 25 minutesYield: Serves 4-6\nRecipe adapted from the cookbook Jerusalem by Yotam Ottolenghi and Sami Tamimi.\nINGREDIENTS\n1 pound ground turkey meat\nJust under 2 cups, lightly packed, coarsely grated zucchini (from about 2 to 3 small zucchinis or one medium zucchini)\n3 green onions, thinly sliced, onion greens included\n2 tablespoons chopped fresh mint (spearmint)\n2 tablespoons chopped fresh cilantro (tender stems included)\n1 clove garlic, crushed and minced\n1 teaspoon ground cumin\n1 teaspoon Kosher salt\n1/2 teaspoon freshly ground black pepper\n1/2 teaspoon cayenne\n3 tablespoons extra virgin olive oil\nSour cream sauce:\n1/4 cup sour cream\n1/3 cup plain Greek yogurt\n1 teaspoon grated lemon zest\n1 tablespoon lemon juice\n1/2 teaspoon minced garlic\n2 teaspoons extra virgin olive oil\n1/4 teaspoon salt\nPinch of freshly ground black pepper\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Make the sour cream sauce by placing all of the sauce ingredients in a bowl and stirring until combined. Chill until ready to use.\n2 Mix the turkey zucchini mixture: In a large bowl place the grated zucchini, sliced green onions, chopped mint, cilantro, and garlic, ground cumin, salt, pepper, and cayenne. Stir to combine.\nWith your hands, mix in the ground turkey until the zucchini mixture is well distributed through the ground turkey.\n3 Form patties: Use your hands to form 3 to 4 inch wide patties, placing them on a baking sheet. Note that the patties will be rather wet, so they may be a little tricky to handle.\n4 Fry gently: Heat 3 Tbsp of olive oil in a large frying pan on medium high heat. Once the oil is hot, lower the heat to medium.\nWorking in batches, place the patties in the pan. Let cook for about 5 minutes, then flip the patties over and cook for another 5 to 6 minutes.\nYou want them to brown and to gently cook all the way through. If the temperature is too high, they'll get browned on the outside but the inside will still be raw. So, cook them gently.\nIf the outsides are browned and the insides still aren't done, lower the heat and cook longer.\n5 Remove to paper-towel lined plate: Once the first batch of patties are done, remove to a paper towel-lined plate while you cook the second batch. Or you can keep the patties warm in a 200\xc2\xb0F oven.\nMakes 8 large patties or up to 18 small ones. Serve with the sour cream sauce.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. b"Print\nGrilled Garlic Shrimp Skewers Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 10 minutesYield: Serves 4\nINGREDIENTS\n1 pound 16-20 count large prawns, peeled and deveined (can still have tail on for presentation)\nExtra virgin olive oil\nSalt\n3 tablespoons butter\n3 cloves garlic, minced\n1/4 teaspoon kosher salt\n1 teaspoon minced chives for garnish\nSpecial equipment:\nShort bamboo skewers, about 20, soaked for 30 minutes in water before grilling\nMETHOD\n1 Prepare grill: Prepare your grill for direct high heat, with one side of the grill as a cool side with no coals or flame.\n2 Thread shrimp on skewers: While the grill is heating, thread the pre-soaked skewers through the shrimp. Start at the tail and push the skewers through the middle and end of the shrimp. Brush shrimp with olive oil and sprinkle with salt.\n3 Melt butter with garlic: Place butter and garlic in a microwave-safe bowl and heat in microwave until the butter has melted and is hot. (If you don't have a microwave you can also just melt the butter with the garlic in a small saucepan on the stovetop.)\n4 Grill shrimp: Arrange skewers on grill so that the shrimp are over the coals or flame and the exposed bamboo skewer ends are over the cool side of the grill. Grill for about 2 minutes on each side.\n5 Serve basted with garlic butter: As soon as the shrimp are done, remove from grill and place in a serving dish. Baste generously with melted garlic butter. Sprinkle with chives to serve!\nServe immediately.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint"
b"Save It Print\nTempura Fried Calamari Recipe\nPrep time: 1 hour, 15 minutesCook time: 25 minutesYield: Serves 4-6 as an appetizer\nThe squid rings cut from the body are easier to fry than the tentacles, which tend to clump. If you have both, fry the rings first, then the tentacles.\nDo not double the recipe. The batter needs to be kept cold and used immediately after making. So it's better to work with small batches.\nIf you want to make more, mix a second batch together after you've gone through the first batch.\nINGREDIENTS\n1 pound cleaned squid\n1 egg yolk\n1 cup ice cold sparkling water (the colder the better)\n1/8 teaspoon baking soda\n1 teaspoon salt\n1/4 cup cornstarch\n3/4 cup rice or regular flour plus more for sprinkling on squid\nPeanut oil or canola oil for frying\nSpecial equipment:\nA deep fryer\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Slice the squid tubes into rings: Slice the squid tubes into rings about 1/2-inch to 3/4-inch wide. Leave the tentacles whole.\n2 Heat oil in a deep fryer or large heavy pot: This recipe was designed for a deep-fryer, but you can also fill a large, heavy-bottomed pot (keep a lid nearby, for safety reasons) halfway with oil, about 3 inches deep. Heat the oil to 360-370\xc2\xb0F.\n3 Mix dry ingredients: While the oil is heating, mix all the dry ingredients together well.\n4 Mix sparkling water with egg yolk, then mix with dry ingredients: Once the oil has reached 360\xc2\xb0F, take the sparkling water out of the refrigerator and mix it with the egg yolk. Immediately mix it in with the dry ingredients.\nMix quickly. Do not worry if there are clumps or lumps. Over-mixing may cause the batter to become chewy when cooked.\n5 Sprinkle squid pieces with flour. Use a small sieve to lightly dust the squid pieces with rice flour or regular flour. This will help the batter adhere to the squid.\n6 Dip squid pieces in batter and fry in hot oil: Working in small batches at a time (about 6 pieces), dip the squid pieces in the batter. Pick them up one by one and gently put them in the hot oil. (Note if your fingers are coated with the batter, it will help protect them from splatter.)\nWhen the squid pieces are in the oil, use a chopstick or the handle of a wooden spoon to dislodge any squid pieces that may have become stuck from the bottom of the pot or fryer. Fry for 45 seconds to 1 minute, and remove to paper towels to drain.\nNote that when done, they will NOT be golden brown, but more of a pale yellow or tan.\nRepeat with the rest of the squid. Working in batches will help keep the oil temperature from falling too far while you are frying the squid.\n6 Serve immediately: Serve immediately with lime or lemon wedges, soy sauce, ponzu sauce, Tabasco or another hot sauce.\nOnce the cooking oil has completely cooled (after about 2 hours), strain it through a paper towel-lined sieve, and save it to reuse the next time you want to deep fry seafood.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b"Save It Print\nShrimp Quesadilla Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 10 minutesYield: Serves one\nIf you are starting with frozen raw shrimp, put them in a bowl of ice water to defrost.\nIf you are starting with cooked shrimp, just toss them with some salt, pepper, chipotle chile powder and lime juice and let them sit while you heat the tortillas.\nINGREDIENTS\n1/4 pound of medium-small raw shrimp, peeled and deveined\n1/4 teaspoon chipotle powder or chili powder\nPinch of salt\nPinch of pepper\n1 Tbsp of lime or lemon juice\n2 1/2 teaspoons extra virgin olive oil (divided, 2 teaspoons and 1/2 teaspoon)\n1 Tbsp chopped red onion\n1 Tbsp chopped fresh cilantro, plus more for garnish\nSalt and pepper\n2 medium-sized flour tortillas\n1/2 cup shredded Monterey Jack cheese\n1/4 avocado, sliced\nDollop of sour cream or crema fresca\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Marinate the shrimp: Toss the shrimp in a small bowl with 1/4 teaspoon of chipotle powder or chile powder, a pinch of salt, pinch of pepper, and a tablespoon of lime or lemon juice. Let sit for 10 minutes. Then drain out the juice.\n2 Cook the shrimp: Heat a couple teaspoons of olive oil in a relatively stick-free skillet (a cast iron skillet works well for this) on medium high heat.\nAdd the shrimp and cook for half a minute on each side, and remove to a bowl.\nThe shrimp shouldn't be completely cooked through; they will continue to cook during the next step.\n3 Heat the tortillas: Wipe out the skillet with paper towels. Add a small amount of olive oil (about 1/2 a teaspoon, you could use butter as well) and heat the pan on medium high.\nPlace one flour tortilla on the skillet. Flip the tortilla over a few times, 10 seconds between flips. Air pockets should begin to form within the tortilla.\nRemove the tortilla and repeat with the second tortilla. Leave the second tortilla in the pan and reduce the heat to medium.\n4 Build the quesadilla: Sprinkle the tortilla with the grated cheese. Distribute the shrimp on top of the cheese. Add chopped onion and cilantro. Place the other tortilla on top.\nFlip the quesadilla over when the bottom tortilla is nicely toasted and the cheese has begun to melt. Remove the quesadilla from the pan when the now bottom tortilla has toasted sufficiently.\nYou can also use just one tortilla instead of two, and fold the tortilla over itself like an omelette.\n5 Cut the quesadilla into triangles: Cut like a pie into six pieces (a pizza wheel works well for this). Place on a serving plate. Serve with avocado slices and sour cream. Garnish with chopped fresh cilantro. Squeeze a little lime juice over everything.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"

Spread the butter all over the top of the tortilla, all the way to the edges. The butter is important for the flavor of a cheese crisp, so don't leave it out!\n3 Bake the tortilla until lightly toasted: Bake the plain buttered tortilla for about 6 minutes or until it begins to get lightly toasted. (Check on the timing for your particular oven.)\n4 Sprinkle with cheese, add green chile strips, return to oven: Remove the tortilla from the oven and sprinkle with the cheddar cheese, leaving about 1/2-inch from the edges. Add strips of green chiles in a star pattern if you want.\nReturn the tortilla to the oven and cook for 2 more minutes, or until all of the cheese has melted. Remove from oven and eat!\nMy mother will use her oven's convection setting when she makes these cheese crisps. For convection, she'll put the buttered tortilla into a cold oven and heat on convection at 375\xc2\xb0F for 7 to 10 minutes. Then she'll sprinkle the cheese and return the quesadilla to the oven for a couple more minutes.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. b"Save It Print\n7 Layer Bean Dip Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 10 minutesYield: Serves 8\nINGREDIENTS\n2 cups refried beans, from one 15-ounce can or homemade\n1 teaspoon (or more) of bacon fat (or 1 strip of bacon, cooked and minced), optional\n1 teaspoon chipotle powder, Tabasco chipotle sauce, or adobo sauce, more to taste (or plain chili powder to taste)\n1/4 to 1/2 teaspoon ground cumin\nSalt\n1 cup shredded cheddar or Monterey Jack cheese\n1/4 cup chopped green Anaheim chiles (canned) OR 1 tablespoon chopped pickled jalape\xc3\xb1os (more to taste)\n1 avocado, peeled and chopped\n1 hot house tomato, cut in half horizontally, seeds and juice gently squeezed out and discarded, chopped\n1/3 cup sour cream, or if you can get it Crema Mexicana (Mexican sour cream)\n1 cup sliced ripe black olives, from a 15-ounce can\nCorn tortilla chips, to serve\nMETHOD\n1 Prepare the refried beans: Heat the refried beans in a medium saut\xc3\xa9 pan or cast iron skillet. Stir in enough water to get a creamy, easily dip-able consistency, about 1/4 of a cup.\nThe taste of refried beans is greatly enhanced by bacon fat; we'll add a teaspoon to canned beans or a tablespoon or more to taste if we are making the beans from scratch.\nIf you don't have bacon fat, you can cook up a strip of bacon, chop it up fine and add that to the beans.\nIf you are trying to avoid pork, note that most canned refried beans are made with added lard, so check the ingredients. You can use olive oil instead, to help the consistency of the beans.\nMix in the chipotle chili powder (or Tabasco, or adobo, or regular chili powder) and cumin to taste. Note that the avocados and the sour cream will cool down the spiciness of the beans considerably, so you can afford to be a bit more spicy than you might think.\nStir in salt to taste, depending on how salted your refried beans are to begin with, and depending on how salty the tortilla chips are that you are serving with the dip.\n2 Spread on serving dish, top with cheese: Once the beans are hot and bubbly, spread them over the bottom of a warmed serving dish. Immediately add the shredded cheese so that the heat from the beans helps melt the cheese.\n(The cheese doesn't need to be completely melted, but even if it is just a little, it will help the dip stay on the chip.)\n3 Layer on toppings: Layer on the chopped green chilies, chopped avocado, chopped tomato. Spoon on the sour cream (or crema Mexicana, crema fresca, or even cream fraiche).\nTop with sliced green onions and olives.\nServe immediately with tortilla chips.\nHello! b"Save It Print\nScallion Pancakes Recipe\nPrep time: 25 minutesCook time: 25 minutesResting time: 30 minutesYield: 4 to 6 servings (4 pancakes)\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the scallion pancakes:\n2 cups all-purpose flour\n1 teaspoon salt\n1/2 teaspoon garlic powder, optional\n3/4 cup hot (just boiling) water, plus a few more tablespoons, if necessary\n1/4 cup canola oil\n3 to 4 scallions, thinly sliced\nFor the dipping sauce:\n2 tablespoons soy sauce\n2 1/2 tablespoons rice vinegar\n1/2 teaspoon toasted sesame oil\nMETHOD\n1 Mix the dough: Add flour, salt and garlic granules to a medium bowl. Stir to combine. Add 3/4 cups of hot water to the flour and stir with a wooden spoon. Continue stirring until all the water has been absorbed by the flour. Don\xe2\x80\x99t worry if the dough has not formed completely yet.\n2 Knead the dough: Using your hands, knead all the bits of dough together inside the bowl. If your dough is still very dry, add a splash of hot water, about 1 to 2 tablespoons, until it comes together and all the flour is absorbed.\nContinue kneading the dough for about 2 more minutes. The dough will feel moist but it should not stick to your hands too much.\n3 Rest the dough: Shape the dough into a round ball. Cover the bowl with plastic wrap and let the dough rest for 30 minutes.\n4 Roll out the pancakes: Sprinkle flour on top of a work surface. Divide the dough into 4 pieces of equal size. Work with one piece at a time, leaving the remaining pieces in the bowl.\nShape piece of dough into a small ball. Use a rolling pin to roll out the dough into a thin circle, about 7 to 8 inches in diameter.\n5 Add the scallions: Brush a thin layer of canola oil on top of the dough, making sure not to miss the edges. Sprinkle sliced scallions all over the dough.\n6 Roll and flatten the pancake: Starting on one end, roll the circle of dough into a log. Take one end of the rolled up dough and curl it toward the center, like a snail's shell. Tuck the end of the dough underneath the spiral.\nUse the palm of your hand to flatten the dough into a thick circle. Roll it out again with your rolling pin. Try to roll it out as thinly as possible. A few slices of scallions may pop out during the process, and that\xe2\x80\x99s perfectly normal.\nTransfer rolled out scallion pancake to a plate. Repeat steps 4 through 6 with the remaining dough pieces.\n7 Cook the pancakes: Heat about 2 teaspoons of canola oil a small nonstick or cast iron skillet over medium heat.\nPlace one of the pancakes in the middle of the pan and pan fry each side for about 2 to 3 minutes, until they\xe2\x80\x99re golden brown. Transfer to a plate and repeat with the 3 remaining scallion pancakes, adding more oil to the pan as needed.\n8 Prepare the dipping sauce: Mix all the sauce ingredients in a small bowl. Adjust the seasonings to your liking, adding more soy sauce or vinegar, if you like. Add any leftover scallions to the dipping sauce, and add a pinch of red pepper flakes if you would like a bit of spice.\n9 Serve the hot pancakes: Cut the scallion pancakes into small wedges and serve while hot, with the dipping sauce. (The pancakes are still good when cooled, but will no longer be crispy.)\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"

b'Save It Print\nCranberry Apple Stuffed Pork Loin Recipe\nPrep time: 25 minutesCook time: 1 hourYield: Serves 6 to 8\nChilling the pork roast before cutting will make the roast easier to cut.\nINGREDIENTS\n1 boneless pork loin (about 3 to 4 pounds)\nSea salt and freshly ground pepper\n1/2 cup panko or homemade breadcrumbs\n1/2 cup chicken stock\n1 cup peeled, chopped tart green apples\n1/3 cup dried cranberries\n1/3 cup chopped walnuts, toasted\n1/4 cup minced shallots\n2 Tbsp pure maple syrup\n1 teaspoon minced rosemary\nSpecial equipment:\nKitchen string\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Preheat oven to 450\xc2\xb0F.\n2 How to butterfly the pork loin: Place the pork loin roast fat side down on a cutting board. Note that one long side of the pork loin roast will be thicker, and one side thinner.\nUsing a sharp knife, make a long cut an inch or so from the edge from the thinner long side of the roast at about a 45\xc2\xb0 degree angle, stopping a half inch from reaching the bottom of the roast.\nThen angle the knife so that it is flat, parallel to the cutting board, and make slow, shallow cuts into the roast, along the same line.\nAs you cut, you can open up the top part of the roast like a book. Keep making slow, even cuts until you have "rolled" the roast out completely.\n3 Pound the butterflied roast to an even thickness: With the pork roast unfolded, cover with 2 layers of of plastic wrap.\nPound with a meat mallet to flatten to a somewhat even thickness. Remove plastic wrap. Sprinkle the pork with salt and pepper and set aside.\n4 Make the filling: Place the panko and stock in a small bowl and stir to combine.\nStir in the apples, walnuts, cranberries, shallots, maple syrup and rosemary.\n5 Roll up pork roast with filling: Spread the filling over surface of the pork, leaving an inch margin around all sides except for the fat layer side\xe2\x80\x94with that side leave a 2-inch margin.\nStarting with the end of the roast rectangle that does not have the fat layer on the bottom, roll up the roast.\n6 Secure with kitchen string. Tie the roast in 1 to 2 inch intervals with cotton kitchen string.\nAt this point you can wrap in plastic wrap and refrigerate if you are making ahead.\n7 Bake: Coat the bottom of a roasting pan with cooking spray or a little olive oil. Place the roast in the pan and cook at 450\xc2\xb0F for 15 minutes to brown the top, then reduce the oven temperature to 325\xc2\xb0F. Cook uncovered, for about 30 to 40 minutes, or until the pork reaches an internal temperature of 140\xc2\xb0F.\n8 Rest and serve: Tent the roast with foil and let it rest for 10 minutes. Remove the kitchen string and slice into 1/2-inch thick slices to serve.\nSave the pan drippings! Serve with pan drippings or use the pan drippings to make gravy. See How to Make Gravy.\nHello!
