b"Save It Print\nHomemade Apple Pie Recipe\nPrep time: 1 hour, 15 minutesCook time: 55 minutesYield: Serves 8\nIf the crust looks like it's getting too browned, take a large piece of aluminum foil and place on top of the pie in the oven. No need to wrap it around the pie, just place it on top. That will keep the top from browning further.\nPies always seem to take longer to cook than one expects. (Perhaps it's because we're always opening the oven to check on how the pie is doing?) The filling should be visibly bubbling, which you should be able to see through the steam vents.\nI recommend putting a rimmed baking sheet on a rack beneath the rack of the pie to catch the filling as some of it invariably bubbles up and out over the pie. Makes oven clean-up a lot easier.\nINGREDIENTS\n3 pounds good cooking apples such as Granny Smith, Jonagold, Golden Delicious, Fuji, or Braeburn (about 6 to 8 apples, depending on the size of your apples and the size of your pie dish)\n1 tablespoon lemon juice or apple cider vinegar (to toss with the sliced apples so they don't brown as you slice them)\n1/2 cup to 2/3 cup sugar, depending on how sweet you like your pie\n3 tablespoons all-purpose flour for thickening\n1/2 teaspoon cinnamon\n1/4 teaspoon ground allspice\n1/4 teaspoon ground nutmeg\n1 tablespoon brandy (Optional. By the way, if you have Calvados apple brandy, use it!)\n1 teaspoon vanilla extract\n1 recipe double crust sour cream pie dough, OR all-butter crust, OR your favorite pie crust recipe\nFor the egg wash:\n1 large egg yolk\n1 tablespoon cream\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Peel, core, and slice the apples: Peel, core and slice or roughly chop the apples into 1/4-inch to 1/2-inch slices or chunks.\nAs you cut your apple slices, add them to a large bowl and sprinkle them with a little lemon juice or apple cider vinegar to help keep them from turning brown.\n2 Make the apple pie filling: Combine sugar, flour and spices (allspice, nutmeg, cinnamon) in a bowl. Add the flour mixture to the apple slices and use your hands to distribute the flour through the apples so they are well coated.\nThen sprinkle with brandy and vanilla extract and stir to coat all the apples.\n3 Prepare oven: Place one oven rack in the lowest position and put a large rimmed baking sheet on it (to catch any drippings from the pie.) Position a second rack the next rung up (still in the lower third of the oven) and preheat to 375\xc2\xb0F.\n4 Roll out the dough and line bottom pie plate: Remove one disk of pie dough from the refrigerator. Let sit at room temperature for 5-10 minutes. Place disk on a lightly floured, clean, flat surface. Using a rolling pin, roll out the pie dough to a 12-inch circle, about 1/8 of an inch thick.\nAs you roll out the dough, check to make sure it isn't sticking. If and when it starts to stick, gently lift it up and sprinkle a little more flour on the table surface or on the pie dough to keep the dough from sticking.\nGently place the rolled out dough onto a 9-inch pie plate. Press down to line the pie dish with the dough.\n5 Place apple slices on top of the bottom crust: Arrange the apple slices in the dough-lined pie plate. Mound the apples in the center.\n6 Roll out top crust, place over apples, trim and crimp edges: Roll out the second disk of dough, again to 12-inches. Gently place the second round of pie dough over the apples. Trim excess dough with kitchen shears, leaving a 3/4 inch overhang from the edges of the pie pan.\nFold the dough under itself so that the edge of the fold comes right to the edge of the pan. Press the top and bottom dough rounds together as you flute edges using thumb and forefinger or press with a fork.\n7 Brush with egg wash, cut vents: Place egg yolk and cream in a small bowl and use a fork to stir until well combined. Use a pastry brush to brush the egg wash over the top and fluted edges of the pie. Use a sharp knife to cut slits in the top of the pie crust for steam vents.\n8 Bake: Place pie on oven rack centered over the baking sheet on the rack below it to catch any drippings. Bake the pie at 375\xc2\xb0F until crust begins to lightly brown, about 20 minutes, then reduce heat to 350\xc2\xb0F.\nBake until crust is golden and juices are bubbling, anywhere from an additional 45 minutes to an hour, depending on the type of apples you are using. (About halfway through baking check to make sure the pie isn't browning too much. When it's nicely browned, tent the pie with a large piece of aluminum foil to keep the pie from browning further.)\n9 Let cool: Transfer the apple pie to a rack to cool for at least 1 hour. Serve slightly warm or at room temperature. Great with a side of vanilla ice cream.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b'Print\nMile High Deep Dish Apple Pie Recipe\nPrep time: 25 minutesCook time: 1 hour, 30 minutesMaking homemade crust time: 2 hoursYield: Serves 6 to 8\nINGREDIENTS\nCrust\n2 cups all-purpose flour, plus extra for rolling\n1/2 cup almond flour or finely ground blanched almonds\n16 tablespoons (2 sticks) unsalted butter, very-cold, cut into 1/2 inch cubes\n1 teaspoon salt\n1 heaping teaspoon brown sugar\n3 to 6 tablespoons nonfat milk, very cold\n1 tablespoon heavy cream\n1 large egg yolk\nFilling\n1/2 cup sugar (white granulated)\n1/4 cup packed light brown sugar\n1/4 teaspoon salt\n1 teaspoon ground cinnamon\n1/4 teaspoon ground ginger\n5 pounds of mixed apples (Granny Smith, Golden Delicious, Fuji, Jonagold, Pippin, Braeburn, Cortland, McIntosh), peeled and cut into 1/4 inch slices\n1 tablespoon of lemon juice and 1/2 teaspoon of grated lemon zest\n2 tablespoons unsalted butter\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Make the pie dough for the crust: In a food processor, combine flour, almonds, salt and brown sugar, pulse to mix.\nAdd butter and pulse 6 to 8 times, until mixture resembles coarse meal.\nAdd milk 1 Tablespoon at a time, pulsing until mixture begins to clump together. Remove dough from machine and shape into 2 discs. Wrap each in plastic wrap and refrigerate at least 1 hour.\n2 Cook the apples: While the pie dough is chilling, start cooking the apples. Mix 1/2 cup white sugar and 1/4 cup brown sugar, salt, ground ginger, and cinnamon into a large mixing bowl. Add the apples and lemon zest and toss to combine.\nTransfer apples to a large, thick-bottomed covered pan or Dutch oven and cook, covered, over medium heat, stirring frequently, until apples are just tender when poked with a fork, but still hold their shape - about 15 to 20 minutes (but not so long for the apples to turn into applesauce.\nPut apples in a colander over a bowl to drain excess liquid. Drain off as much juice as possible.\nSpread out on a sheet pan to cool for 5 to 10 minutes.\n3 Preheat oven to 425\xc2\xb0F with a baking sheet on a rack on the lowest rung of the oven.\n4 Roll out the bottom crust: While the apples are cooling and draining, remove one crust disk from the refrigerator. Let sit at room temperature for 5-10 minutes. Sprinkle some flour on top of the disk.\nRoll out with a rolling pin on a lightly floured surface to a 12 inch circle; about 1/8 of an inch thick. As you roll out the dough, use a metal spatula to check if the dough is sticking to the surface below. Add a few sprinkles of flour if necessary to keep the dough from sticking. Gently fold in half.\nPlace on to a 9-inch pie plate, lining up the fold with the center of the pan. Gently unfold and press down to line the pie dish with the dough.\n5 Add the filling: Add the apple filling to the dough-lined pie pan. Sprinkle with 1 tablespoon of lemon juice. Dot with butter.\n6 Roll out top crust, place over apples, trim and crimp edges: Roll out second disk of dough, as before. Gently turn over onto the top of the apples in the pie. Pinch top and bottom of dough rounds firmly together. Trim excess dough with kitchen shears, leaving a 3/4 inch overhang.\nFold the dough under itself so that the edge of the fold is flush with the edge of the pan. Flute edges using thumb and forefinger or press with a fork.\n7 Score the top, brush with egg wash: Score the top of the pie with four 2-inch long cuts, so that steam from the cooking pie can escape. Beat egg yolk with cream and brush on the surface of the pie with a pastry brush.\n7 Bake: Set pie on preheated baking sheet (to catch any juices that may escape from the pie while cooking). Bake at 425\xc2\xb0F for 15 minutes. Lower the heat to 375\xc2\xb0F and cook for an additional 50 to 60 minutes or more, until filling bubbles in the center and crust turns golden brown.\n8 Cool: Cool on a wire rack for 1 1/2 hours. Cut into wedges and serve with vanilla ice cream.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'
b"Save It Print\nApple Cranberry Pie Recipe\nPrep time: 1 hour, 30 minutesCook time: 1 hour, 30 minutesYield: Serves 8\nAs you peel, core, and slice the apples, put the apple slices in a bowl and sprinkle with a little lemon juice or apple cider vinegar to prevent them from discoloring.\nThe crust recipe given includes ground almonds which give the crust a lovely flavor that works well with the apples and cranberries. You can also use our favorite sour cream pie crust that is easy to put together and makes an especially flaky crust.\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the crust:\n2 cups all-purpose flour, plus extra for rolling\n1/3 cup finely ground blanched almonds or almond flour\n16 tablespoons (2 sticks) unsalted butter, very-cold, cut into 1/2 inch cubes\n1 teaspoon salt\n1 heaping teaspoon brown sugar\n3 to 6 tablespoons ice water\nFor the filling:\n1 cup dried sweetened cranberries\n1/2 to 2/3 cup sugar (depending on how sweet you want the filling to be)\n2 tablespoons all purpose flour\n1/4 teaspoon ground allspice or cinnamon\n2 1/4 pounds of an assortment of good cooking apples such as Granny Smith, Pippin, Golden Delicious, peeled, cored, and sliced into 1/4-inch thick slices (about 7 cups of apple slices)\n1 tablespoon brandy\n1 teaspoon vanilla extract\nFor the egg wash:\n1 large egg yolk\n1 tablespoon whipping cream\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Make the pie dough: In a food processor, combine flour, almond flour, salt and brown sugar, pulse to mix. Add butter and pulse 6 to 8 times, until mixture resembles coarse meal, with pea size pieces of butter. Add water 1 Tablespoon at a time, pulsing until mixture just begins to clump together. If you pinch some of the crumbly dough and it holds together, it's ready, if not, add a little more ice water and pulse again.\nRemove dough from machine and place on a clean surface. Carefully shape into 2 discs. Do not over-knead the dough! You should still be able to see little bits of butter in the dough. These bits of butter are what will allow the result crust to be flaky. Wrap each disc in plastic wrap and refrigerate at least 1 hour.\n2 Preheat oven to 375\xc2\xb0F with a rack in the bottom third of the oven.\n3 Make the apple filling: Whisk together the sugar, flour, and allspice or cinnamon in a large bowl. Add the dried sweetened cranberries and toss to coat with the sugar flour mixture. Add the apples and toss to coat and make sure that the cranberries are well distributed throughout the apples. Sprinkle with the brandy and vanilla extract.\n4 Roll out the bottom crust: Remove one crust disk from the refrigerator. Let sit at room temperature for 5-10 minutes. Sprinkle some flour on top of the disk. Roll out with a rolling pin on a lightly floured surface to a 12 inch circle; about 1/8 of an inch thick.\nAs you roll out the dough, use a metal spatula to check if the dough is sticking to the surface below. Add a few sprinkles of flour if necessary to keep the dough from sticking. Place on a 9-inch pyrex pie dish. Press down to line the pie dish with the dough.\n5 Place the apple cranberry filling in the pie dish.\n6 Roll out top crust, top the pie, crimp edges: Roll out second disk of dough, as before. Gently place on top of the apples in the pie. Pinch top and bottom of dough rounds firmly together. Trim excess dough with kitchen shears, leaving a 3/4 inch overhang.\nFold dough under itself so that the edge of the fold is flush with the edge of the pan. Flute edges using thumb and forefinger or press with a fork.\n7 Brush pie with egg wash: In a small bowl whisk together the egg yolk and cream until well blended. Use a pastry brush to brush over the top of the pie. Use a sharp knife to cut slits in the top crust to allow steam to escape as the pie bakes.\n8 Bake: Bake the pie at 375\xc2\xb0F for 30 minutes. Then place a sheet of aluminum foil over the pie and lower the oven temp to 350\xc2\xb0F. Bake for another 45 to 55 minutes or longer, depending on the type of apples you are using.\nWhen done the crust should be golden brown and the apples soft and cooked through. Remove the pie and let cool on a rack for at least one hour. Serve pie warm or at room temperature.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b'Save It Print\nSour Cream Apple Pie Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 50 minutesYield: Serves 8\nAs you slice the apples, put them in a bowl and toss them with a little lemon juice or apple cider vinegar. The acidity of the lemon juice or vinegar will help keep the apples from discoloring while you work and will intensify the apple flavor in the pie.\nINGREDIENTS\nFilling:\n1 cup sour cream\n2/3 cup sugar (can easily reduce to 1/2 cup if you like your apple pies a little less sweet)\n2 Tablespoons flour\n1/4 teaspoon salt\n1 teaspoon vanilla\n1 egg\n3 cups peeled, sliced tart apples (about 1 1/4 pounds of slices, cut 1/4-inch to a 1/2-inch thick)\n1 Tablespoon lemon juice or apple cider vinegar\nOne 9" unbaked pie shell, frozen or chilled in the freezer for at least 30 minutes (see sour cream pie crust recipe, use a single crust recipe)\nTopping:\n1/2 cup brown sugar, packed\n1/2 cup flour\n1/4 cup butter (1/2 a stick), chilled, cut into cubes\n1/2 teaspoon cinnamon\nMix together all ingredients until the mixture resembles coarse crumbs. Chill until needed in the recipe.\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Make the streusel topping: Place the streusel topping ingredients in a medium bowl and mix with a fork or your hands until the mixture resembles coarse crumbs.\nChill in the refrigerator until the topping is needed half-way through the baking.\n2 Preheat oven to 400\xc2\xb0F with a rack in the middle and another rack below it. Place a large rimmed baking sheet on the lower rack to catch any of the drippings from the pie.\n3 Mix sour cream with sugar, flour, salt, vanilla, egg, and coat apple slices with it: In a large bowl put the sour cream, sugar, flour, salt, vanilla, and egg. You may also want to put a pie protector or foil around the outer crust edges to keep them from getting too browned. b'Save It Print\nGrain-Free Apple Honey Cake Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 30 minutesCooling time: 45 minutesYield: 8 to 10 servings\nThis cake can be made up to a day ahead. Or, if you\xe2\x80\x99re in a big hurry to serve it, you can serve the cake warm, too.\nFor a more rustic cake, use almond meal instead of almond flour, and leave the apple unpeeled.\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the cake:\n1 1/2 cups (6 ounces) almond flour\n1 teaspoon ground cinnamon\n1/4 teaspoon ground nutmeg\n3/4 teaspoon salt\n3 large eggs\n1/4 cup honey\n2 tablespoons neutral-tasting oil (I use avocado oil)\n1 medium (7-ounce) Granny Smith apple, peeled and cut into thin matchsticks, or grated coarsely\nFor the glaze and topping:\n1/2 cup powdered sugar\n2 tablespoons honey\n1 tablespoon almond milk or water\n1/4 cup sliced almonds\nSpecial equipment:\n8-inch cake pan\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Preheat the oven and prepare a cake pan: Preheat the oven to 325\xc2\xbaF. Grease an 8-inch cake pan and place a round of parchment in the bottom of the pan.\n2 Make the cake batter: In a medium mixing bowl, whisk together the almond flour, cinnamon, nutmeg, and salt. Make a well in the center of the flour, then add in the eggs, honey, and oil. Whisk wet ingredients together in the middle, then gradually whisk in the flour from the sides of the bowl. Continue whisking until the batter is smooth. Stir in the julienned or grated apple.\n3 Pour the batter into the pan and bake the cake: Pour the batter into the cake pan, taking care not to move the parchment around. Spread out the batter in an even layer using an offset spatula or butter knife, then tap the cake pan against the countertop to remove any air bubbles.\n4 Bake the cake: Bake the cake for 30 minutes, until it is browned around the edges and a toothpick inserted in the middle comes out clean. You may also use a probe thermometer to test for doneness\xe2\x80\x94the center of the cake should be 210\xc2\xbaF.\n5 While the cake is baking, make the glaze and toast the almonds: In a small bowl, stir together the sugar, honey, and almond milk. Cover the bowl and set it aside until needed.\nToast the sliced almonds in a skillet over medium heat until they are lightly browned, about five minutes. Shake the pan often so that the almonds are browned evenly. When they are done, immediately transfer to bowl to cool.\n6 Transfer the cake to a cooling rack: Allow the finished cake rest for 5 minutes, then run a knife around the edge of the pan to and invert the cake to a cooling rack. Peel the parchment off the bottom of the cake and flip it right side up.\n7 While the cake is still warm, pour the glaze over the top. Spread the glaze so that it drips over the edges of the cake. While the glaze is still wet, sprinkle the almonds on top.\n8 Let the cake cool to room temperature and serve. The cake can also be made and glazed up to a day ahead.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'

b"Save It Print\nSlow Cooker Cider Pulled Pork Recipe\nPrep time: 30 minutesCook time: 25 minutesSlow cooker time: 8 hoursYield: 10 to 12 servings\nThe meat will release liquid as it cooks. A 6-quart slow cooker for 6 pounds of meat works well. If you want to double the recipe, it's best to borrow a neighbor's slow cooker so you can have two going at once.\nIf you\xe2\x80\x99d like, the pork can be served as soon as it finishes slow-cooking. Remove the pork from the liquid and transfer the liquid to a measuring cup. Shred the pork and then keep it warm in the slow cooker or on a covered baking sheet in a low oven. Use 2 cups of the cooking liquid to make the sauce. Serve immediately.\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the rub:\n2 1/2 tablespoons brown sugar, packed\n2 1/2 tablespoons Kosher salt\n1 1/2 teaspoons pumpkin pie spice (or 1 teaspoon cinnamon, 1/4 teaspoon ground ginger, 1/4 teaspoon ground cloves, and a dash of nutmeg)\n1 1/2 teaspoons chili powder\n1 1/2 teaspoons freshly ground black pepper\n1 teaspoon ground dry mustard\n1/4 teaspoon cayenne pepper\nFor the pork:\n6 pound boneless pork shoulder, trimmed of excess fat\n1 (12-ounce) bottle hard apple cider\n2 cups apple cider\nFor the sauce:\n2 tablespoons tomato paste\n3 garlic cloves\n3/4 cup ketchup\n1/2 cup brown mustard\n1/3 cup brown sugar\n1/4 cup apple cider vinegar\n1/4 cup Worcestershire sauce\n2 teaspoons liquid smoke\n3/4 teaspoon Kosher salt\n2 cups pork stock leftover from braising\nSpecial equipment:\n6-quart slow cooker\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Make the rub and prep the pork: In a small bowl, combine all of the ingredients for the rub. Trim your pork shoulder of excess exterior fat. Massage the rub into the meat.\n2 Slow cook the pork: Place the pork in a 6-quart slow cooker. Pour in both ciders. The liquid should come about 3/4 of the way up the side of the meat; the meat should not be completely submerged.\nCover with the lid, and set slow cooker to low heat for at least 8 hours.\n3 Cool the pork and refrigerate overnight: Let the pork with the cooking liquid cool completely while still in the slow cooker insert on the counter. Transfer the pork to a cutting board and pour the cooking liquid into a separate storage container.\nTransfer the pork back to the slow cooker insert and cover. Refrigerate the pork and the cooking liquid overnight or up to three days. (Refrigerating the pork whole, rather than shredded, helps keep it moist and prevents it from drying out too much until you're ready to serve.)\n4 Shred the pork: When ready to serve the pork, remove it and the cooking liquid from the refrigerator. Scrape any solidified fat from the outside of the pork and the surface of the cooking liquid.\nUsing your fingers or two forks, shred the pork. You can do this right in the slow cooker, on a sheet pan, or on a cutting board. Pick out and discard any large pieces of fat as you go.\n5 Warm the pork: Warm the shredded pork in the slow cooker on the Low or Warm setting while you prepare the sauce. If the pork seems dry at any point, stir in a few tablespoons of the leftover cooking liquid.\nAlternatively, you can warm the pork on a sheet pan covered with foil in a low oven.\n6 Make the sauce: Measure out two cups of the leftover cooking liquid. The remainder can be strained and saved for another purpose, or frozen for up to three months.\nIn a medium saucepan over medium heat, add the tomato paste and garlic. Whisk together and cook for about 1 minute until fragrant. Whisk in the remaining ingredients, finishing with the reserved 2 cups of cooking liquid.\nIncrease heat to medium high and bring to a gentle boil. Reduce the sauce, whisking occasionally until it has the viscosity of thick tomato soup, but not as thick as ketchup, about 15 minutes. Taste and adjust the seasoning as you wish.\n7 Serve the pork: Reserve about 1/2 cup of sauce to serve in a small bowl alongside the pork. Pour the rest of the sauce over the pork, toss to combine, and serve it to the masses.\nPlace a pile of pork on top of buttered, toasted buns, top with pickles, pickled onions, or extra sauce, and dig in.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b'Save It Print\nApple Cider Glazed Donut Holes Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 25 minutesYield: 30 donut holes\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the donut holes:\n2 cups (255g) all-purpose flour\n1 1/2 teaspoons baking powder\n3/4 teaspoon kosher salt\n1/2 cup (100g) sugar\n1 large egg\n3/4 cup (6oz/170g) sour cream\n1/2 cup apple cider\n2 tablespoons unsalted butter, melted\n1 1/2 quarts canola oil for frying\nFor the apple cider glaze:\n2 cups powdered sugar\n4 tablespoons apple cider\nPinch of kosher salt\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Prepare your drying station: Set a wire cooling rack over a baking sheet. Add chicken thighs skin-side down to a large, cold cast iron skillet. Place the skillet over medium heat and let the thighs cook, untouched, for 15 minutes, until the skin is deeply golden and crispy.\n3 Add the remaining ingredients: After the chicken thighs have cooked for 15 minutes, carefully flip them. Add the sweet potatoes, onion, apple cider, chicken stock, and fresh rosemary to the skillet. Stir gently to make sure ingredients are distributed evenly. The thighs should only be submerged halfway in the liquid so the skin stays crispy while baking.\n4 Cook the chicken thighs in the oven: Transfer the skillet to the oven and cook for 30-35 minutes, or until sweet potatoes are fork-tender and the chicken is cooked through. (It should reach at least 165\xcb\x9aF in the thickest part.) It\xe2\x80\x99s very hard to overcook chicken thighs in this environment, so don\xe2\x80\x99t worry if they register much hotter than that.\n5 Serve the chicken thighs: Divide the chicken thighs between four plates and add cooked rice or orzo to the side, which is great for soaking up the juices. Spoon sweet potatoes and onions on top.\nLeftovers will keep in the fridge for 4-5 days. To reheat, microwave the thighs for about 90 seconds on high. To regain some of the crispiness, reheat the thighs in the oven until warmed through.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'

b"Save It Print\nHomemade Apple Pie Recipe\nPrep time: 1 hour, 15 minutesCook time: 55 minutesYield: Serves 8\nIf the crust looks like it's getting too browned, take a large piece of aluminum foil and place on top of the pie in the oven. No need to wrap it around the pie, just place it on top. That will keep the top from browning further.\nPies always seem to take longer to cook than one expects. (Perhaps it's because we're always opening the oven to check on how the pie is doing?) The filling should be visibly bubbling, which you should be able to see through the steam vents.\nI recommend putting a rimmed baking sheet on a rack beneath the rack of the pie to catch the filling as some of it invariably bubbles up and out over the pie. Makes oven clean-up a lot easier.\nINGREDIENTS\n3 pounds good cooking apples such as Granny Smith, Jonagold, Golden Delicious, Fuji, or Braeburn (about 6 to 8 apples, depending on the size of your apples and the size of your pie dish)\n1 tablespoon lemon juice or apple cider vinegar (to toss with the sliced apples so they don't brown as you slice them)\n1/2 cup to 2/3 cup sugar, depending on how sweet you like your pie\n3 tablespoons all-purpose flour for thickening\n1/2 teaspoon cinnamon\n1/4 teaspoon ground allspice\n1/4 teaspoon ground nutmeg\n1 tablespoon brandy (Optional. By the way, if you have Calvados apple brandy, use it!)\n1 teaspoon vanilla extract\n1 recipe double crust sour cream pie dough, OR all-butter crust, OR your favorite pie crust recipe\nFor the egg wash:\n1 large egg yolk\n1 tablespoon cream\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Peel, core, and slice the apples: Peel, core and slice or roughly chop the apples into 1/4-inch to 1/2-inch slices or chunks.\nAs you cut your apple slices, add them to a large bowl and sprinkle them with a little lemon juice or apple cider vinegar to help keep them from turning brown.\n2 Make the apple pie filling: Combine sugar, flour and spices (allspice, nutmeg, cinnamon) in a bowl. Add the flour mixture to the apple slices and use your hands to distribute the flour through the apples so they are well coated.\nThen sprinkle with brandy and vanilla extract and stir to coat all the apples.\n3 Prepare oven: Place one oven rack in the lowest position and put a large rimmed baking sheet on it (to catch any drippings from the pie.) Position a second rack the next rung up (still in the lower third of the oven) and preheat to 375\xc2\xb0F.\n4 Roll out the dough and line bottom pie plate: Remove one disk of pie dough from the refrigerator. Let sit at room temperature for 5-10 minutes. Place disk on a lightly floured, clean, flat surface. Using a rolling pin, roll out the pie dough to a 12-inch circle, about 1/8 of an inch thick.\nAs you roll out the dough, check to make sure it isn't sticking. If and when it starts to stick, gently lift it up and sprinkle a little more flour on the table surface or on the pie dough to keep the dough from sticking.\nGently place the rolled out dough onto a 9-inch pie plate. Press down to line the pie dish with the dough.\n5 Place apple slices on top of the bottom crust: Arrange the apple slices in the dough-lined pie plate. Mound the apples in the center.\n6 Roll out top crust, place over apples, trim and crimp edges: Roll out the second disk of dough, again to 12-inches. Gently place the second round of pie dough over the apples. Trim excess dough with kitchen shears, leaving a 3/4 inch overhang from the edges of the pie pan.\nFold the dough under itself so that the edge of the fold comes right to the edge of the pan. Press the top and bottom dough rounds together as you flute edges using thumb and forefinger or press with a fork.\n7 Brush with egg wash, cut vents: Place egg yolk and cream in a small bowl and use a fork to stir until well combined. Use a pastry brush to brush the egg wash over the top and fluted edges of the pie. Use a sharp knife to cut slits in the top of the pie crust for steam vents.\n8 Bake: Place pie on oven rack centered over the baking sheet on the rack below it to catch any drippings. Bake the pie at 375\xc2\xb0F until crust begins to lightly brown, about 20 minutes, then reduce heat to 350\xc2\xb0F.\nBake until crust is golden and juices are bubbling, anywhere from an additional 45 minutes to an hour, depending on the type of apples you are using. (About halfway through baking check to make sure the pie isn't browning too much. When it's nicely browned, tent the pie with a large piece of aluminum foil to keep the pie from browning further.)\n9 Let cool: Transfer the apple pie to a rack to cool for at least 1 hour. Serve slightly warm or at room temperature. Great with a side of vanilla ice cream.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b'Save It Print\nSour Cream Apple Pie Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 50 minutesYield: Serves 8\nAs you slice the apples, put them in a bowl and toss them with a little lemon juice or apple cider vinegar. The acidity of the lemon juice or vinegar will help keep the apples from discoloring while you work and will intensify the apple flavor in the pie.\nINGREDIENTS\nFilling:\n1 cup sour cream\n2/3 cup sugar (can easily reduce to 1/2 cup if you like your apple pies a little less sweet)\n2 Tablespoons flour\n1/4 teaspoon salt\n1 teaspoon vanilla\n1 egg\n3 cups peeled, sliced tart apples (about 1 1/4 pounds of slices, cut 1/4-inch to a 1/2-inch thick)\n1 Tablespoon lemon juice or apple cider vinegar\nOne 9" unbaked pie shell, frozen or chilled in the freezer for at least 30 minutes (see sour cream pie crust recipe, use a single crust recipe)\nTopping:\n1/2 cup brown sugar, packed\n1/2 cup flour\n1/4 cup butter (1/2 a stick), chilled, cut into cubes\n1/2 teaspoon cinnamon\nMix together all ingredients until the mixture resembles coarse crumbs. Chill until needed in the recipe.\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Make the streusel topping: Place the streusel topping ingredients in a medium bowl and mix with a fork or your hands until the mixture resembles coarse crumbs.\nChill in the refrigerator until the topping is needed half-way through the baking.\n2 Preheat oven to 400\xc2\xb0F with a rack in the middle and another rack below it. Place a large rimmed baking sheet on the lower rack to catch any of the drippings from the pie.\n3 Mix sour cream with sugar, flour, salt, vanilla, egg, and coat apple slices with it: In a large bowl put the sour cream, sugar, flour, salt, vanilla, and egg. Use a wooden spoon and beat by hand until smooth. Fold in the apples and stir until all of the apples are coated with the sour cream filling mixture.\n4 Put the filling into a frozen pie shell. For the first stage of baking, bake the pie for 25 minutes at 400\xc2\xb0F.\n5 After the first 25 minutes, remove the pie from the oven and sprinkle the top with the brown sugar butter flour topping mixture. You may also want to put a pie protector or foil around the outer crust edges to keep them from getting too browned. Bake for another 20 minutes at 400\xc2\xb0F.\n6 Cool: Let the pie cool on a rack for one hour before cutting and serving.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. b"Save It Print\nGluten-Free Apple Tart Recipe\nPrep time: 45 minutesCook time: 45 minutesChill time: 1 hourYield: 8 to 10\nMaple sugar is a granulated sugar made from dehydrated maple syrup. You can find it on Amazon or in many Whole Foods Stores. Coconut sugar is becoming more widely available. It is a fine substitute, but it will make the tart a much darker shade of golden than the maple sugar.\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the paleo pie crust:\n2 cups finely ground almond flour (I used Bob\xe2\x80\x99s Red Mill Superfine Almond Flour)\n1 cup arrowroot starch\n2 tablespoons maple sugar (or 3 tablespoons coconut sugar)\n1 1/2 tablespoons ground chia seeds (I used white chia seeds)\n1/2 tablespoon ground flax (I used golden flax seeds)\n2 teaspoons baking powder\n1/4 teaspoon salt\n4 tablespoons cold unsalted butter, ghee, lard, duck fat, refined coconut oil, or sustainable palm shortening\n1 large egg\n1 egg yolk\n3 to 6 tablespoons ice water\nExtra arrowroot or tapioca starch for shaping and rolling\nFor the apple filling:\n6 medium baking apples (I like a mix of Granny Smiths and Honeycrisp)\n2 tablespoons unsalted butter, ghee, refined coconut oil, or palm shortening\n2 tablespoons maple sugar (or three tablespoons coconut sugar)\n2 tablespoons lemon juice\n1 tablespoon vanilla extract (optional)\nZest of one lemon\nSpecial equipment:\nFood processor\n9-inch tart pan\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Make the pie crust: Combine the almond flour, arrowroot, maple sugar, chia, flax, baking powder, and salt to the bowl of a food processor and pulse 5 to 6 times to combine. Add the butter and pulse another 4 to 5 times until the mixture starts to look like sandy, pea-sized gravel. Add the egg and egg yolk, then sprinkle 3 tablespoons water evenly over the top of the dough. Pulse a few times until the mixture just starts to clump together and form a ball.\n2 Chill the crust: Turn the pastry dough out onto a cutting board and use your hands to shape it into a chubby disk. Wrap tightly in plastic and refrigerate for at least one hour or up to three days.\n3 Roll out the crust: When ready to bake the tart, lay a sheet of parchment on your counter or other flat surface and sprinkle with arrowroot or tapioca starch. Place the chilled pie dough in the center of the parchment and roll into a circle about 12 inches in diameter.\n4 Transfer the crust to the tart pan: Flip your tart pan upside down and place it in the center of the rolled out pastry dough. There should be at least 1 1/2 inches of pie dough showing around the edge. Carefully, slide one hand palm side up under the parchment and place the other hand on the tart pan. Quickly, and with great confidence, flip the whole thing over.\nGently ease the crust into the tart dish and press it into the corners. Peel back the parchment and discard. Your pastry dough may break, but just press the cracks back together if it does. Use a paring knife to trim away the excess dough and then prick the bottom of the tart all over with the tines of a fork.\n5 Place the tart shell in the freezer to chill while you prepare the apples.\n6 Preheat oven to 350F.\n7 Prepare the apples. Peel the apples and halve them lengthwise. Use a melon baller, paring knife, or small spoon to remove the core, seeds, and stem. Slice the apples very thinly (ideally 1/8-inch thick) using a chef's knife or mandoline.\n8 Prepare the glaze: In a small saucepan, melt butter (or other fat) with the sugar, lemon juice, and vanilla over medium heat. Whisk to combine while bringing to a simmer. Keep whisking until all sugar is dissolved.\n9 Assemble the tart: Find a few of your thinnest apple slices and set them aside. Remove the tart shell from the freezer and begin laying the apple slices in concentric circles, starting from the outer edge of the crust and spiraling inward.\nWhen you get to the center, take your thinnest apple slices and fold them gently to form the center of the pattern. (You might have some apple slices leftover.)\nSprinkle the lemon zest evenly over the tart. Drizzle about half of the glaze evenly over the tart. (I dipped a pastry brush in the glaze and let it drip onto onto the apples.)\n10 Bake the tart for 40 minutes, turning the pan halfway through baking.\n11 Brush the rest of the glaze over the apple slices. Return to the oven and bake for 5 more minutes.\n12 Serve warm or at room temperature.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b"Print\nNew England Apple Cheddar Galette Recipe\nPrep time: 40 minutesCook time: 30 minutesYield: Makes 8 servings\nIf using a tart apple such as a Granny Smith, you may want to add a little sugar or more maple syrup to the filling to balance the tartness of the apple.\nINGREDIENTS\nCrust:\n1 1/2 cups (200g) of all purpose flour\n1/2 teaspoon salt\n1 1/2 teaspoons sugar\n1 1/2 sticks (3/4 cups, 6 ounces, 170 g) unsalted butter\n1/4 cup plus 2 Tbsp (85 ml) sour cream (full fat, not light)\n2 Tbsp finely grated sharp cheddar cheese\nFilling:\n4 good cooking apples, such as McIntosh, Courtland, Jonagold, Pippin, Golden Delicious, Jonathan, Fuji, or a mixture of various cooking apples (NOT red delicious)\n1/2 teaspoon lemon zest\n1 half of a lemon, or the juice of half a lemon (to acidulate the water for holding the apples while you peel them to keep them from discoloring)\n1 Tbsp maple syrup\n2 teaspoons minute tapioca or instant tapioca for thickener (can substitute corn starch)\n1 teaspoon ground cinnamon\n1/2 cup lightly packed grated cheddar cheese\nFinishing:\n1 egg for egg wash\nCoarse sugar for sprinkling on the crust\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\nMake the pastry dough\n1 Cut the butter into cubes. In a large bowl whisk together the flour, salt, and sugar. Sprinkle the butter cubes over the flour.\n2 Use your clean hands to squish the flour and butter together, breaking up the butter into smaller pieces until the mixture resembles a rather shaggy coarse meal with a few pea-sized pieces of butter. Add the sour cream and a couple tablespoons of finely grated sharp cheddar cheese and stir with a fork until incorporated.\n3 Gather the mixture with your hands and form a ball. Shape the ball into a disk. Sprinkle with a little flour, wrap in plastic wrap, and chill in the refrigerator for at least 30 minutes and up to a day ahead.\n  Prepare the galette\n1 Peel, core, quarter the apples, place in water with lemon juice: Preheat oven to 400\xc2\xb0F (205\xc2\xb0C). Prepare a large bowl half filled with water. Squeeze into it the juice of half a lemon (and put the squeezed lemon in too if you want). Peel, quarter, and core the apples, and place into the acidulated water while you work to keep the apples from discoloring.\n2 Slice the apple quarters: Remove the apple quarters from the water. Slice each apple quarter into 4 or 5 slices, lengthwise, about 1/4 inch to 3/8 inch thick at the widest end. Return the apple slices to the acidulated water.\n3 Drain apple slices, sprinkle with maple syrup, cinnamon, minute tapioca, zest: Drain the apple slices. Place the apple slices back in the now empty bowl. Sprinkle with maple syrup and cinnamon and gently toss so that the apple slices are lightly coated with both. Add the minute tapioca and the lemon zest. Gently toss again.\n4 Roll out the dough, transfer to lined baking sheet: On a clean, lightly floured, flat surface, place the disk of dough. Roll out with a rolling pin to an even thickness and about 14 inches wide. Gently move the rolled out pastry dough to a parchment lined baking sheet.\n5 Arrange apple slices on the dough: Starting from 2 inches from the perimeter of the pastry round, arrange the apple slices, side by side, in a circular pattern, filling the circle. It's okay if some of the apple slices overlap a little.\n6 Sprinkle with cheese, fold edges over in pleats: Sprinkle the top of the apples with grated cheddar cheese. Gently fold the dough up over the apple slices, forming pleats with the dough every few inches.\n7 Brush with egg wash, sprinkle with coarse sugar: Place an egg in a small bowl with a teaspoon of water, beat with a fork or whisk until smooth. Use a pastry brush to brush the egg wash over the exposed border of the dough (don't put on the apples, just the dough). Sprinkle the egg washed crust with coarse sugar.\n8 Bake: Bake for 10 to 15 minutes (until beginning to brown) at 400\xc2\xb0F (205\xc2\xb0C). Then lower the temperature to 375\xc2\xb0F (190\xc2\xb0C) and bake for 15 to 20 minutes more, until the apples are cooked through and the crust is nicely browned.\nCool until just lightly warm before serving.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint"

b'Save It Print\nApplesauce Spice Cake Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 30 minutesCooling time: 15 minutesYield: Serves 6 to 8\nThis cake is also great topped with Cream Cheese Frosting!\nRecipe adapted from Kitchen Sense by Mitchell Davis.\nINGREDIENTS\n1/2 cup (1 stick) unsalted butter, room temperature\n2 cups all-purpose flour\n1 teaspoon baking soda\n1 teaspoon cinnamon\n1/2 teaspoon ground allspice\n1/2 teaspoon grated nutmeg\n1/4 teaspoon ground cloves\n1/2 teaspoon salt\n1 cup sugar\n3 large eggs\n1/2 teaspoon vanilla extract\n1 cup applesauce\n1/4 cup plain yogurt diluted a bit with milk, or 1/4 cup of buttermilk\n1/2 cup of chopped walnuts\n1/2 cup raisins\nMETHOD\n1 Preheat oven, prepare pan: Preheat oven to 375\xc2\xb0F. Butter and flour an 8-in square baking pan, set aside.\n2 Combine dry ingredients: Vigorously whisk together the flour, baking soda, cinnamon, allspice, nutmeg, cloves, and salt. Set aside.\n3 Make batter: In an electric mixer, beat butter until light, add sugar and beat until fluffy. Add the eggs, one at a time, beating to incorporate after each addition. Add the vanilla and the applesauce and beat until smooth.\n4 Mix in half of the dry ingredients. Just before they are blended, add the thinned yogurt (or buttermilk). Then mix in the rest of the dry ingredients and the nuts and raisins, until completely incorporated. Do not over-mix.\n5 Bake: Pour out the batter into your prepared cake pan. Place in the middle rack of the 375\xc2\xb0F oven and bake for 25-35 minutes, until done.\nThe cake should spring back to the touch, and a tester or thin skewer should come out clean after being inserted in various spots in the middle of the cake.\nRemove the cake from the oven. b"Save It Print\nHow to Make Fruit Leather\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 9 hoursYield: 4 cups of fruit yield about one baking sheet of fruit leather.\nINGREDIENTS\nFresh fruit (apricots, peaches, plums, berries, apples, pears, grapes)\nWater\nLemon juice\nSugar (if needed)\nSpices such as cinnamon and nutmeg (optional)\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Rinse, taste, and prep the fruit: Rinse the fruit. If you working with stone fruit, take out the pits, chop the fruit. If working with apples or pears, peel and core them, then chop. If working with grapes, de-stem them.\nTaste the fruit before proceeding. Note how sweet the fruit is. If very sweet (ripe Concord grapes for example) you will not need to add any sugar. If still a little tart, you may need to add some sugar in the next step.\n2 Cook fruit with water, sugar, lemon juice, spices: Place fruit in a large saucepan. Add a half cup of water for every 4 cups of chopped fruit.\nBring to a simmer, cover and let cook on a low heat for 10-15 minutes, or until the fruit is cooked through. Uncover and stir.\nUse a potato masher to mash up the fruit in the pan.\nTaste the fruit and determine what and how much sugar, lemon juice, or spices to add.\nAdd sugar in small amounts (1 Tbsp at a time if working with 4 cups of fruit), to desired level of sweetness.\nAdd lemon juice one teaspoon at a time to help brighten the flavor of the fruit. Add a pinch or two of cinnamon, nutmeg, or other spices to augment the flavor.\nContinue to simmer and stir until any added sugar is completely dissolved and the fruit pur\xc3\xa9e has thickened, another 5 or 10 minutes (or more).\nNote if you are working with grapes - strain the juice out of the mashed grapes to make grape juice. Force what is left behind, after straining, through a food mill, to make the pur\xc3\xa9e for the next step.\n3 Pur\xc3\xa9e the cooked, mashed fruit: Put the pur\xc3\xa9e through a food mill or chinoise. Alternatively pur\xc3\xa9e it thoroughly in a blender or food processor.\nTaste again and adjust sugar/lemon/spices if necessary. The pur\xc3\xa9e should be very smooth.\n4 Pour pur\xc3\xa9e into lined baking sheet: Line a rimmed baking sheet with sturdy plastic wrap (the kind that is microwave safe). Pour out the pur\xc3\xa9e into the lined baking sheet to about an 1/8 to 1/4 inch thickness.\n5 Slowly dry out in oven at a very low temp: Place the baking sheet in the oven, try to keep any plastic wrap from touch the sides of the oven or the oven racks. Also try to make sure that the plastic wrap hasn't folded back over on top of the pur\xc3\xa9e. If this happens, the pur\xc3\xa9e won't dry out.\nHeat the oven to a low 140\xc2\xb0F. If you have a convection setting, use it, it will speed up the process and help dry out the pur\xc3\xa9e. Let dry in the oven like this for as long as it takes for the pur\xc3\xa9e to dry out and form fruit leather.\nWe usually keep it in the oven overnight, so about 8-12 hours. The fruit leather is ready when it is no longer sticky, but has a smooth surface.\nAlternatives to the oven. If you have a food dehydrator, this would be a great use of it. My mother suggested putting the tray in the weber grill, and leaving covered, in the sun all day. Sounds like a good trick, but I haven't tried it yet.\nMy parents remember the traditional way of making fruit leather was just to tent the tray with some cheesecloth and leave it outside in the sun on a hot day.\n6 Roll up in its plastic wrap to store: When the fruit leather is ready, you can easily peel it up from the plastic wrap.\nTo store it, roll it in its plastic wrap, put it in an airtight container and store in the refrigerator or freezer.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b"Save It Print\nCouscous with Pistachios and Apricots Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 10 minutesYield: Serves 4-6 as a side dish\nThis recipe calls for boxed couscous that is available in most supermarkets in the U.S. This couscous is precooked semolina, which requires only minimal preparation. Cooking raw couscous is a much more involved process, which we do not cover here in this recipe.\nINGREDIENTS\n1/2 cup chopped red onion\n1/4 cup lemon juice\n1 10-ounce box of couscous, about 1 1/3 cups\n2 tablespoons extra virgin olive oil, divided\n1 teaspoon salt, plus more to taste\n1/2 cup shelled raw pistachios*\n10 dried apricots, chopped\n1/3 cup chopped parsley\nOptional 2 teaspoons harissa, prepared or homemade (see this Paula Wolfert harissa recipe)\n*If you only have access to shelled roasted pistachios, use them and skip step 2 in the method instructions.\nMETHOD\n1 Soak chopped onion in lemon juice: Place the chopped onion in a small bowl. Pour the lemon juice over the onions, set aside and let the onions soak in the lemon juice.\n2 Toast pistachios: Toast the pistachios in a small pan on medium-high heat until lightly browned and fragrant. (Take care when toasting nuts, they can burn quickly if you don't pay attention!) Remove from heat and place into a small bowl to cool.\n3 Cook the couscous: Put 2 cups of water in a medium saucepan and bring to a boil. Add one tablespoon of olive oil and one teaspoon of salt to the water. Once the salt dissolves, stir in the couscous, turn off the heat and cover the pot. Move the pot off the hot burner and let the couscous steam, covered, for 5-6 minutes.\n4 Combine ingredients to make salad: Scoop out the couscous into a large bowl and fluff with a fork. Stir in the harissa, if using. Stir in the pistachios, chopped apricots and parsley. Stir in the red onion and lemon juice. Add one more tablespoon of olive oil, stir well and add salt to taste. Serve warm or at room temperature.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b'Print\nRosemary Duck with Apricots Recipe\nPrep time: 2 hoursCook time: 10 minutesYield: Serves 4\nThis recipe will work with either domestic or wild ducks.\nINGREDIENTS\n3 Tbsp chopped fresh rosemary\n2 Tbsp brown sugar\n1 Tbsp freshly ground black pepper\n2 teaspoons salt\n2 whole duck breasts, halved\n1/2 cup granulated sugar\n1/2 cup champagne vinegar or white wine vinegar\n4 apricots, quartered\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Marinate the duck breasts: Combine the rosemary, brown sugar, black pepper, and salt. Rub the mixture over the duck breasts. Cover and chill 2 hours. Rinse duck with cold water, pat dry.\n2 Score the fatty skin with a sharp knife: If the duck breasts are very fatty, score the skin side with a sharp knife. Be careful not to cut the meat.\n3 Cook fat side down, starting with a cold pan: Lay the duck breast halves skin side down in a cold saut\xc3\xa9 pan and turn on the heat to medium-high. (Yes, start with a cold pan.) Once you hear the duck breasts sizzle, turn the heat down to medium and allow to cook undisturbed until the skin is brown and crispy, about 6-8 minutes.\n4 Turn breasts over to finish cooking: Turn the duck breast over and cook another 2-3 minutes, depending on how well done you like your duck. Use the finger test to check for doneness. As a final step, tip the duck breasts on their sides \xe2\x80\x94 thick side down \xe2\x80\x94 and let them sizzle another minute or so. Remove to a cutting board to rest.\n5 Caramelize the apricots: While the duck is cooking, combine the granulated sugar and vinegar in a small saucepan, and bring to a boil. Cook until thick and amber-colored (about 5 minutes).\nAdd apricots; reduce heat, and cook for 1 minute or until the apricots begin to soften.\n6 Serve: To serve, cut duck diagonally across the grain into slices. Serve with caramelized apricots.\nVARIATION WITH WHOLE DUCK INSTEAD OF BREASTS:\nYou can instead roast a whole duck. Here are the steps (also from Keith):\n1 Marinate the duck: Rinse off the duck, outside and inside, pat dry. Remove any remaining feathers.\nPrick the skin all over with a sharp-tined fork, taking care not to prick the meat.\nRub the duck all over with a little bit of olive oil. Rub the rosemary mixture all over the duck and some in the cavity.\nTie the legs together loosely. Put in a plastic bag and chill in the refrigerator for 2 hours.\n2 Roast the duck breast side up: At least a half an hour before you plan to cook the duck, remove from the refrigerator so it can get to room temperature. Preheat the oven to 350\xc2\xb0F. Place the duck on a roasting rack in a roasting pan, breast side up. Pour a cup of water into the pan. Roast for 45 minutes. Remove the pan from the oven and pour off the fat and water. Separate the fat to use for basting.\n3 Finish roasting the duck breast side down: Turn the bird on the rack so now the breast is facing down. Baste the bird with the fat. Return the bird to the oven. Increase the temperature to 400\xc2\xb0F. Estimate a total cooking time of 15 minutes per lb of bird. So if you have a 4 lb duck, cook it another 30 minutes.\nThe bird is done when the juices run clear from a thigh pricked all the way down to the joint and when a meat thermometer inserted in the inner thigh below the leg joint reads 175 to 180 degrees. Be careful not to overcook the duck. When the bird is done, transfer it to a platter and let it rest for 15 minutes before carving.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'
b"Save It Print\nRoast Chicken with Apricot Glaze Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 1 hourMarinate in Rub time: 1 hourYield: Serves 4\nWe are using a whole chicken for this recipe. You can use parts if you want, bone-in skin on. Follow the instructions for our basic baked chicken for the roasting part, glazing with apricot preserves the last 5 to 10 minutes of cooking.\nWhen cooking a whole chicken, remember to remove to giblets (liver, gizzards, neck) first. They're often in a bag in the cavity. I fry up the liver in butter for a little snack and save the neck and gizzards for making stock.\nINGREDIENTS\nRub:\n2 teaspoons ground cumin\n1/2 teaspoon ground cinnamon\n1 1/2 teaspoon kosher salt\nChicken:\n1 4-pound (1.8 kg) whole chicken\n1 tablespoon extra virgin olive oil\nApricot glaze:\n1/3 cup (80 ml) apricot preserves\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Rub chicken with spices and let sit: Whisk together the cumin, cinnamon, and salt in a small bowl. Rub the spices all over the chicken. Loosely cover and let sit at least one hour, or preferably refrigerate overnight. In either case allow chicken to sit at room temperature for at least one hour (preferably two) before cooking.\n2 Rub chicken with olive oil and roast in oven: Preheat oven to 375\xc2\xb0F. Place the chicken in a roasting pan, breast-side up. Rub olive oil all over the chicken. Place in the middle rack of the oven and cook for 50 minutes at 375\xc2\xb0F or until the internal temperature of the chicken thighs reaches 165\xc2\xb0F.\n3 Heat apricot preserves: While the chicken is roasting, heat the apricot preserves in a small saucepan or in the microwave until warm and runny.\n4 Baste chicken with apricot preserves: Remove chicken from oven, and baste the exposed surfaces of the chicken all over with the apricot preserves, using a basting brush.\n5 Increase oven temp and return chicken to oven: Increase the oven temperature to 400\xc2\xb0F. Return the chicken to the oven and bake for an additional 8 to 10 minutes, basting the chicken again with the glaze halfway through, until the glaze is bubbly and beginning to brown.\n6 Let chicken rest: Remove from oven and let rest for 15 minutes before serving.\nHello! b'Print\nLamb Stew with Almonds and Apricots Recipe\nYield: Serves 6 to 8\nINGREDIENTS\n3 pounds lamb shoulder or neck, trimmed of fat and cut into 2 1/2 inch cubes\n1 teaspoon ground ginger\n1 teaspoon freshly ground black pepper\n1 teaspoon cinnamon\n1/4 teaspoon turmeric\n1/4 teaspoon cayenne\n1/4 teaspoon cardamom\n1/4 teaspoon ground coriander\n1/4 teaspoon nutmeg\n1/4 teaspoon cloves\n1/2 cup water\n1/2 cup (1 stick) unsalted butter\n2 medium onions, finely chopped\n2 cloves garlic, finely chopped\n2 cinnamon sticks\n3 cups chicken stock or water\n1 1/2 cups dried apricots, roughly chopped, or raisins\n1 1/2 cups almonds, whole and blanched\n1/3 cup honey\n1-2 tablespoons freshly squeezed lemon juice (optional)\n1 cup carrots, cut into 1/2-inch thick slices\n1/2 cup flat-leaf parsley, chopped\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Marinate lamb: In a bowl combine the ginger, pepper, cinnamon, turmeric, cayenne, coriander, cardamom, nutmeg, cloves and water and mix well. Add the meat and rub in the paste, coating evenly. Cover and refrigerate overnight.\n2 Cook onions with garlic and cinnamon: In a Dutch oven or other heavy, lidded pot, melt the butter over medium heat. Add the onions, garlic, and cinnamon sticks and cook until the onions are translucent and the mixture is fragrant.\n3 Add meat, marinade, stock: Add the marinated meat (including the marinade) to the pot and then the chicken stock. Bring the stock to a boil, and skim off any scum that appears.\n4 Simmer until tender: Reduce the heat to low, cover and simmer, stirring from time to time. Add water if the pot becomes too dry. Stew until the meat is tender, about 1 1/2 hours, more if needed.\n5 Add apricots, almonds, honey, carrots: Add the apricots, almonds, honey, and carrots and simmer, uncovered, stirring often to prevent scorching, until the meat is very soft and almost falling apart, about 30 minutes longer.\nThe sauce should reduce to a syrupy glaze. At this point taste and add lemon juice to desired level. The lemon juice brings some balance to the sweetness from the honey and apricots.\nNote: this recipe can be prepared in advance up to this point. Allow to cool, refrigerate and serve within a couple of days.\n6 Serve: Stir in the chopped parsley and transfer to a warmed serving dish. Serve immediately with couscous or rice.\nHello! b'Save It Print\nApricot Riesling Jam Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 35 minutesYield: Makes four 8 oz. jars\nMost of the alcohol cooks out and leaves a delightful flavor that I encourage you try, but if you don\'t want to use wine, just substitute with water. This recipe can be easily doubled; if doubling, use an 8-quart pot.\nINGREDIENTS\n5 cups of chopped apricots, pits discarded*\n2 + 3/4 cups of sugar\n1/3 cup of Riesling (or Gew\xc3\xbcrztraminer)\n5 tablespoons of lemon juice\nMETHOD\n1 Place a couple small plates in the freezer, these will be used to test the jam later.\n2 Bring apricots, sugar, wine, lemon juice to a boil: Place the apricots, sugar, wine, and lemon juice in a large (at least 4-qt), thick-bottomed, stainless steel pot and bring to a boil over medium-high heat.\n3 Skim the foam, gently stir: The mixture will boil and rise in volume. Skim off the pale yellow foam that forms at the top and discard. The boil will subside to larger bubbles, but still bubble vigorously. Be sure to begin gently stirring the jam frequently to prevent it from sticking to the bottom.\n4 Test jam on cold plate: After about 25 minutes begin testing the jam by placing a small amount on a cold plate. Allow 30 seconds to pass and then run your finger through it to see what the cooled consistency will be. Boil for a few minutes longer if desired for a thicker jam.\n5 Ladle into jars: Ladle into hot, sterilized canning jars** and seal leaving 1/4 inch of head space. Before applying the lids, sterilize the lids by placing them in a bowl and pouring boiling water over them. Wipe the rims of the jars clean before applying the lids.\nWill keep for up to a year.\n* If you want, you can use a few of the kernels from the pits to give your jam a slight almond-y flavor. Roast the pits at 350 for about 10 minutes. Take them and crack them open with a hammer (do outside on concrete), and extract the kernel. Roast the "nuts" for a couple of minutes. Pop one or two in each sterilized jar when you pour the jam in.\n** To sterilize the jars, rinse out clean Mason jars, dry them, and place them, without lids, upright in a 200\xc2\xb0F oven for 10 minutes.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'

b'Save It Print\nApricot Cherry Galette Recipe\nPrep time: 30 minutesCook time: 1 hourDough chilling time: 1 hourYield: Serves 4\nINGREDIENTS\nCrust:\n1 cup (130 g) all purpose flour\n1 teaspoon sugar\n1/2 teaspoon salt\n1/2 teaspoon crushed fennel seeds\n4 ounces butter (1 stick, 8 Tbsp, 112 g), cut into cubes\n1/4 cup (57 ml) sour cream\n1 egg, beaten, for egg wash\n1 teaspoon cream for egg wash\nCoarse sugar for sprinkling\nFilling:\n1 pound apricots (about 12 apricots, 450 g), pitted and quartered, skin on, recommend Blenheims\n8 pitted cherries, sliced in half\n1/4 cup (50 g) sugar\n1 teaspoon lemon zest\n1 teaspoon minute tapioca for thickening (can sub same amount of cornstarch)\n1/4 teaspoon vanilla extract\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Make the dough: To make the dough, whisk together the flour, sugar, salt, and fennel seeds in a large bowl. Add the butter and work the butter into the flour with your (clean) hands until the mixture resembles crumbs and no piece of butter is bigger than a pea.\nMake a well in the center and add the sour cream. Use a fork to work the flour into sour cream.\nForm the dough into a ball and flatten into a disk. Refrigerate for 1 hour before rolling out.\n2 Toss apricots with sugar, lemon zest, tapioca, vanilla: Put the apricots and cherries into separate bowls. In the bowl with the apricots add the sugar, lemon zest, minute tapioca, and vanilla extract. Gently toss to combine.\n3 Roll out the dough: Roll out the dough and transfer to a parchment lined baking sheet.\n4 Arranged apricots and cherries on rolled out dough: Arrange the apricot quarters in a circular pattern in the center of the rolled out pastry dough, leaving a border of 2 1/2 inches from the edge. Dot with cherry halves.\n5 Fold dough edges over: Fold up the edges of the dough round over the outer edge of the fruit.\nIf at this point the dough has become sticky, put chill the pastry for 10 minutes before proceeding.\n6 Preheat oven to 375\xc2\xb0F (190\xc2\xb0C).\n7 Brush egg wash on crust edges, sprinkle with coarse sugar: Whisk together the beaten egg and the cream for the egg wash. Gently apply the egg wash with a pastry brush to outer edge of the crust (note you will only use a little bit of the egg wash). Sprinkle with a little coarse sugar.\n8 Bake: Bake for 40 to 45 minutes, tenting with foil halfway through the baking process if the crust is getting too browned. The galette is done when the filling is bubbly and thickened, and the crust is nicely browned.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'
b'Save It Print\nApricot Berry Cobbler Recipe\nPrep time: 30 minutesCook time: 45 minutesYield: Serves 8-10\nINGREDIENTS\nCobbler Filling:\n5 cups pitted, quartered apricots (Blenheims if you can get a hold of some)\n3 cups blackberries (or boysenberries or blueberries)\n1 cup white granulated sugar\n2 Tbsp flour (for thickening)\nCobbler Topping:\n2 cups all purpose flour\n2 teaspoons baking powder\n1/2 teaspoon baking soda\n1/2 teaspoon salt\n1 Tbsp white granulated sugar\n1/2 cup (1 stick or 4 ounces) butter softened plus 1/4 cup melted butter\n1 cup buttermilk\n1/2 teaspoon almond extract\n2 Tbsp brown sugar\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Toss the apricots with sugar and flour, place in baking dish: In medium bowl toss the apricots, berries, 1 cup white sugar, and 2 Tbsp flour together.\nPlace filling into baking dish (one 9x13x2 baking dish, or two smaller baking dishes).\n2 Whisk flour, baking powder, baking soda, salt, sugar, then work in butter: Whisk together the 2 cups of flour, baking powder, baking soda, salt, 1 Tbsp white sugar in a medium bowl.\nCut the butter into small cubes and toss into the flour mixture. Work the butter with your fingers to smear it and crumble it into the flour, until the mixture resembles a coarse cornmeal.\nTip: at this point, if you briefly heat the apricot berry mixture in the microwave or oven, until it is warm, it will help the biscuit topping to rise.\n3 Add almond extract and buttermilk: Add almond extract to the buttermilk, then form a well in the middle of the flour mixture and pour in the buttermilk.\nGently mix (with wooden spoon or your hands) until the dough just comes together. Do not over-mix.\n4 Form "cobblestone" shapes of the dough and arrange on the top of the apricot berry mixture. (You can also just crumble the dough over the top.) Sprinkle brown sugar over the top of the dough. Drizzle melted butter over the top (aim for the fruit more than the biscuits).\n5 Preheat oven to 425\xc2\xb0F. Let the cobbler sit and rise for 10-20 minutes before baking.\n6 Bake: Bake at 425\xc2\xb0F for 10-15 minutes or until the top is just beginning to brown, then reduce the heat to 350\xc2\xb0F. Cook for an additional 30 to 40 more minutes, until the center fruit is thickened and bubbly.\nCheck during cooking, if the topping is getting too brown, cover it with foil and turn the heat down to 325\xc2\xb0F.\nHello! b'Save It Print\nApricot Hamantaschen Recipe\nPrep time: 1 hour, 30 minutesCook time: 12 minutesChill time: 12-72 hoursYield: 26-36 cookies\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the apricot filling:\n1-1/4 cups (7 ounces) dried apricots, preferably Turkish\n2 tablespoons honey\nFor the dough:\n2 cups (262 grams) all-purpose flour\n3/4 cup (156 grams) sugar\n1/2 teaspoon baking powder\n1/2 teaspoon salt\n1/2 cup (1 stick) unsalted butter or margarine, chilled\n1 teaspoon finely grated lemon zest\n1 teaspoon finely grated orange zest\n1 large egg, lightly beaten\nSpecial equipment:\nFood processor\nBox grater\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Make the filling: Put the apricots in a small saucepan and add enough water to cover. Put on the lid, bring to a boil, reduce the heat, and simmer until the fruit is tender, about 10-15 minutes.\nRemove the apricots from the saucepan with a slotted spoon and place in a food processor. Reserve the cooking water.\nAdd the honey and 1 tablespoon of the cooking water to the food processor, and puree until very smooth, scraping down the sides of the food processor from time to time. If the fruit is too thick for the machine to puree it, add 1 to 2 more tablespoons of cooking water.\nScrape the filling into a container, let it cool, cover with plastic wrap, and refrigerate overnight or up to 3 days before baking.\n2 Make the dough: Lay a large sheet of plastic wrap on the counter.\nIn a large bowl, whisk together the flour, sugar, baking powder, and salt. Using the large holes of a box grater, grate the margarine or butter into the bowl (work quickly so the butter does not melt). Add the lemon and orange zest.\nWork the grated butter into the flour with a pastry cutter or your fingertips until the mixture resembles coarse cornmeal. Add the egg and knead with your hands for a minute or 2, until the dough is smooth and no longer crumbly.\nLay the dough on the plastic wrap, press into a flat rectangle, and wrap tightly. Chill in the refrigerator overnight, or up to 3 days.\n3 Heat the oven and prepare the baking sheets: Preheat the oven to 400\xc2\xb0F and position racks in the upper and lower thirds of the oven. Line 2 baking sheets with parchment paper or silicone baking mats. Take the dough out of the refrigerator and let it come to temperature for 10 minutes.\n4 Roll out the dough Lightly flour your countertop. Cut the dough in half; return one half to the refrigerator.\nDust both sides of the dough lightly with flour. Roll out to an even 1/8-inch thickness. Use a dry pastry brush or your hands to brush off the excess flour. Using a 3-inch biscuit or cookie cutter or a drinking glass, cut the dough into rounds.\nPlace the rounds on the baking sheets as you go. Once your first sheet is filled, pop it in the fridge so the cookies keep their shape while you work on the second baking sheet. Save and refrigerate the dough scraps.\nRepeat with remaining half of dough, then re-roll scraps and get as many rounds as you can out of them. (You\xe2\x80\x99ll have anywhere between 26 to 36 rounds).\n5 Fill the cookies: Transfer the chilled filling to a piping bag or a zip-top sandwich bag with the corner snipped off.\nWorking with one baking sheet at a time, pipe a circle of filling (about 1-1/2 teaspoons) on the center of each dough round. (You will likely have extra filling. Store it in the refrigerator and use it to spread on toast or stir into yogurt.)\n6 Shape the cookies: Start by folding one edge over. Fold the second edge over so one corner overlaps the other and forms a 60-degree angle. Fold the third edge over, creating the three distinct corners of a triangle. The first few cookies you shape might not be perfect, but you\xe2\x80\x99ll get the hang of it quickly. There is no need to press, pinch or seal the edges.\n7 Bake the cookies: Arrange the cookies so they are about 2 inches apart (they should all fit on two baking sheets). Bake and set your timer for 6 minutes.\nWhen the timer goes off, rotate the sheets front to back and top to bottom. Reset the timer, and bake the cookies for an additional 5 to 10 minutes, or until the edges are golden brown. Total baking time will be 12 to 16 minutes.\n8 Cool the cookies: Cool the cookies on sheets for 2 minutes, then transfer to cooling racks with a metal spatula. You may serve the cookies warm, but they are best at room temperature.\nThe cookies are crispiest on the day you bake them, but they will last up to 3 days in a tightly covered container.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'

b'Save It Print\nKale with Seaweed, Sesame and Ginger Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 15 minutesYield: Serves 4\nINGREDIENTS\n1/2 cup dried arame sea vegetables (food-grade seaweed)\n3 Tbsp vegetable oil\n1 teaspoons dark (roasted) sesame oil\n1 Tbsp peeled and minced ginger\n1 bunch kale (we used dinosaur kale)\n1 Tbsp minced garlic\n1 Tbsp soy sauce (can sub with Bragg Liquid Aminos)\n1 Tbsp Toasted sesame seeds\nMETHOD\n1 Prepare the seaweed: Rinse the seaweed in water and let soak, covered in water for 5-7 minutes.\nDrain seaweed and place in a large bowl. Add garlic and gently saut\xc3\xa9 for one minute, until fragrant. Add the seaweed and ginger, gently cook for 1 minute. Remove seaweed/ginger/garlic from pan back to the bowl and set aside.\n4 Saut\xc3\xa9 kale: Add another 1 Tbsp oil to the skillet. When the oil is hot, add the chopped kale. Add 1 Tbsp soy sauce. Gently mix in the pan to coat the kale with the oil and soy sauce. Cover; lower heat to low; let cook for 5-10 minutes or until kale is wilted - soft enough to eat easily, but not so soft as to be mushy.\nRemove cover and let cook a minute more to evaporate any excess moisture. Remove from heat.\n5 Mix in the kale with the seaweed ginger mixture. Add more dark sesame oil and soy sauce to taste. Garnish with toasted sesame seeds.\nHello! b'Save It Print\nHow to Cook and Eat an Artichoke\nPrep time: 5 minutesCook time: 35 minutes\nINGREDIENTS\n1 or more large globe artichokes\n1-2 cloves of garlic, cut in half (can leave skin on)\n1 bay leaf\n1 slice of lemon\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\nHOW TO COOK AN ARTICHOKE\n1 Cut of the tips of the leaves: If the artichokes have little thorns on the ends of their leaves, take a kitchen scissors and cut off the tips. This step is mostly for aesthetics as the thorns soften with cooking and pose no threat to the person eating the artichoke. But snipping them off will make the artichokes easier to handle.\n2 Slice off the top of the artichoke: Slice about 3/4 inch to an inch off the tip of the artichoke. A serrated bread knife works great for this.\n3 Remove small leaves at the base: Pull off any smaller leaves towards the base and on the stem.\n4 Cut off excess stem: Cut off excess stem, leaving up to an inch on the artichoke. The stems can be more bitter than the rest of the artichoke, but some people like to eat them. The inner cores of the stems taste like the heart.\nAlternatively you can leave the whole long stem on the artichoke, just cut off the very end of the stem, and peel the tough outside layer of the stem with a vegetable peeler.\n5 Rinse the artichokes: Rinse the artichokes in running cold water. While you rinse them, open up the leaves a little so that the water gets inside more easily. (This is where it helps to have cut off the thorny tips, it makes the artichoke easier to open without getting poked!)\n6 Set up a pot with some water, aromatics, and a steaming basket: In a large pot, put a couple inches of water, the garlic, a slice of lemon, and a bay leaf (this adds wonderful flavor to the artichokes). Insert a steaming basket.\n7 Steam the artichokes: Place artichokes on top of the steaming basket. Cover the pot. Bring to a boil and reduce heat to simmer.\nCook for 25 to 35 minutes or longer, until the outer leaves can easily be pulled off.\nNote: artichokes can also be cooked in a pressure cooker (about 5-15 minutes at high pressure). Cooking time depends on how large the artichokes are. The larger, the longer they take to cook.\nHOW TO EAT AN ARTICHOKE\nArtichokes may be eaten cold or hot, but I think they are much better hot. They are served with a dip, either melted butter or mayonnaise. My favorite dip is mayo with a little bit of balsamic vinegar mixed in.\n1 Pull off the leaves and dip: Pull off the outer leaves, one at a time. Dip the white fleshy end in melted butter, a vinaigrette, or sauce.\n2 Place light end in mouth, dip side down, pull, scraping through your teeth: Tightly grip the other end of the petal. Place in mouth, dip side down, and pull through teeth to remove soft, pulpy, delicious portion of the petal. (Why dip-side down? Your tongue is where most of your taste buds are, so you\'ll get a fuller flavor if you strip the leaves that way.) Discard remaining petal.\nContinue until all of the petals are removed.\nWhen you get to the tender inner leaves with the purple tips, you can remove them all at once. Dip and eat just the light colored parts of these leaves.\n3 Scrape out the choke: With a knife or spoon, scrape out and discard the inedible fuzzy part (called the "choke") covering the artichoke heart.\n4 Cut the heart into pieces and eat: Underneath the artichoke choke is the heart. Cut the heart into pieces and dip into melted butter, a vinaigrette, or a sauce to eat.\nMy favorite artichoke dipping sauce? Some mayonnaise with a little balsamic vinegar stirred in.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'
b'Save It Print\nPasta with Spinach, Artichokes and Ricotta Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 20 minutesYield: 4 servings\nIf you have time, let the artichokes sit out for 10 minutes or so to partially defrost. If you don\xe2\x80\x99t have time, then they will take just a few minutes longer to heat all the way through in the skillet.\nINGREDIENTS\n3 tablespoons olive oil, divided\n3/4 cup Panko breadcrumbs\n1/4 cup coarsely chopped toasted almonds\n1/2 teaspoon salt, divided\n3/4 pound medium shaped pasta, such as penne, medium shells, lumache, or fusilli\n1 clove garlic, minced\n1 (12-ounce) package frozen artichoke hearts, partially thawed if time allows (See Recipe Note)\n3 ounces (3 packed cups) baby spinach\n2 teaspoons finely grated lemon zest\n1/3 cup grated Parmesan\n2 tablespoons lemon juice\n3/4 cup ricotta cheese\n2 tablespoons chopped fresh parsley, to garnish\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Make the breadcrumb topping:  In a small skillet over medium heat, heat 1 tablespoon of the oil. Add the breadcrumbs and chopped almonds, and cook, stirring, for 2 to 3 minutes, or until brown and crisp. Add 1/4 teaspoon salt, or to taste. Set aside.\n2 Cook the pasta: Bring a large pot of salted water to a boil. Add the pasta and cook for 8 to 10 minutes, or until al dente. (Check the package for recommended cooking time and cook one minute less.)\nScoop out and set aside 1 cup of the pasta cooking water. Drain the pasta in a colander.\n3 While the pasta cooks, cook the artichokes: In a large skillet over medium-high heat, heat the remaining 2 tablespoons of oil. Add the garlic and cook, stirring, for 30 seconds. Add the artichokes and stir and cook for 3 to 4 minutes, or until lightly browned.\nStir in the spinach and cook for another 30 seconds, or until it has wilted very slightly. Stir in the lemon zest and 1/4 teaspoon salt. Taste and add additional salt if needed.\n4 Toss the pasta with the artichokes: Add the drained pasta to the skillet with the artichokes. Add the Parmesan and lemon juice, and toss to combine. Dollop the ricotta over the pasta by the spoonful. Toss together. If the pasta seems dry, add a little of the pasta cooking water. Taste and add salt and freshly ground black pepper.\n5 Serve the pasta: Divide the pasta among 4 bowls and top with the toasted breadcrumbs and almonds. Sprinkle with parsley and serve.\nHello! b"Save It Print\nBaked Stuffed Artichokes Recipe\nPrep time: 25 minutesCook time: 1 hour, 5 minutesYield: Serves 4\nINGREDIENTS\n2 large globe artichokes\n4 slices lemon\n1 teaspoon lemon zest\n6 slices white bread\n1/2 cup grated Parmesan cheese\n1/2 cup chopped parsley\n6 cloves garlic, minced\n1 teaspoon fresh oregano, minced\n1/2 cup plus 2 tablespoons extra virgin olive oil\n1/8 teaspoon black pepper\n  1 bay leaf\n2 slices lemon\n2 cloves garlic, halved\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Make fresh breadcrumbs: Cut off the crust from 6 slices of bread. Chop the centers and put into a food processor. Pulse until you have coarse breadcrumbs. You should have about 3 cups.\n2 Make the stuffing: In a large bowl, stir together the breadcrumbs, lemon zest, Parmesan cheese, minced garlic, chopped parsley, minced oregano, 1/2 cup olive oil, and black pepper. Set aside.\n3 Prep the artichokes: Cut off the stem, leaving 1/2 inch from the bottom row of leaves. Using kitchen scissors, cut off 1/2-inch of the tips of all of the artichoke leaves.\nCut 1 inch from the top of the artichoke. (It helps to use a serrated knife like a bread knife for this.)\nTake a slice of lemon and rub over the cut edges of the artichokes to keep them from turning brown.\n4 Preheat oven to 375\xc2\xb0F (190\xc2\xb0C).\n5 Stuff the artichokes: Use your finger to gently pull open the center leaves of the artichokes. Pull out the inner tender yellow artichoke leaves. Use a small metal spoon to scrape and scoop out all of the inner fuzzy choke.\nNote that removing the choke at this stage isn't entirely necessarily, and it does require some elbow grease. That said, it makes eating the stuffed artichoke a much easier, and more enjoyable experience.\nPlace artichokes on a sheet pan (to catch the breadcrumbs) and start stuffing the artichoke with your stuffing mix. Put some stuffing mix between each large leaf and the artichoke, as well as a generous amount in the center.\n6 Bake the artichokes: Put about 1-inch of boiling water in the bottom of a Dutch oven that will snugly hold the artichokes. Add 2 slices of lemon, a bay leaf, 2 cloves garlic to the water.\nPlace the artichokes sitting upright in the water. Drizzle with remaining 2 Tbsp olive oil.\nCover the pot tightly with a lid. (Remember to cover the dish or this method will not work!)\nBake for 1 hour at 375\xc2\xb0F (190\xc2\xb0C), or until a knife easily penetrates the heart of the artichoke or you can easily remove one of the outer petals. (Depending on the size of the artichoke baking time can vary from 50 minutes to 1 hour 30 minutes or longer.)\nRemove the cover and broil for a minute or so, enough to get some browning on the top of the stuffing.\nRemove artichokes to a serving dish to serve.\nHello! b"Save It Print\nArtichoke Lemon Dip Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesYield: Makes about 2 cups of dip\nINGREDIENTS\n1 14-ounce (400 g) can of artichoke hearts, packed in water, drained\n1/4 cup chopped fresh parsley\n1/4 cup (25 g), packed, grated Parmesan cheese\n1 Tbsp lemon zest\n1 clove garlic, minced (about 1 teaspoon)\n1/2 teaspoon fresh black pepper\n1/4 teaspoon salt\n8 ounces (225 g) cream cheese, room temperature\n3 to 4 Tbsp lemon juice\nMETHOD\n1 Pulse artichoke hearts, parsley, Parmesan, zest, garlic, salt and pepper: Put the drained artichoke hearts, parsley, Parmesan, lemon zest, garlic, and salt and pepper in a food processor.
