b'Save It Print\nGrilled Artichokes Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 45 minutesYield: Serves 4\nINGREDIENTS\n1 tablespoon chopped fresh herbs such as rosemary, oregano, thyme\n1/3 cup extra virgin olive oil\n2 cloves garlic, cut in half (no need to peel)\n1 bay leaf\n1 lemon, cut into wedges\n2 to 4 large globe artichokes\nSalt\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Steep herbs in warm olive oil: Place chopped fresh herbs in a small bowl (not the bay leaf), cover with olive oil. Microwave on high heat for 30 seconds (or heat oil and herbs on the stovetop until warm). Let the herbs steep in the warm olive oil while you prepare the artichokes.\n2 Prep the artichokes: Prepare a large pot with an inch of water at the bottom. Add the cut cloves of garlic and the bay leaf, and place a steamer rack in the pot.\nTo prepare the artichokes, have lemon wedges ready. If you want a nice presentation, use scissors to snip away the pointy tips of the artichoke leaves. As you trim the artichokes, rub the cut areas with juice from the lemon wedges to prevent the artichokes from turning brown from oxidation.\nUse a vegetable peeler to cut away the thick outer layer of the artichoke stems. Trim the stems to 2 inches from the base of the artichoke. Cut off and discard the top 1/2 inch of the artichokes. Cut the artichokes in half.\nUse a strong metal spoon to scoop out the fuzzy chokes and the small inner artichoke leaves. Rub lemon juice all over the inside and exposed cut areas of the artichokes.\n\n3 Steam the artichokes: Heat the water in the large pot with a steamer rack on high. When it comes to a boil, reduce the heat to medium high and place the artichoke halves, cut side down on the steam rack.\nCover. Steam for 20 minutes (less or more, depending on the size of the artichokes), until you can easily pull off the outer leaves, and you can pierce the heart easily with a knife.\nThe artichokes can be just a tiny bit less cooked than would be typically perfect for steamed artichokes, as you will be cooking them further on the grill.\n4 Grill the artichokes: Prepare your grill for direct, high heat. Use a pastry brush to brush the artichoke all over with the herb infused oil. Sprinkle all over with salt.\nPlace the artichoke halves cut-side-down on the grill grates. Cover, and grill for 5 to 10 minutes, until you have nice grill mark on the cut sides of the artichokes.\nTo serve, sprinkle the cut sides with more lemon juice. Serve alone or with mayonnaise, remoulade, or aioli.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'
b'Save It Print\nSpinach and Artichoke Quiche Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 40 minutesMaking Homemade Crust time: 2 hoursYield: Serves 6 to 8\nWe give instructions for making your own crust from scratch. You can also easily use a frozen pie shell, just keep it frozen, do not defrost.\nWe use goat cheese in this recipe. You could easily sub with grated Gruyere or Monterey jack.\nINGREDIENTS\nCrust:\n1 cup all purpose flour\n1/2 teaspoon salt\n1/2 cup (1 stick, 4 ounces, 8 Tbsp) butter\n2 to 2 1/2 Tbsp of water\nOne 9-inch pie dish\nQuiche: \n1/2 cup, packed, finely chopped artichoke hearts (cooked fresh or canned artichoke hearts packed in water)\n6 ounces cooked spinach (if using frozen, thaw first), squeezed to remove excess water (wrap in clean tea towel or several layers of paper towels and squeeze), finely chopped\n1 Tbsp butter\n1/2 cup minced shallots\n2 teaspoons grated lemon zest\n4 eggs (large)\n1 cup milk\n1/2 cup heavy whipping cream\n4 ounces goat cheese\n1 teaspoon salt\n1/4 teaspoon black pepper\n2 Tbsp minced chives or green onion greens\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1a Make the dough for the quiche crust: In a medium bowl, whisk together the flour and salt.\nCut the butter into cubes and use your (clean) hands to work the butter into the flour until you have a mixture that looks like a coarse meal with pieces of butter no bigger than a pea.\nSprinkle water onto the flour mixture a little at a time, and work the dough with your hands until the dough can be formed into a ball.\nFlatten the ball into a disk and wrap with plastic wrap. Chill for at least 1 hour.\n1b Roll out the dough: When you are ready to roll out the dough, remove the disk from the refrigerator and let come to room temp for 10 minutes.\nRoll out the dough on a lightly floured surface to a diameter 2 inches wider than your pie or tart pan. Drape the rolled out dough over the pie or tart pan and press the dough into the sides of the pan. Trim and crimp the edges.\nPlace in freezer for 30 minutes to an hour.\n2 (Optional) Pre-bake the crust: At this point, if you want, you can "blind bake" or pre-bake the crust. Pre-baking the crust will ensure that the bottom crust is browned and won\'t get soggy. I often skip this step and find that although the bottom crust might not get browned, it\'s usually perfectly palatable.\nTo pre-bake a store-bought crust, just follow the directions on the crust package.\nTo pre-bake the homemade crust in this recipe, line the inside with aluminum foil and fill it with pie weights such as beans. The foil and the pie weights will help keep the sides of the crust from sliding down as it bakes.\nBake for 15 minutes at 375\xc2\xb0F, then remove the foil and weights, prick the bottom of the crust with the tines of a fork , and bake for another 10 minutes. Let cool down a bit before filling with the quiche custard filling.\n3 Cook the shallots: Melt butter in a small saucepan on medium heat. Add the minced shallots and cook 3 to 4 minutes until translucent. Remove from heat.\n4 Prepare the filling: Preheat oven to 375\xc2\xb0F. Beat the eggs in a large bowl. Add the goat cheese and whisk until smooth. Whisk in the milk, cream, salt, pepper, chopped spinach, chopped artichokes, the cooked shallots, lemon zest, and the chives.\n5 Bake the quiche: Pour filling into the frozen pie crust. (If you are using a tart pan with a removable bottom, you may want to put the pan on a foil lined or rimmed sheet pan.)\nPlace in oven. Bake at 375\xc2\xb0F for 10 minutes, then reduce the heat to 350\xc2\xb0F and cook for 30 minutes, or until the center of the quiche has set.\n6 Let cool before serving: Remove from oven and let sit and cool to room temperature before slicing and serving.\n  Hello! b"Save It Print\nArtichoke Leek Frittata Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 35 minutesYield: Serves 4\nINGREDIENTS\n2 Tbsp butter\n2 cups sliced, cleaned leeks, white and light green parts only  (sliced in half lengthwise, then sliced crosswise, about 1/4-inch thick slices) (see How to Clean Leeks)\n4 ounces frozen artichoke hearts, thawed, sliced into 1/2-inch slices\n1/2 teaspoon dried tarragon (can sub 2 teaspoons of chopped fresh tarragon, or dried herbes de Provence or dried thyme)\n1/4 teaspoon Kosher salt\n5 eggs\n8 ounces (1 cup) small curd cottage cheese (can use ricotta if you prefer)\n2 Tbsp all purpose flour (omit for gluten-free version)\n1/2 teaspoon baking powder\n1 cup grated Parmesan cheese\nFresh chopped chives or parsley for garnish\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Cook the leeks in butter: In an 8 to 9-inch oven-proof stick-free pan (like hard anodized aluminum with stainless handle) or well seasoned cast-iron pan, melt butter on medium heat. Add the sliced leeks and gently cook until softened, about 10 minutes.\n2 Add artichoke hearts, tarragon, salt: Once the leeks are cooked through and softened, add the artichoke hearts, tarragon, and salt. Cook until the artichoke hearts are warmed through, then remove from pan to a bowl and set aside.\n3 Make the egg batter: In a medium bowl, whisk together the eggs and the cottage cheese.\nIn a small bowl, whisk together the flour, Parmesan, and baking powder.\nAdd the flour mixture to the egg mixture and whisk.\nStir the artichokes and leeks into the egg  mixture. Note that the color of the mixture may change, don't worry if this happens, it will go back to normal when cooked.\n4 Pour egg mixture into pan and gently cook: Wipe out the pan with a paper towel. Then melt another tablespoon of butter into the pan on medium heat, and swirl along the bottom and sides to coat well. Pour the egg mixture into the pan, swirling to make sure the artichokes and leeks are evenly distributed.\nLower the heat. Cover the pan, slowly cook on the stove top for 12 to 15 minutes, until all but the center has set. You'll need to check every few minutes.\nThe heat should be high enough to set the mixture, but low enough so that the edges don't brown. This frittata benefits from slow, gentle cooking.\n5 Finish in the broiler: Place rack in upper third of oven. Preheat the broiler. When the frittata is mostly set, except for the center which is still wiggly, place the pan in the oven. Broil for 3 to 4 minutes until the top is lightly browned and the center has set.\n6 Serve: Remove pan from oven. (Be careful about the hot handle! Use a pot holder. I like to run an ice cube over the handle to to be extra safe.) Use a blunt knife or a metal spatula to loosen the edges of the frittata from the pan. Gently insert the spatula under the frittata to loosen it from the bottom of the pan. Then gently slide the frittata onto a serving plate.\nGarnish with chives or parsley to serve.\nHello! Remove from oven and let rest for 5 minutes before serving.\n  Hello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. b"Save It Print\nBraised Marinated Artichokes Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 40 minutesYield: Serves 4\nChoose globe artichokes whose petals are closed. They'll be fresher than artichokes whose petals have started to open wide. Frost-kissed artichokes are especially delicious, so even though they may look a little blemished, they'll taste great.\nINGREDIENTS\n2 large globe artichokes\n1 lemon\n1/4 cup extra virgin olive oil\n3/4 cup sliced shallots\n3 cloves garlic, minced, about 1 Tbsp\n3 bay leaves\n1 cup dry white wine (such as a Sauvignon blanc)\n3/4 cup water\n1 teaspoon salt\n3 Tbsp chopped fresh parsley leaves\n2 Tbsp chopped fresh mint leaves\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Prep the artichokes: Prepare a large bowl with cold water. Squeeze half a lemon into the water. Using a serrated knife (bread knife works well for this), cut off the top inch of the artichokes. Squeeze a little lemon over the cut areas to keep the artichokes from turning brown.\nUse kitchen shears to snip off the thorny tips of the artichoke leaves.\nUse the serrated knife to cut the artichokes into quarters.\nUse a metal teaspoon to scrape away the hairy choke above the artichoke heart. Remove the small, papery, purplish leaves close to the choke. Rub the cut areas again with lemon.\nPlace the quartered artichoke hearts into the bowl of acidulated water as you finish prepping them.\n2 Saut\xc3\xa9 shallots and garlic: Heat olive oil on medium heat in a thick-bottomed pot that will hold all of the artichokes tightly in a single layer. (Choose a pot with a tight-fitting lid.)\nWhen the oil is hot, add the shallots and saut\xc3\xa9 for 3 to 5 minutes, until softened.\nAdd the garlic and cook an additional minute.\n3 Add wine, water, bay leaves, salt, then simmer: Add the white wine, water, bay leaves, and salt to the pot. Make sure there is enough liquid to cover the bottom of the pan by 1/4-inch. If not, add more water until there is. Bring to a simmer, and simmer for a minute.\n4 Add quartered artichokes, simmer: Place the quartered artichokes, cut side down in a single layer, in the pot. Bring to a boil on high heat.\nCover the pot with a tight fitting lid and lower the heat to medium. Simmer for 20 minutes. (If it looks like the pot is at risk of running out of liquid, add more hot water to the pot.)\n5 Toss with parsley, mint, continue to simmer: Then toss with the parsley and mint, turning the artichokes over to coat them with the sauce, cover again, and cook for an additional 5 to 15 minutes, until the leaves are tender and are easy to pull off the artichoke.\nNote that older artichokes may take a longer cooking time (and therefore more water/wine in the pot) to get tender.\nLet cool to slightly warm or room temperature. Serve with some of the pan juices and shallots from the braising liquid. Especially good if you make a day ahead, giving the cooked artichokes more time to marinate. Just chill, and return to room temperature before serving.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b"Save It Print\nSpinach & Artichoke Sheet Pan Pizza Recipe\nPrep time: 30 minutesCook time: 15 minutesYield: 4 to 6 servings\nOne pound of dough is perfect for making a thin-crust pizza, but use 2 pounds of dough if you'd like a thicker, breadier crust.\nIf your artichoke hearts seem like they'd be a large mouthful, cut them into smaller, more bite-sized pieces. b"Print\nHow to Trim an Artichoke\nYou'll need a sharp paring knife, a large empty bowl for leaves, and a large bowl filled two-thirds with ice water.\nINGREDIENTS\nArtichokes\nA fresh lemon cut in half\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Squeeze half a lemon into a large bowl of water: If you are trimming more than one artichoke, squeeze half a lemon into a large bowl of ice water. You will be dropping trimmed artichokes into this bowl to keep them from browning while you work others.\n2 Snap off outer green leaves, then pull off yellow petals: Start by snapping off the artichoke leaves and tossing them into a large empty bowl. When you get to the yellow petals, just pull them off. Wipe the exposed surface with the other half of the lemon you cut.\n3 Pull out the pink tipped leaves: Take care when you get to the pink center of the artichoke leaves. There are sharp spines on the end of the inner leaves. Pull them out.\n4 Use a paring knife to dig out the fuzzy choke. You will want to slice off the narrowest layer of the heart to get all of the choke without cutting away too much of the delicious heart.\nA note on this whole process. Don\xe2\x80\x99t do it if there are distractions. You need to focus. You will be using a sharp knife close to your hands. Since artichokes are tough when raw, you can easily cut yourself if you take your eye off what you are doing.\n5 Rub cut lemon over exposed artichoke heart: Once the fuzzy choke is out, smear the cut lemon all over the exposed heart.\nThis prevents the heart from oxidizing and turning brown. An artichoke is still perfectly edible when oxidized, it just is not particularly attractive.\n6 Slice off all but the last inch or so of the stem. Rub lemon juice on the cut end.\n7 Trim the hard green exterior of the rest of the heart. Cut away from you as you rotate the artichoke, slicing off just the hard green part and leaving the light green underneath. Rub this with lemon.\n8 To finish, slice the outside layer off the stem and then coat the whole heart one more time with lemon. Drop into the lemon-water bath and go on to the next one.\nHere's a tip: as your cut lemon gets used up, put it in the water bath, which will help keep the bath\xe2\x80\x99s citric acid content high, and help keep the artichokes from browning.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint"
b'Save It Print\nArtichoke and Shrimp Risotto Recipe\nPrep time: 7 minutesCook time: 35 minutesYield: Serves 3 to 4\nIf starting with frozen shrimp, thaw by placing in a bowl of cold water with a teaspoon of salt stirred in. Peel and devein once thawed.\nWe are using artichokes canned in water for this recipe and we suggest including the artichoke water in with the risotto. Taste the artichoke water first. If it tastes good to you, then include. If not, then don\'t.\nYou can also use frozen or fresh cooked artichoke hearts instead of canned. For frozen you\'ll probably need about 8 ounces. For fresh, you\'ll probably need the hearts from 2 globe artichokes, cooked and finely chopped.\nSee How to Cook and Eat an Artichoke for instructions on cooking artichokes.\nINGREDIENTS\n12 ounces raw shrimp (26-30 size), about 18 pieces\n1/2 teaspoon paprika\nSalt\n1/8 teaspoon freshly ground black pepper\n1 Tbsp butter + 2 Tbsp butter\n1/3 cup minced shallots\n1 Tbsp minced garlic\n1 1/2 cup risotto rice (recommend carnaroli, can also use arborio)\n1/2 cup dry white wine (like a Sauvignon Blanc)\n8 ounces clam juice\n1 14-ounce can artichoke hearts packed in water, drained (reserve the water!), and finely chopped\n2-3 cups water\n2 Tbsp chopped fresh parsley\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Toss shrimp with paprika, salt, pepper: Pat dry the peeled and deveined shrimp and place them in a medium bowl, toss to coat with 1/2 teaspoon salt, the paprika, and pepper.\n2 Saut\xc3\xa9 shrimp: Heat 1 Tbsp butter in a small saut\xc3\xa9 pan on high heat. Add the shrimp and saut\xc3\xa9 for 1 to 2 minutes on each side, until they are cooked on the outside, but not quite cooked through (they\'ll continue to cook as they sit outside of the pan). Then remove to a bowl and set aside.\n3 Simmer salted water: Put 3 cups of water with about a teaspoon of salt in a small saucepan. Heat until simmering and keep warm while you start the risotto.\n4 Saut\xc3\xa9 shallots, garlic: Heat 2 Tbsp butter in a 3 to 4-quart thick-bottomed pot on medium heat. Add the minced shallots and cook until translucent, about 3 to 4 minutes.\nAdd the garlic and cook a minute more.\n5 Add risotto rice: Add the risotto rice to the pot, stir to coat. Let cook for a minute or two for the rice to just barely begin to brown.\n6 Add 1/2 cup dry white wine. Let come to a low simmer and slowly stir until the wine has been absorbed by the rice.\n7 Add clam juice, artichoke can water: Add the clam juice and the reserved water from the can of artichokes, a half cup at a time, slowly stirring and allowing the rice to absorb the liquid before adding more liquid.\n8 Start adding hot salted water, 1/2 cup at a time: Once the rice as absorbed the wine, clam juice, and artichoke water, you can start adding the hot, lightly salted water from step one.\nAdd it 1/2 cup at a time, again stirring slowly allowing the rice to absorb it for a minute or two before adding any more. You\'ll need between 2 and 3 cups of water.\nYou\'ll want to stop adding water when the rice is cooked through, but still a little firm to the bite, "al dente".\n9 Stir in the chopped artichoke hearts. Fold in the shrimp and chopped parsley. Serve immediately.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'

b"Save It Print\nSweet and Sour Glazed Artichokes with Caramelized Onions Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 45 minutesYield: Serves 4\nYou can use either standard large globe artichokes for this recipe, or if you can find them, Roman artichokes.\nThink of artichoke leaves as the petals of a flower (which indeed they are). Choose artichokes where the leaves haven't opened much. If they've begun to open, the artichoke is probably not as fresh and good as one where the leaves are still closed and tight.\nINGREDIENTS\n3 large globe artichokes (or 4 Roman artichokes)\n1 large onion, cut in half and thinly sliced cross-wise\n2 1/2 tablespoons extra virgin olive oil\n1/2 teaspoon Kosher salt\n1 tablespoon sugar\n3 tablespoons white vinegar\nLemon for the acidulated water\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Prep the artichokes: Prepare a large bowl of water, squeeze half a lemon into the water. b'Print\nOil-Poached Artichoke Heart Salad Recipe\nPrep time: 25 minutesCook time: 45 minutesYield: Serves 4\nThe seasonings are a guide here: If you\xe2\x80\x99d rather toss the \xe2\x80\x98chokes with something else, go for it.\nINGREDIENTS\n3 large artichoke hearts\nSalt\nLots of extra virgin olive oil\n2 smashed garlic cloves\nJuice of 2 lemons\n1 tablespoon minced parsley\n1 tablespoon minced chives\nBlack pepper\nMETHOD\n1 Trim your artichokes: (see How to Trim an Artichoke). b"Save It Print\nAngel Hair Pasta with Salmon, Arugula, and Creamy Lemon-Parmesan Sauce Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 25 minutesYield: 6 servings\nINGREDIENTS\n2 tablespoons extra virgin olive oil, separated\n6 salmon fillets (2 1/2 to 3 ounces each, about 1 to 1 1/4 pounds total), preferably wild-caught King or Sockeye salmon\n2 1/4 teaspoon kosher salt, divided\n1 teaspoon ground black pepper, divided\n1 pound angel hair pasta\n4 tablespoons unsalted butter, separated\n1 tablespoon minced shallot\n4 garlic cloves, minced\n1 cup dry white wine or seafood stock\nJuice and rinds of 2 lemons (1/3 to 1/2 cup juice)\n2 cups heavy cream\n5 ounces arugula (4 packed cups)\n1 cup freshly grated Parmesan cheese\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Warm your oven: Set the oven to its lowest setting (mine is 150\xc2\xb0F) to keep the salmon warm once it's cooked.\n2 Start the water for pasta. Bring a large pot of salted water to boil.\n3 Season the salmon fillets: Rub both sides of the fillets with 1 teaspoon of the kosher salt and a 1/2 teaspoon of the black pepper.\n4 Sear the salmon: Heat 1 tablespoon of the olive oil over medium-high heat in a large saut\xc3\xa9 pan (preferably nonstick). Once the oil starts to ripple in the pan, place the salmon fillets into the pan, skin-side up.\nPress the fillets down gently to make sure the entire surface makes contact with the pan. Sear the salmon fillets for 3 minutes, or until the flesh turns an opaque pink 1/4 of the way up the sides of the fillets.\n5 Flip the salmon and keep it hot: Use a spatula to flip the salmon and sear it, skin-side down, for an additional 3 minutes.\nTransfer the fillets to a sheet pan and place them in the heated oven while you finish the dish. It\xe2\x80\x99s okay if the salmon is not cooked completely through just yet\xe2\x80\x94it will continue to cook in the oven.\n6 Cook the shallot and deglaze the pan: In the same pan you used to sear the salmon, heat the remaining tablespoon of olive oil and 2 tablespoons of the butter over medium-high heat. Add the shallot and the garlic to the pan and saut\xc3\xa9 for 3 minutes, or until glossy and fragrant.\nPour the white wine and lemon juice into the pan and use a wooden spoon to scrape up any bits of food that have stuck to the bottom of the pan. Add the lemon halves and bring the mixture to a boil.\n7 Reduce the sauce and cook the pasta: Reduce the sauce in the pan by half by maintaining a boil. This should take 3 to 4 minutes.\n8 Cook the pasta: By now, your pasta water should be at a rolling boil. Add generous tablespoon of salt to the boiling water and drop the pasta into the middle of the pot. Stir the pasta immediately to separate the noodles.\nLower the temperature slightly to prevent the water from boiling over and cook the pasta for 4 to 5 minutes, until al dente (or according to package directions). Drain the pasta.\n9 Finish the sauce:  Once the liquid in the pan has reduced by half, reduce the heat to medium-low. Remove the lemon halves. Slowly stir in the heavy cream and the remaining butter.\nAllow the sauce to come to a simmer, then add the arugula. Stir to coat the arugula in the sauce and allow it to wilt slightly\xe2\x80\x94this should only take a minute or so. Add the Parmesan, along with the remaining salt and pepper. Taste and adjust the seasoning, if necessary, by adding a bit more salt or pepper.\n10 Combine the pasta and sauce: Add the pasta to the pan with the sauce. Using tongs, toss in the pasta in the sauce until it is evenly coated.\n11 Serve the pasta with the salmon: Remove the warm salmon fillets from the oven and arrange on top of the pasta. Serve immediately. While this dish is best enjoyed the same day it\xe2\x80\x99s made, we have had success with reheating the leftovers in the microwave the next day.\nHello! b"Save It Print\nPasta with Tuna and Arugula Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 15 minutesYield: Serves 4\nWhile you are heating the pasta water, prep the ingredients.\nThis recipe requires tuna canned in olive oil. Tuna canned in water just doesn't work well with this recipe. If water canned tuna is your only option, drain it, and soak it in half a cup of good quality olive oil for an hour first.\nINGREDIENTS\n3/4 pound (12 ounces) dried fettuccine, spaghetti or linguine\n1/4 cup extra virgin olive oil\n2 cloves garlic, minced\n1/8 teaspoon hot red pepper flakes (more to taste)\n2 6-ounce cans tuna packed in olive oil, drained\nSalt\n5 to 8 ounces baby arugula\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Cook pasta: Bring a large pot of salted water (1 Tbsp salt for every 2 quarts of water) to a rolling boil. Add the pasta, return to a rolling boil, and boil uncovered until the pasta is al dente, cooked, but still a little firm to the bite.\n2 Cook garlic and red pepper flakes in olive oil; add tuna, salt: While the pasta is cooking, heat the olive oil in a large skillet on medium-low heat. Add the garlic and hot pepper flakes and cook until garlic is fragrant.\nAdd the tuna and shred it into fine flakes with a fork. Season with salt. Keep warm over low heat.\n3 Set aside a cup of pasta water: Just before the pasta is ready, set aside 1 cup of boiling water. b"Print\nGrilled Italian Sausage with Peppers, Onions and Arugula Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 20 minutesYield: Serves 4-6\nIf you don't have a grill, sear the onions and bell peppers in a little oil on high heat in a large, preferable cast iron, frying pan. Then lower the heat to medium low, add the sausages, and cook, turning the sausages occasionally, until the sausages are cooked through.\nTowards the end of cooking, baste with the honey balsamic mixture.\nINGREDIENTS\n1 large red onion, cut into wedges*\n2 large red bell peppers, seeded and cut into thirds\n1 pound sweet Italian sausage links\nExtra virgin olive oil\nSalt\n3 Tbsp honey\n3 Tbsp balsamic vinegar\n2 to 3 handfuls of baby arugula\n*Cut the onion wedges so that the root end is still intact on each wedge. It will make the onion wedges easier to grill and help keep them from falling apart on the grill.\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Preheat the grill.\n2 Mix together the balsamic vinegar and honey in a small bowl and set aside.\n3 Grill the onions: Coat the onions with a little olive oil, and sprinkle with salt. Coat the grill grates with a little olive oil. Put the onion wedges on the grill and cover the grill.\nLet the onions roast for 5 minutes, or until they are a little charred. Turn the onions and move them to a cooler part of the grill to finish.\n4 Grill the sausages and peppers: Coat the sausages and peppers with olive oil. Sprinkle salt on the peppers. If your grill has two levels, place the sausages on the top part of the grill and the peppers directly below them.\nDone this way, as the sausages drip juice and fat, it will fall on the peppers, flavoring them while simultaneously preventing flare-ups.\nIf your grill does not have two levels, put the peppers on the hottest part of the grill and the sausages on the coolest.\nCover and grill everything for 15 to 20 minutes or so, periodically checking and turning the sausages and peppers as needed.\n5 Baste with honey balsamic mixture: Towards the end of cooking, baste the sausages, peppers and onions with the honey and balsamic mixture.\n6 Remove from grill, cut sausages, cut peppers and onions: When the sausages are cooked through and the peppers and onions cooked, remove them from the grill to a sheet pan or large bowl.\nIf you want, pick off some or all of the charred skin on the peppers. Cut the peppers into long strips, and slice the root end off the onions to separate the pieces.\nCut the sausages into thirds. Mix everything well in the pan or bowl.\n7 Serve: To serve, place a bed of baby arugula on the serving plates and top with the sausage, peppers and onion.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint"

(You can also grill the shrimp if you prefer.)\nWhen the shrimp are barely cooked through, remove from the pan and set aside to cool. (The shrimp will continue to cook for a little bit after you remove them from the pan, and you don't want overcooked rubbery shrimp.)\n2 Assemble the salad: Put the drained beans, cut cherry tomatoes, diced onion, lemon zest, and arugula leaves into a large bowl. Fold in the shrimp.\n3 Make the dressing: In a small bowl, whisk together the red wine vinegar, olive oil, garlic, salt and pepper.\nGently fold the dressing into the salad and serve!\nHello! b'Print\nQuinoa, Arugula, and Feta Salad Recipe\nPrep time: 5 minutesCook time: 15 minutesYield: 4 servings\nINGREDIENTS\n1/2 cup (165 g) red quinoa\nScant 1 cup water (1 cup minus 1 tablespoon)\n1/4 teaspoon salt\n3 tablespoons olive oil\n5 ounces (8 loosely packed cups, 165 g) baby arugula\n2 tablespoons (30 ml) lemon juice, or more to taste\n8 ounces (110 g) firm feta, cut into 1/2-inch cubes\n1/4 teaspoon ground black pepper\nMETHOD\n1 Toast the quinoa: In a dry sauce pan over low heat, toast the quinoa, shaking the pan often, for 5 minutes, or until some of the grains start to turn a darker color.\n2 Cook the quinoa: Add the water and salt to the pan with the quinoa. Turn the heat to high and bring to a boil. Reduce the heat to low and cover the pan. Simmer for 15 minutes, or until the quinoa is tender when tasted and all the water is absorbed. If there\xe2\x80\x99s water in the pan, let the quinoa cook 2 minutes more.\n3 Cool the quinoa: Tip the quinoa into a large bowl and sprinkle with 1 tablespoon of the olive oil. Stir well and leave to cool, stirring occasionally. (Once cooled, the quinoa can be refrigerated for a few days before using.)\n4 Dress the arugula: In another bowl, toss the arugula with the remaining 2 tablespoons olive oil, 2 tablespoons of the lemon juice, and pepper.\n5 Toss the salad: Add the cooled quinoa and feta cubes to the bowl with the greens. Toss well and taste for seasoning. Add more salt or lemon juice, if you like. Serve immediately.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'

They hold their shape without becoming mushy, look pretty, and have a slightly chewy texture.\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the dressing:\n2 tablespoons sherry vinegar\n1 teaspoon coriander seeds, coarsely crushed in a mortar or with a rolling pin (or 1/2 teaspoon ground coriander)\n1 teaspoon ground sumac (optional), plus more for garnish\n1/8 teaspoon salt\nFresh black pepper\n5 tablespoons olive oil\nSalt and pepper to taste\nFor the salad:\n1 cup small dried lentils, such as French green lentils\nSalt and pepper to taste\n1/4 cup pine nuts\n1/4 red onion, thinly sliced\n1/4 cup dried currants\n1/4 cup chopped fresh cilantro\n2 bunches (about 6 cups) arugula\n12 cherry tomatoes, halved\n3 ounces (about 2/3 cup) feta cheese, crumbled\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Make the dressing:  In a bowl, whisk the vinegar, coriander and sumac (if using) with 1/8 teaspoon salt and a few grinds of fresh black pepper. b'Save It Print\nEasy Breakfast Casserole with Prosciutto Recipe\nPrep time: 25 minutesCook time: 45 minutesYield: 6 to 8\nYou can make and bake this savory strata all in one fell swoop, or assemble and refrigerate it the night before (but leave the cheese off until morning). Pull it out of the fridge 30 minutes before baking; add the cheese, and pop it into the oven.\nIf you have vegetarians at your table, feel free to skip the prosciutto and add one teaspoon of smoked paprika instead.\nThe strata holds up well as a leftover, so enjoy it for breakfast the next day, or pack up a slice for your desk lunch.\nINGREDIENTS\n1 tablespoon extra-virgin olive oil\n1 medium yellow onion, chopped\n2 big handfuls tender greens, such as arugula, dandelion greens, baby kale, or spinach (tough stems removed)\n1 1/2 cups asparagus, cut into 3/4-inch pieces\n1 teaspoon kosher salt, divided\n3 ounces thinly sliced prosciutto\n2 packed cups cubed crusty bread, such as levain, baguette, or Italian bread (slightly stale is ok)\n8 large eggs\n1 cup low fat cottage cheese\n1 cup 2% milk (or whatever kind you have in the fridge)\nFreshly ground black pepper\n1 1/2 cups (3 oz) grated cheddar, divided\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Preheat the oven to 350\xc2\xb0F.\n2 Saut\xc3\xa9 the vegetables: Add oil to a 12-inch ovenproof skillet set over medium heat. I use cast iron, but any ovenproof skillet will do.\nAdd the onion and saut\xc3\xa9 until tender, about 5 minutes. Add the greens, asparagus, and 1/2 teaspoon salt and saut\xc3\xa9 until the greens wilt, about 2 minutes. Remove from heat.\n3 Add the prosciutto and bread: Tear the prosciutto slices into smaller pieces and distribute over the vegetables. Add the bread and stir everything together. Leave that to cool while you whisk the eggs.\n4 Whisk the eggs: In a large bowl, whisk together the eggs, cottage cheese, milk, the remaining 3/4 teaspoon salt, and several generous grinds of black pepper. Add 1/2 cup of the cheese and stir again. Pour the eggs over the vegetables and scatter the remaining cheese on top.\n5 Bake the casserole: Place the casserole in the oven and bake until it is just set with no obvious liquid remaining, about 35 minutes. It should be a little jiggly. Keep in mind that it will continue to cook a bit once it\xe2\x80\x99s out of the oven.\n6 Serve: Cool for 10 minutes. Cut into wedges and serve.\nHello! b"Save It Print\nRadicchio Salad with Citrus Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 15 minutesYield: 4-6 servings\nFor this recipe, any variety of citrus will work\xe2\x80\x94you just need about two cups total of whatever you have on hand. It\xe2\x80\x99s best to supreme the citrus, which means to trim the peel off the citrus, then cut the individual segments of fruit from the inner membrane.\nINGREDIENTS\n3 slices (about 2 cups) sourdough bread, torn into bite-sized pieces\n1/4 cup plus 3 tablespoons extra-virgin olive oil, divided\n3/4 teaspoon kosher salt\n1/4 teaspoon ground black pepper\n1/2 cup chopped walnuts\n2 citrus fruits, like orange, lemon, and/or grapefruit\n1 small head radicchio (about 4 cups), cored and cut into bite-sized pieces\n2 cups arugula\n1/4 cup crumbled feta cheese\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Make the croutons: Heat the oven to 350\xcb\x9aF. Place the bread pieces on a rimmed baking sheet and toss with 1/4 cup olive oil. Sprinkle with 1/2 teaspoon salt and bake, tossing the bread on the baking sheet partway through, until golden and crunchy, about 15 minutes; let cool.\n2 Toast the nuts: While the croutons are in the oven, toast the nuts in a medium-sized skillet set over medium heat on the stovetop until fragrant and toasted, about 8-10 minutes. Stay near the pan, and stir the nuts occasionally. They can go from toasted to burnt in a matter of seconds. Let cool.\n3 Peel and segment (a.k.a. supreme) the citrus : For each fruit, cut about an inch off the top and bottom just so some of the flesh is exposed. Set the fruit with the cut-side down on a cutting board.\nStart at the top, and slice down the side of the fruit with a sharp knife, cutting away the peel and the pith, exposing the flesh. Then carefully cut out the citrus segments over a bowl to collect the juice. You should have about 1 cup of citrus segments.\n4 Squeeze the juice: Once all of the segments have been removed, squeeze the juice from what's left of the fruit into the same bowl. Drain the juice from the segments and keep separate.\n5 Make the citrus vinaigrette: In a mason jar or small bowl, combine 3 tablespoons of the reserved citrus juice with the remaining 3 tablespoons olive oil. Add pepper and the remaining 1/4 teaspoon salt. Secure the lid if using a jar, and shake vigorously for a few seconds until emulsified. If using a bowl, whisk the ingredients together.\n6 Assemble the salad: Add the radicchio and arugula to a large bowl. Drizzle with the vinaigrette and toss until evenly coated. Taste and season with additional salt and pepper to suit your preferences. Add the croutons, walnuts, citrus segments, and feta cheese, and toss until evenly combined.\n7 To serve: Transfer to a large serving bowl for family-style eating, or divide among individual bowls for serving.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"

Arrange on individual plates. Sprinkle with avocado. Lay on top several slices of chilled sliced steak. Sprinkle with pomegranate seeds or sliced kumquats if using.\n4 Make dressing: Mix together the lemon juice, olive oil, mustard, and salt and pepper to taste. Drizzle on salad.\nHello! Arrange the asparagus spears in a single layer on the lined roasting pan.\nDrizzle with olive oil and rub the spears all over with the olive oil to coat. Sprinkle with salt, pepper, and minced garlic, and rub over the asparagus spears to evenly distribute.\n3 Roast in oven: Roast at 400\xc2\xb0F (205\xc2\xb0C) for 10 minutes, more or less, depending on your particular oven and how thick the spears are, until the asparagus are just lightly browned and tender when you pierce them with a fork.\n4 Drizzle with lemon juice or balsamic to serve: To serve, drizzle with fresh lemon juice or balsamic vinegar, and if you want, a sprinkling of grated Parmesan cheese (skip if cooking vegan).\nHello! b'Save It Print\nProsciutto-Wrapped Asparagus Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 10 minutesYield: 4 to 6 servings\nProsciutto is naturally salty, so you shouldn\xe2\x80\x99t need to add any more salt to the asparagus.\nIf you want to make a bigger batch, just double up the ingredients in the recipe and use 2 large baking sheets for roasting.\nINGREDIENTS\n1 pound asparagus, preferably thick spears\n3 to 3 1/2 ounces sliced prosciutto\n1 to 2 tablespoons olive oil\nGround black pepper\nLemon zest, optional\nFreshly grated Parmesan cheese, optional\nMETHOD\n1 Heat the oven to 400F. This helps to ensure that the prosciutto wraps around the asparagus tightly.\nLay the wrapped asparagus spears on the lined sheet pan.\n4 Drizzle the asparagus with 1 to 2 tablespoons of olive oil. b'Save It Print\nFlank Steak Stir Fry with Asparagus and Red Pepper Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 25 minutesYield: Serves 4\nIf you are planning to serve this dish with rice, in a separate pan, prepare 2 cups of white rice, following the instructions on the rice package.\nINGREDIENTS\n3 Tbsp canola or peanut oil\n1/2 lb asparagus, trimmed, cut on the diagonal into 1 1/2 inch lengths (about 1 1/2 cups)\n1 lb of flank steak, sliced in half lengthwise (along the grain) and then cut into thin strips (across the grain), 2 inches long and 1/4 inch wide (put the steak in the freezer for 15 minutes before slicing to make it easier to slice)\n1 red bell pepper, seeded, de-ribbed, and cut into thin strips 2 inches long and 1/4 inch wide\n2 teaspoons of cornstarch dissolved into 3 Tablespoons of water\nStir Fry Sauce\n3 Tbsp soy sauce (use gluten-free soy sauce for gluten-free version)\n1 teaspoon finely chopped, peeled, fresh ginger\n1 small clove garlic, minced\n1 green onion, including green tops, chopped\n1/2 teaspoon chili oil\nMETHOD\n1 Blanch the asparagus: Fill a medium sized saucepan halfway with water and bring to a boil. Blanch the cut asparagus for 2 minutes. Drain, rinse with cold water to stop the cooking, and set aside.\n2 Assemble stir fry sauce: In a small dish, stir together the stir fry sauce ingredients\xe2\x80\x94soy sauce, chopped ginger, minced garlic, chopped green onion, chili oil\xe2\x80\x94and set aside.\n3 Stir fry asparagus: Heat 1 tablespoon of oil in a wok (or a thick-bottomed pot that can handle high heat) on high heat until shimmery. Add the asparagus and fry, stirring constantly, for 2 minutes or until lightly browned. Remove the asparagus from the pan and set aside.\n4 Stir fry beef strips: Heat another tablespoon of oil in the pan on high heat until shimmery. Stir fry the beef strips in batches, for 2 to 3 minutes per batch, until they are browned but still a little pink inside.\n5 Stir fry bell pepper: Return the first batches of beef strips to the pan along with the bell pepper strips. Stir and toss over high heat until the bell pepper strips are just beginning to wilt, 1-2 minutes.\n6 Add cornstarch slurry and stir fry sauce: Quickly stir the cornstarch liquid and add it to the pan along with the stir fry sauce. Cook until sauce thickens, 1-2 minutes.\nReturn the asparagus to the pan, toss to evenly coat and serve with steamed white rice (unless you are going low-carb, in which case, leave out the rice).\nHello! b'Save It Print\nAsparagus Risotto Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 35 minutesYield: Serves 2-3 as a main course, or 4 as a side\nIf you want to make this a vegetarian dish, use vegetable stock or water instead of the chicken stock.\nINGREDIENTS\nAbout 4 cups chicken stock (or vegetable stock for vegetarian option)\n2 Tbsp unsalted butter, divided\n1/2 cup chopped shallots\n1 cup arborio rice\n1/4 cup dry white wine (or 1 Tbsp lemon juice and 3 Tbsp water)\n1/2 pound asparagus, trimmed, tips cut off, tough skins of the spears peeled (if working with thick apparatus spears), and the spears cut into thin disks\n1/2 cup freshly grated Parmesan cheese\nSalt and pepper\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Heat the stock: Heat the stock in a small saucepan until it comes to a low simmer.\n2 Cook shallots in butter to soften, then add rice: In a separate 3 or 4 quart saucepan, heat 1 tablespoon butter on medium heat. Add the shallots and cook for a minute or two, until translucent. Add the arborio rice and cook for 2 minutes more, stirring until nicely coated.\n3 Add the white wine: Add the white wine. Slowly stir, allowing the rice to absorb the wine.\n4 Add the stock, 1/2 cup at a time, adding only after the previous addition has been absorbed by the rice: Once the wine is almost completely absorbed, add 1/2 cup of hot stock to the rice. Continue to stir until the liquid is almost completely absorbed, adding more stock in 1/2 cup increments. Stir often to prevent the rice from sticking to the bottom of the pan.\nContinue cooking and stirring rice, adding a little bit of broth at a time, cooking and stirring until it is absorbed, until the rice is tender, but still firm to the bite, about 20-25 minutes.\n5 Add the asparagus: With the last ladle of stock, add the asparagus. Stir and cook for a couple of minutes, until the risotto has absorbed the stock, but is still loose, and the asparagus are just cooked through.\nNote the stock amount given is approximate. You may need a little more or less. If you end up needing more stock and you find yourself without, just use water.\n6 Stir in the Parmesan, remaining butter, add salt, pepper: Turn off the heat. Gently stir in the Parmesan cheese and the remaining 1 tablespoon butter. Add salt and pepper to taste. Serve immediately.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'

b"Save It Print\nCreamy Asparagus Soup Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 30 minutesYield: Serves 4-6\nWant more vibrant green in the soup? Stir in a handful of chopped baby spinach in step 5 with the parsley.\nMake sure to use heavy cream or full-fat sour cream, or the soup may curdle. Cooking light? Skip the cream all together.\nThe vermouth really makes this soup shine. If you don't have any, try adding a 1/4 cup of white wine to the pot after you saut\xc3\xa9 the onions and garlic. Let it bubble up and reduce by half before adding the asparagus. Otherwise skip.\nINGREDIENTS\n2 lbs asparagus, trimmed of woody stem bottoms\n1 large yellow onion, chopped (1 1/2 to 2 cups chopped)\n1 teaspoon minced garlic, or 1 Tbsp minced green garlic\n3 Tbsp butter\n4 cups chicken broth or vegetable broth (vegetarian option)\n1 cup water\n2 sprigs of fresh thyme\n1 bay leaf\n1/4 cup chopped fresh parsley\n1/4 cup heavy cream or full-fat sour cream\n1 Tbsp dry vermouth\n1 teaspoon lemon juice\n1/2 teaspoon black pepper (more to taste)\n1 teaspoon salt (more to taste)\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Cut asparagus tips and reserve, cut the rest of asparagus into 1/4-inch rounds: Cut tips from the asparagus 1 1/2 inches from top and reserve. Chop the rest of the asparagus stalks into 1/4-inch rounds.\n2 Saut\xc3\xa9 onions, garlic: Melt the butter in a 4 to 5 quart pot on medium heat. Add the onions and cook until translucent, about 5 minutes.\nAdd the garlic (or green garlic) and cook a minute more.\n3 Add asparagus: Add the chopped asparagus (not the spear tips) to the onions. Sprinkle with salt and pepper to taste. Cook another 5 minutes.\n4 Add the broth, water, thyme sprigs and bay leaf to the pot. Increase the heat to a boil, then reduce to a simmer. Simmer, covered, until the asparagus are tender, about 10 minutes.\n5 At the end of cooking, stir in the chopped parsley.\n6 Blanch asparagus tips: While the soup is cooking, blanche the asparagus tips in a small pot of boiling, salted water, until the tips are just tender, about 2-4 minutes, depending on the size of the asparagus.\nDrain. Rinse with cool water to stop the cooking. Set aside.\n7 Pur\xc3\xa9e the soup: Remove bay leaf and thyme sprigs. Use either an immersion blender or an upright blender (working in batches) to pur\xc3\xa9e the soup. If you use an upright blender, work in small batches, fill no more than a third the blender bowl at a time, and hold down the lid while blending.\nFor a creamy texture, if you want, press the pur\xc3\xa9ed soup through a sieve or food mill.\n8 Stir in cream, vermouth, lemon juice: Stir in the cream (or full-fat sour cream). Stir in the vermouth and lemon juice. Season with salt and pepper to taste.\nGarnish with asparagus tips.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b'Save It Print\nHam and Asparagus Quiche Recipe\nPrep time: 1 hour, 30 minutesCook time: 30 minutesYield: Serves 6 to 8\nINGREDIENTS\n1 recipe pie dough, enough for one bottom crust (see P\xc3\xa2te Bris\xc3\xa9e recipe)\n2 tablespoons extra virgin olive oil\n2 medium shallots, thinly sliced\n10 ounces asparagus spears, cut on the diagonal into 1-inch long pieces\n1/2 pound ham, cut into 1/4-inch cubes\nFreshly ground pepper\n1/2 cup milk\n1/2 cup heavy cream\n3 large eggs\n6 ounces Gruy\xc3\xa8re cheese, grated (1 1/2 cups)\nSpecial equipment:\n10-inch tart pan\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Roll out dough and fit into tart pan, then freeze: On a lightly floured surface, roll out dough into a 12-inch circle. Transfer to freezer to chill for 30 minutes.\n2 Pre-bake tart crust: Preheat oven to 350\xc2\xb0F. Line pastry with aluminum foil, pressing into the corners and edges. Fill to the top with baking weights \xe2\x80\x94 sugar, dried beans, or rice.\nBake for 45 minutes. Lift sides of aluminum foil to remove pie weights from tart pan. Spread asparagus and ham over the cheese and then top with remaining cheese.\nIn a medium bowl, whisk together milk, cream, and eggs. Season with fresh ground pepper. Pour over cheese.\n5 Bake: Transfer to oven, and bake at 375\xc2\xb0F until just set in the center, 30 to 35 minutes. Cool on a wire rack for about 10 minutes before slicing.\nHello! b'Print\nHow to Cook Asparagus Sous Vide Recipe\nPrep time: 5 minutesCook time: 10 minutesYield: 4 servings\nINGREDIENTS\n1 bunch asparagus, about 1 pound\n1/2 teaspoon black pepper\n2 tablespoons olive oil or unsalted butter\nZest and juice of one lemon\nSea salt for garnish\nSpecial equipment:\nSous vide immersion circulator\nGallon-sized zip-top freezer bags\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Heat the water: Fill a pot with water and place your immersion circulator inside. Set your immersion circulator to 180\xc2\xb0F and let the water come up to temperature.\n2 Prep the asparagus: Wash the asparagus and, like a bunch of flowers, make a fresh cut on the bottom, eliminating any of the tough, woody ends.\nAdd the asparagus to a zip-top, gallon-sized plastic freezer bag. Add the black pepper and olive oil; save the salt for after it\xe2\x80\x99s cooked, as the salt will turn this green veggie a little grey. Toss together in the bag to distribute the ingredients.\nAdd a few heavy soup spoons to the bag to help weigh it down. This will help keep the asparagus submerged, which will ensure that it cooks evenly.\n  3 Seal the bag: Seal the bag as tightly as possible by using water-displacement method to help press out all the air. Just put the food in the bag and slowly lower it into the water, letting the pressure of the water press the air through the top of the bag. Once the air is out of the bag, seal it just above the water line. (Read more here.)\nYou can do this in the pot of water as it heats\xe2\x80\x94just be careful if the water is already steaming!\n4 Cook the asparagus: Once the water has come up to temperature, submerge the bag of asparagus in the pot of water. Make sure the bag is completely submerged (if it floats, remove it from the water and add a few more spoons to weigh it down).\n* Check the asparagus after 6 to 7 minutes if it\xe2\x80\x99s pencil thin.\n* Check average or thick asparagus after 8 to 10 minutes.\nIf you\xe2\x80\x99re at all in doubt, pull them out after 8 minutes, open the bag carefully, and use a fork to determine how tender the spears are. If the fork is getting stuck in the asparagus, it\xe2\x80\x99s not ready; reseal the bag and return it to the water for another minute or two.\n5 Serve: Remove from the water, turn off the circulator and serve immediately. Sprinkle some lemon juice and zest over the top of the asparagus, along with some of the cooking oil or butter (if desired) and some flaky sea salt, such as Maldon.\nLeftover asparagus will keep refrigerated for about 5 days.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'
b'Save It Print\nSteamed Asparagus with Hollandaise Sauce Recipe\nPrep time: 5 minutesCook time: 15 minutesYield: Serves 4\nINGREDIENTS\n1 bunch of asparagus (about 1 lb)\n10 Tbsp unsalted butter (1 stick plus 2 Tbsp)\n3 egg yolks\n1 Tbsp lemon juice\n1/2 teaspoon salt (skip if using salted butter)\nPinch of cayenne\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Prep the asparagus: Break off the tough ends with your fingers. Bend the asparagus spears near the end and they will break naturally where the spear is no longer tough.\nFor an elegant presentation of the spears, use a vegetable peeler to peel off a very thin layer of the outer skin of the lower two to three inches of the asparagus spears.\nPrepare a large, shallow pan (with a cover) with a half inch of water and a steamer rack.\n2 Prepare the Hollandaise sauce: Melt the butter in a small pot. Put the egg yolks, lemon juice, salt and cayenne into a blender.\nBlend the eggs for 20-30 seconds at medium to medium high speed until lighter in color.\nTurn blender down to lowest setting and slowly drizzle in the hot melted butter while the blender is going. Continue to blend for a few seconds after all of the butter is incorporated.\nTaste the sauce and add more salt or lemon juice if needed. Keep warm while you are steaming the asparagus.\n3 Steam the asparagus: Bring the water in your steaming pan to a boil. Place the asparagus on the steaming rack. Cover.\nSteam for 3 to 5 minutes, until tender, but still a little crisp, definitely not mushy. The timing depends on how thick the asparagus spears are.\n4 Serve: To serve, plate the asparagus. Pour Hollandaise sauce over them.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'
b'Print\nAsparagus Artichoke Breakfast Casserole Recipe\nPrep time: 25 minutesCook time: 40 minutesYield: Serves 6 to 8\nINGREDIENTS\n6 cups of 1 to 1 1/2-inch cubed rustic bread (about half a loaf), or 6 slices of bread\n2 ounces bacon (2 to 3 thick-cut slices), roughly chopped\n1 medium onion, chopped (about 1 1/2 cups)\n1 pound of asparagus, trimmed of tough bottoms, spears sliced on the diagonal, in 1-inch long pieces\n1 15-ounce can of artichoke hearts (packed in water), drained, chopped\n2 Tbsp minced chives or green onion greens\n6 eggs\n2 cups milk\n8 ounces cheddar cheese, grated\n1 1/2 teaspoons salt\n1/4 teaspoon black pepper\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Dry cubed bread in oven: Place cubed bread on a baking sheet, put in a 200\xc2\xb0F for 10 to 15 minutes, until somewhat dry. Gently fold in the onions, bacon, asparagus, chopped artichoke hearts, and chives. (Be gentle as to not break up the bread.)\n8 Assemble the casserole: Generously butter the inside of a 2 1/2 to 3 quart (8 x 13 inch) casserole dish. Gently pour the bread egg milk vegetable mixture into the casserole dish and spread out in an even layer.\nAt this point you can make up to a day ahead. Cover and refrigerate until ready to cook.\n9 Bake: Bake uncovered at 350\xc2\xb0F for 4o minutes. If the casserole starts to get too browned while cooking, cover with foil. Remove from oven and let rest for 5 minutes before serving.\n  Hello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'

If the top is getting too brown before the custard is done, you can tent it with foil. Remove from oven and let cool for 5 minutes before cutting to serve.\nHello! b'Save It Print\nRoasted Asparagus Recipe\nPrep time: 6 minutesCook time: 12 minutesYield: Serves 4\nFor best results for roasting asparagus, use thick asparagus spears, not skinny ones. b'Save It Print\nProsciutto-Wrapped Asparagus Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 10 minutesYield: 4 to 6 servings\nProsciutto is naturally salty, so you shouldn\xe2\x80\x99t need to add any more salt to the asparagus.\nIf you want to make a bigger batch, just double up the ingredients in the recipe and use 2 large baking sheets for roasting.\nINGREDIENTS\n1 pound asparagus, preferably thick spears\n3 to 3 1/2 ounces sliced prosciutto\n1 to 2 tablespoons olive oil\nGround black pepper\nLemon zest, optional\nFreshly grated Parmesan cheese, optional\nMETHOD\n1 Heat the oven to 400F. Wrap each spear of asparagus with one strip of sliced prosciutto. Tug the prosciutto a little as you wrap it around the asparagus to give it tension. This helps to ensure that the prosciutto wraps around the asparagus tightly.\nLay the wrapped asparagus spears on the lined sheet pan.\n4 Drizzle the asparagus with 1 to 2 tablespoons of olive oil. Sprinkle a pinch of black pepper on top.\n5 Bake the asparagus for 8 to 10 minutes. b'Save It Print\nFlank Steak Stir Fry with Asparagus and Red Pepper Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 25 minutesYield: Serves 4\nIf you are planning to serve this dish with rice, in a separate pan, prepare 2 cups of white rice, following the instructions on the rice package.\nINGREDIENTS\n3 Tbsp canola or peanut oil\n1/2 lb asparagus, trimmed, cut on the diagonal into 1 1/2 inch lengths (about 1 1/2 cups)\n1 lb of flank steak, sliced in half lengthwise (along the grain) and then cut into thin strips (across the grain), 2 inches long and 1/4 inch wide (put the steak in the freezer for 15 minutes before slicing to make it easier to slice)\n1 red bell pepper, seeded, de-ribbed, and cut into thin strips 2 inches long and 1/4 inch wide\n2 teaspoons of cornstarch dissolved into 3 Tablespoons of water\nStir Fry Sauce\n3 Tbsp soy sauce (use gluten-free soy sauce for gluten-free version)\n1 teaspoon finely chopped, peeled, fresh ginger\n1 small clove garlic, minced\n1 green onion, including green tops, chopped\n1/2 teaspoon chili oil\nMETHOD\n1 Blanch the asparagus: Fill a medium sized saucepan halfway with water and bring to a boil. Blanch the cut asparagus for 2 minutes. Drain, rinse with cold water to stop the cooking, and set aside.\n2 Assemble stir fry sauce: In a small dish, stir together the stir fry sauce ingredients\xe2\x80\x94soy sauce, chopped ginger, minced garlic, chopped green onion, chili oil\xe2\x80\x94and set aside.\n3 Stir fry asparagus: Heat 1 tablespoon of oil in a wok (or a thick-bottomed pot that can handle high heat) on high heat until shimmery. Add the asparagus and fry, stirring constantly, for 2 minutes or until lightly browned. Remove the asparagus from the pan and set aside.\n4 Stir fry beef strips: Heat another tablespoon of oil in the pan on high heat until shimmery. Stir fry the beef strips in batches, for 2 to 3 minutes per batch, until they are browned but still a little pink inside.\n5 Stir fry bell pepper: Return the first batches of beef strips to the pan along with the bell pepper strips. Stir and toss over high heat until the bell pepper strips are just beginning to wilt, 1-2 minutes.\n6 Add cornstarch slurry and stir fry sauce: Quickly stir the cornstarch liquid and add it to the pan along with the stir fry sauce. Cook until sauce thickens, 1-2 minutes.\nReturn the asparagus to the pan, toss to evenly coat and serve with steamed white rice (unless you are going low-carb, in which case, leave out the rice).\nHello! b'Save It Print\nAsparagus Risotto Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 35 minutesYield: Serves 2-3 as a main course, or 4 as a side\nIf you want to make this a vegetarian dish, use vegetable stock or water instead of the chicken stock.\nINGREDIENTS\nAbout 4 cups chicken stock (or vegetable stock for vegetarian option)\n2 Tbsp unsalted butter, divided\n1/2 cup chopped shallots\n1 cup arborio rice\n1/4 cup dry white wine (or 1 Tbsp lemon juice and 3 Tbsp water)\n1/2 pound asparagus, trimmed, tips cut off, tough skins of the spears peeled (if working with thick apparatus spears), and the spears cut into thin disks\n1/2 cup freshly grated Parmesan cheese\nSalt and pepper\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Heat the stock: Heat the stock in a small saucepan until it comes to a low simmer.\n2 Cook shallots in butter to soften, then add rice: In a separate 3 or 4 quart saucepan, heat 1 tablespoon butter on medium heat. Add the shallots and cook for a minute or two, until translucent. Add the arborio rice and cook for 2 minutes more, stirring until nicely coated.\n3 Add the white wine: Add the white wine. Slowly stir, allowing the rice to absorb the wine.\n4 Add the stock, 1/2 cup at a time, adding only after the previous addition has been absorbed by the rice: Once the wine is almost completely absorbed, add 1/2 cup of hot stock to the rice. Continue to stir until the liquid is almost completely absorbed, adding more stock in 1/2 cup increments. Stir often to prevent the rice from sticking to the bottom of the pan.\nContinue cooking and stirring rice, adding a little bit of broth at a time, cooking and stirring until it is absorbed, until the rice is tender, but still firm to the bite, about 20-25 minutes.\n5 Add the asparagus: With the last ladle of stock, add the asparagus. Stir and cook for a couple of minutes, until the risotto has absorbed the stock, but is still loose, and the asparagus are just cooked through.\nNote the stock amount given is approximate. You may need a little more or less. If you end up needing more stock and you find yourself without, just use water.\n6 Stir in the Parmesan, remaining butter, add salt, pepper: Turn off the heat. Gently stir in the Parmesan cheese and the remaining 1 tablespoon butter. Add salt and pepper to taste. Serve immediately.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. b"Save It Print\nCreamy Asparagus Soup Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 30 minutesYield: Serves 4-6\nWant more vibrant green in the soup? Stir in a handful of chopped baby spinach in step 5 with the parsley.\nMake sure to use heavy cream or full-fat sour cream, or the soup may curdle. Cooking light? Skip the cream all together.\nThe vermouth really makes this soup shine. If you don't have any, try adding a 1/4 cup of white wine to the pot after you saut\xc3\xa9 the onions and garlic. Let it bubble up and reduce by half before adding the asparagus. Otherwise skip.\nINGREDIENTS\n2 lbs asparagus, trimmed of woody stem bottoms\n1 large yellow onion, chopped (1 1/2 to 2 cups chopped)\n1 teaspoon minced garlic, or 1 Tbsp minced green garlic\n3 Tbsp butter\n4 cups chicken broth or vegetable broth (vegetarian option)\n1 cup water\n2 sprigs of fresh thyme\n1 bay leaf\n1/4 cup chopped fresh parsley\n1/4 cup heavy cream or full-fat sour cream\n1 Tbsp dry vermouth\n1 teaspoon lemon juice\n1/2 teaspoon black pepper (more to taste)\n1 teaspoon salt (more to taste)\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Cut asparagus tips and reserve, cut the rest of asparagus into 1/4-inch rounds: Cut tips from the asparagus 1 1/2 inches from top and reserve. Chop the rest of the asparagus stalks into 1/4-inch rounds.\n2 Saut\xc3\xa9 onions, garlic: Melt the butter in a 4 to 5 quart pot on medium heat. Add the onions and cook until translucent, about 5 minutes.\nAdd the garlic (or green garlic) and cook a minute more.\n3 Add asparagus: Add the chopped asparagus (not the spear tips) to the onions. Sprinkle with salt and pepper to taste. Cook another 5 minutes.\n4 Add the broth, water, thyme sprigs and bay leaf to the pot. Increase the heat to a boil, then reduce to a simmer. Simmer, covered, until the asparagus are tender, about 10 minutes.\n5 At the end of cooking, stir in the chopped parsley.\n6 Blanch asparagus tips: While the soup is cooking, blanche the asparagus tips in a small pot of boiling, salted water, until the tips are just tender, about 2-4 minutes, depending on the size of the asparagus.\nDrain. Rinse with cool water to stop the cooking. Set aside.\n7 Pur\xc3\xa9e the soup: Remove bay leaf and thyme sprigs. Use either an immersion blender or an upright blender (working in batches) to pur\xc3\xa9e the soup. If you use an upright blender, work in small batches, fill no more than a third the blender bowl at a time, and hold down the lid while blending.\nFor a creamy texture, if you want, press the pur\xc3\xa9ed soup through a sieve or food mill.\n8 Stir in cream, vermouth, lemon juice: Stir in the cream (or full-fat sour cream). Stir in the vermouth and lemon juice. Season with salt and pepper to taste.\nGarnish with asparagus tips.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"

b'Save It Print\nHow to Cook Asparagus Sous Vide Recipe\nPrep time: 5 minutesCook time: 10 minutesYield: 4 servings\nINGREDIENTS\n1 bunch asparagus, about 1 pound\n1/2 teaspoon black pepper\n2 tablespoons olive oil or unsalted butter\nZest and juice of one lemon\nSea salt for garnish\nSpecial equipment:\nSous vide immersion circulator\nGallon-sized zip-top freezer bags\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Heat the water: Fill a pot with water and place your immersion circulator inside. Set your immersion circulator to 180\xc2\xb0F and let the water come up to temperature.\n2 Prep the asparagus: Wash the asparagus and, like a bunch of flowers, make a fresh cut on the bottom, eliminating any of the tough, woody ends.\nAdd the asparagus to a zip-top, gallon-sized plastic freezer bag. Add the black pepper and olive oil; save the salt for after it\xe2\x80\x99s cooked, as the salt will turn this green veggie a little grey. Toss together in the bag to distribute the ingredients.\nAdd a few heavy soup spoons to the bag to help weigh it down. This will help keep the asparagus submerged, which will ensure that it cooks evenly.\n  3 Seal the bag: Seal the bag as tightly as possible by using water-displacement method to help press out all the air. Just put the food in the bag and slowly lower it into the water, letting the pressure of the water press the air through the top of the bag. Once the air is out of the bag, seal it just above the water line. (Read more here.)\nYou can do this in the pot of water as it heats\xe2\x80\x94just be careful if the water is already steaming!\n4 Cook the asparagus: Once the water has come up to temperature, submerge the bag of asparagus in the pot of water. Make sure the bag is completely submerged (if it floats, remove it from the water and add a few more spoons to weigh it down).\n* Check the asparagus after 6 to 7 minutes if it\xe2\x80\x99s pencil thin.\n* Check average or thick asparagus after 8 to 10 minutes.\nIf you\xe2\x80\x99re at all in doubt, pull them out after 8 minutes, open the bag carefully, and use a fork to determine how tender the spears are. If the fork is getting stuck in the asparagus, it\xe2\x80\x99s not ready; reseal the bag and return it to the water for another minute or two.\n5 Serve: Remove from the water, turn off the circulator and serve immediately. Sprinkle some lemon juice and zest over the top of the asparagus, along with some of the cooking oil or butter (if desired) and some flaky sea salt, such as Maldon.\nLeftover asparagus will keep refrigerated for about 5 days.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'

b"Save It Print\nSheet Pan Chicken with Asparagus and Potatoes Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 1 hour, 30 minutesYield: 4 servings\nIf you can't find the chicken parts called for in this recipe, you can buy a whole chicken and cut it into parts yourself (or ask a butcher to do it for you).\nIf you don't have fresh herbs, you can substitute dried thyme. Use 1/2 teaspoon of dried thyme with the vegetables and 1/2 teaspoon sprinkled over the chicken.\nINGREDIENTS\n16 small new potatoes (red or golden), halved\n3 small sweet onions (such as Vidalia or Walla Walla), quartered through the roots; or 1 large super sweet onion, cut into thin wedges\n1 medium lemon, very thinly sliced\nLarge handful fresh lemon thyme or other fresh herb (oregano, marjoram, or thyme).\n5 tablespoons olive oil\n1 teaspoon salt, or more to taste\n1/2 teaspoon black pepper, or more to taste\n2 large bone-in chicken breast halves (1 1/2 pounds, 680 g)\n2 whole chicken legs, thighs and drumsticks attached; or 2 legs and 2 drumsticks (1/2 pounds, 227 g)\n1 bunch (1 pound) fresh asparagus\nSpecial equipment:\nSheet pan, at least 11-by-17 inches or larger\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Prepare the vegetables for roasting: Heat the oven to 375F. In a bowl, combine the new potatoes, onions, lemon, a few of the herb sprigs, 2 tablespoons of the olive oil, and half the salt and pepper. Toss well and spread on a rimmed baking sheet.\n2 Roast the vegetables for 40 minutes, or until the potatoes are almost tender when pierced with a skewer.\n3 Prepare the chicken: While the vegetables roast, sprinkle the chicken with 2 tablespoons of the remaining olive oil, and the remaining salt and pepper. Remove the leaves from several thyme springs and scatter them on the chicken.\n4 Add the chicken to the vegetables and roast: Move the vegetables in the pan aside to make room for the chicken. Set the chicken in the pan, skin side up, so it isn\xe2\x80\x99t sitting on vegetables. Continue cooking for 30 minutes.\n5 Prepare the asparagus: Snap the spears near the base, where they break without much effort. Cut the spears in half to make shorter lengths. In a bowl, toss the asparagus with the remaining 1 tablespoon oil.\n6 Add the asparagus and roast: After the chicken has been roasting for 30 minutes, pull out the sheet pan and scatter the asparagus around the chicken.\n7 Continue roasting for 10 to 20 minutes, or until the chicken pieces all register at least 165\xc2\xb0F in the thickest part of the meat on an instant-read thermometer (the thighs will cook slightly faster than the breasts; you can pull them off the sheet pan as they reach temperature and keep them on a plate covered with foil, if you like).\nAll of the vegetables should also be cooked through. (Total cooking time is roughly 1 1/2 hours.)\nIf your chicken isn\xe2\x80\x99t brown enough, slide the pan under the broiler for 2 minutes, watching it carefully to avoid burning.\n8 To serve the chicken: Discard the cooked thyme sprigs. Use kitchen shears to separate the legs to form 2 drumsticks and 2 thighs. Snip the breasts in half horizontally.\nArrange the chicken and vegetables on a platter. b'Save It Print\nBreakfast Casserole with Leeks and Asparagus Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 1 hour, 30 minutesYield: Serves 6 to 8\nPro tip: raw bacon is much easier to slice if it is frozen. So keep your bacon chilled until you are ready to cut it, or put it in the freezer for several minutes before slicing.\nINGREDIENTS\n3 slices thick-sliced bacon (about 3 ounces), cut into 1/2-inch pieces\n1 pound of asparagus, trimmed of woody ends, cut into 1/2-inch diagonal pieces\n6 slices of bread, cut into 1 1/2 inch wide square pieces, including crusts\n2 leeks, cleaned, cut in half lengthwise, sliced crosswise into 1/2-inch pieces, white and light green parts only, about 2 cups total\n2 Tbsp butter, divided 1 Tbsp and 1 Tbsp\n1/2 cup of crumbled feta cheese\n8 eggs\n2 cups milk\n1/2 teaspoon of dried herbes de provence (can sub dried tarragon or thyme)\n1 teaspoon kosher salt\n1/8 teaspoon freshly ground black pepper\n1/4 cup of freshly grated Parmesan cheese\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Place bacon in a medium skillet on medium heat. Gently cook, turning occasionally, until the bacon pieces are lightly browned and much of the bacon fat has been rendered, about 10-12 minutes. Remove cooked bacon from the pan with a slotted spoon, leaving the rendered bacon fat in the pan.\n2 While the bacon is cooking, cut up the bread. If the bread is a little stale, great. If it is fresh, then spread it out on a baking sheet and heat it in a 200\xc2\xb0F oven for about 10-15 minutes to help it dry out a bit. This will help the keep the bread from disintegrating when mixed with the eggs later.\n3 Bring a small pot of water to a boil. Add the cut asparagus and blanch for 1 minute. Remove the asparagus from the pot to a bowl of ice water. Let cool in the ice water and then drain.\n4 Once the bacon is done and removed from the pan add a tablespoon of butter to the pan with the remaining bacon fat. Add the leeks and gently cook on medium to medium low heat for 10-12 minutes until the leeks are softened, but not browned. Do not let brown.\n5 In a large bowl, whisk together the eggs, milk, crumbled feta cheese, herbes de provence, salt, and pepper.\n6 Place the bread pieces into the egg milk mixture and press down so that the bread becomes completely saturated with the mixture. Add the asparagus and leeks and gently mix to combine, taking care to not break up the bread.\n7 Preheat oven to 350\xc2\xb0F. With the remaining tablespoon of butter, butter the insides of a 9x13-inch casserole dish. Sprinkle the bacon over the bottom of the dish. Gently pour the filling mixture into the casserole. Top with Parmesan cheese. Push the grated Parmesan down a bit into to the top of the casserole so that it gets moistened. (At this point you can make the night before, refrigerate and bake the next morning.)\n8 Bake, uncovered, for 45 minutes or until the top is lightly browned and the custard is cooked through. If the top is getting too brown before the custard is done, you can tent it with foil. Remove from oven and let cool for 5 minutes before cutting to serve.\nHello! Check the directions on the pasta package. b'Save It Print\nAsparagus Quiche with Fontina Cheese Recipe\nPrep time: 30 minutesCook time: 40 minutesChilling time: 1 hourYield: 4 to 6 servings\nINGREDIENTS\n1 9-inch pie crust, chilled for 30 minutes and ready to roll out\nFlour (for sprinkling)\n1 pound (445 g) fresh asparagus\n1/4 pound Fontina cheese, cut into 1/4-inch cubes\n4 large eggs, lightly beaten in a large bowl\n1 cup heavy cream\n1/2 teaspoon salt\n1/4 teaspoon black pepper\nSpecial equipment:\n9 1/2- or 10-inch porcelain or metal tart pan\nPie weights or dried beans for baking\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Roll out the pie crust: Roll out the pie crust on a lightly floured counter to an 11-inch round, moving it often to prevent it from sticking.\nLift it onto the rolling pin and gently ease it into a 9 1/2 or 10-inch porcelain tart pan. Press the dough all around the bottom edge so it sticks to the pan. With scissors, cut the pastry around the top edge so it has an even 1-inch overhang.\n2 Crimp the dough: Tuck the overhang inside the pan all around, like a hem. Crimp the top edge with your fingers.\n3 Chill the pie crust: Set the pie crust on a rimmed baking sheet. Cover loosely with plastic wrap and freeze for 1 hour. (At this point, you can freeze it overnight, loosely covered; if you want to freeze for up to 1 month, wrap tightly after the crust is frozen).\n4 Blind bake the pie crust: Heat the oven to 375F. Prick the dough all over with a fork. Line the dough with parchment paper or crumpled foil, and fill with pie weights or dried beans.\nBake for 12 to 15 minutes, or until the top edge of the pastry is beginning to take on some color. Lift off the paper or foil and beans, and set aside. Return the pie crust to the oven and continue baking for 5 to 10 minutes, or until the bottom of the dough is beginning to cook through. If the dough forms puffs, prick them with the tip of a knife.\nSet on a wire rack to cool. Leave the oven on.\n5 Prepare the asparagus: Snap off the dry and woody part of the spears near the base, where they break without much effort. Cut the spears into 1-inch pieces.\nBring a saucepan of water to a boil. Add the asparagus and cook for 1 minute. Drain and transfer the asparagus to ice water to cool.\nDry the asparagus with paper towels. Set aside 3 asparagus tips to garnish the quiche. Halve the remaining pieces lengthwise.\n6 Finish the filling: Scatter the blanched asparagus (not the tips) and Fontina over the bottom of the cooled pie crust. Thoroughly stir the cream into the eggs, add salt and pepper, and pour the egg mixture over the asparagus and cheese.\n7 Bake the quiche: Return the pan to the oven and bake for 35 to 40 minutes, or until the filling is set all over and the top is starting to brown. Set on a wire rack to cool completely.\n8 Serve: Garnish the top of the quiche with the reserved asparagus tips before serving.\nThe quiche can be served immediately, or once cool, cover and refrigerate for up to 5 days. Quiche can be served cold, room temperature, or warm. (If serving warm, heat in a 300F oven until just warm to the touch.)\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'
b"Print\nHow to Make Perfect Guacamole Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesYield: Serves 2-4\nBe careful handling chiles if using. Wash your hands thoroughly after handling and do not touch your eyes or the area near your eyes with your hands for several hours.\nINGREDIENTS\n2 ripe avocados\n1/4 teaspoon of salt, more to taste\n1 tablespoon fresh lime juice or lemon juice\n2 tablespoons to 1/4 cup of minced red onion or thinly sliced green onion\n1-2 serrano chiles, stems and seeds removed, minced\n2 tablespoons cilantro (leaves and tender stems), finely chopped\nA dash of freshly grated black pepper\n1/2 ripe tomato, seeds and pulp removed, chopped\nRed radishes or jicama, to garnish\nTortilla chips, to serve\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Cut the avocado, remove flesh: Cut the avocados in half. Remove the pit. Score the inside of the avocado with a blunt knife and scoop out the flesh with a spoon. (See How to Cut and Peel an Avocado.) Place in a bowl.\n2 Mash with a fork: Using a fork, roughly mash the avocado. (Don't overdo it! The guacamole should be a little chunky.)\n3 Add salt, lime juice, and the rest: Sprinkle with salt and lime (or lemon) juice. The acid in the lime juice will provide some balance to the richness of the avocado and will help delay the avocados from turning brown.\nAdd the chopped onion, cilantro, black pepper, and chiles. Chili peppers vary individually in their hotness. So, start with a half of one chili pepper and add to the guacamole to your desired degree of hotness.\nRemember that much of this is done to taste because of the variability in the fresh ingredients. Start with this recipe and adjust to your taste.\nChilling tomatoes hurts their flavor, so if you want to add chopped tomato to your guacamole, add it just before serving.\n4 Serve: Serve immediately, or if making a few hours ahead, place plastic wrap on the surface of the guacamole and press down to cover it and to prevent air reaching it. (The oxygen in the air causes oxidation which will turn the guacamole brown.) Refrigerate until ready to serve.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint"
b"Print\nHow to Cut and Peel an Avocado\nPrep time: 1 minute\nINGREDIENTS\n1 avocado\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Grip the avocado gently on one side with one hand. With a large, sharp knife in the other hand, cut the avocado lengthwise around the seed. Open the two halves to expose the pit.\n2a At this point there are a few ways you can proceed to remove the pit from the avocado half that has the pit. One way is to use a spoon to scoop out the pit.\nOne way is to make another cut, lengthwise on the avocado half that has the pit, cutting around the pit, exposing it so that it is easier to remove.\n2b Another method is a bit tricky, as you'll see. This method is very popular, but you must be careful lest you cut your hand. For safety, fold up a kitchen towel and use that to hold the avocado half with the pit.\nGently tap the pit with a knife with enough force so that the knife edge wedges into the pit, but not so hard as to cut all the way through it. If unsure, just tap it very gently a few times, each time with increasing pressure, until a cut is made in the pit sufficiently to twist the pit out. Getting the pressure just right takes a little practice.\nWith the edge of the knife, twist the pit out of the avocado and discard.\n3a At this point, you can either scoop out the avocado flesh with a spoon (for making guacamole), or slice the avocado into segments.\nTo make it more easy to scoop out the avocado flesh, take a knife (you can easily use a dull dinner knife) and gently make cuts in the avocado flesh in a cross-hatch pattern, careful not to break through the avocado peel. Then use a spoon to easily scoop out the avocado pieces.\nIf you are making guacamole, don't worry about slightly discolored or brownish sections. Scoop them up with the rest of the avocado to mash.\n3b To make avocado slices, use a knife to slice the inside of the avocado halves into sections. Don't worry if you cut right through the peel.\n4 Use your fingers to separate the avocado segments from the peel.\n  Hello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint"
