b'Print\nBay Shrimp and Avocado Salad Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesYield: Serves 4\nBay shrimp are also called Maine shrimp or boreal shrimp. They are sustainably harvested and they come already shelled and cooked.\nINGREDIENTS\n1/4 cup of white wine vinegar\n1/4 cup extra virgin olive oil\n1 green onion, thinly sliced\nPinch of salt\n3/4 pound cooked bay shrimp or extra small shrimp that are cooked, peeled, and de-veined, most of the shrimp roughly chopped\n3 ripe avocados\nLettuce - preferably butter lettuce or red leaf lettuce\nOptional\n2 tablespoons chopped roasted hazelnuts, almonds, or pistachios\n1 tablespoon chopped cilantro\nLemon slices for garnish\nMETHOD\n1 Whisk together the oil, vinegar, chopped green onion and salt in a medium bowl. Add the shrimp and toss to coat with the dressing.\n2 Arrange leaves of lettuce on individual plates. Cut two of the avocados in half and remove pits. (See How to Peel and Cut an Avocado.) With a spoon, carefully scoop out avocado halves from their skins in one piece. Place avocado half on plate with lettuce.\nPeel and chop the remaining avocado and mix it with the shrimp.\n3 Spoon shrimp mixture onto avocado. Sprinkle with nuts and/or cilantro if using.\nServe with lemon slices for garnish.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'
b'Print\nSalmon Avocado Poke Bowl Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesYield: 2 to 3 servings\nI use short-grain white rice (sometimes also called "sushi rice") in my bowls, but it\'s fine to use medium- or long-grain rice if that\'s what you have in your kitchen.\nGluten-free option: Substitute 3 tablespoons of tamari for the soy sauce. Because of the deeper color of the tamari, your salmon may not look as vibrant once mixed with the dressing.\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the poke bowl:\n1 cup short-grain white rice\n1 pound sashimi-grade salmon\n1/4 cup soy sauce\n1 1/2 tablespoons rice vinegar\n1/2 tablespoon sugar\n1 teaspoon toasted sesame oil\n1/4 teaspoon garlic powder\n2 scallions, thinly sliced\nOther toppings for your bowl:\nSliced cucumber\nSliced radish\n1 large avocado, cubed\nFurikake\nRed pepper flakes\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Cook the rice: Start the rice first and prep the rest of the ingredients while it cooks. Rinse the rice a few times under cool water, rubbing it gently with your hands, until the water isn\'t quite so cloudy. Then cook the rice according to package instructions or in a rice cooker. Fluff and keep covered until ready to eat.\n2 Prepare the salmon: Gently pat the salmon all over to make sure that there are no pin bones still lodged in the fillet; if there are, use needle-nosed pliers to remove them. Cut the salmon into 1/2-inch cubes. Add the salmon into a medium bowl and set aside.\n3 Make the dressing: In a small bowl, stir together the soy sauce, rice vinegar, sesame oil, sugar and garlic powder. The garlic powder and sugar will not dissolve completely, but that\'s fine.\n4 Combine the salmon and the dressing: Add the sliced scallions to the bowl with the salmon, saving 1 to 2 tablespoons for garnish. Add the soy sauce mixture to the salmon and scallions. Using a large spoon or a rubber spatula, gently mix the salmon with the soy sauce mixture.\n5 Serve: Divide the rice between each bowl and then the salmon. Top with the rest of the sliced scallions, sliced cucumber, sliced radishes, diced avocado, furikake and red pepper flakes, if you like. The poke bowl is best enjoyed immediately.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'
b"Print\nStrawberry Guacamole Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesYield: Makes about 2 1/2 cups\nWe've intentionally omitted chiles from this guacamole, but please feel free to add some if you want the heat! Just a serrano or half jalape\xc3\xb1o minced will do.\nINGREDIENTS\n2 ripe avocados, peeled and seeded (seeHow to Cut and Peel an Avocado)\n1/2 teaspoon salt\n1 Tbsp lime or lemon juice\n1/4 cup minced red onion\n1 cup chopped cored strawberries\n1/4 cup chopped sweetened dried cranberries (omit for paleo version)\n2 Tbsp chopped cilantro (optional)\nMETHOD\n1 Mash the avocados: Mash up the flesh of two avocados with a fork. Don't overdo it, the guacamole should have some texture.\n2 Add lime juice, salt, onion, strawberries, dried cranberries, cilantro: Stir in the lime juice and salt. Stir in the red onion, the chopped dried cranberries, and most of the strawberries (reserve a few chopped strawberries for the top).\n3 Adjust salt and lime juice to taste: Taste and adjust salt and lime juice if needed. Guacamole is all about balance of the creamy flesh of the avocado with the acid in the lime and the salt.\n4 Top with more strawberries: Serve topped with remaining chopped strawberries. Serve with tortilla chips\nTo store, cover with plastic wrap so that no air touches the guacamole, chill until ready to serve.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint"
b'Save It Print\nCrab Mango and Avocado Salad Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesYield: Serves 4\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the sauce:\n1 Tbsp extra virgin olive oil\n1 ripe mango, peeled, pitted and diced\n1/4 cup of water\n1 teaspoon freshly squeezed lemon juice\nSalt and freshly ground pepper to taste\nFor the salad:\n1 lb of fresh lump Dungeness crabmeat, picked through to remove the small pieces of shell or cartilage\n1 1/2 Tbsp freshly squeezed lime juice\n3 Tbsp extra virgin olive oil\n1 Tbsp cilantro leaves, finely chopped\n2 teaspoons mint leaves, finely chopped\n1 Tbsp minced shallot or purple onion\n1 medium sized mango, peeled, pitted, and diced (See How to Cut a Mango)\n1 firm but ripe avocado, pitted, peeled, and diced\nTabasco sauce\nSalt and freshly ground pepper to taste\nOptional: ruby red grapefruit sections, peeled\nMETHOD\n1 Make the sauce: Heat 1 Tbsp extra virgin olive oil in a small pan over medium heat. Add dice mango from 1 whole mango, season with salt and pepper. Cook, stirring, for about 3 minutes until the fruit is very tender.\nAdd 1/4 cup water, bring to a boil and remove from heat. Stir in 1 teaspoon of lemon juice.\nPour the mixture into a blender and pur\xc3\xa9e until smooth. Chill.\nAlternatively, if you are pressed for time, put all of the sauce ingredients into a blender and pur\xc3\xa9e.\n2 Gently combine crab meat with mint, shallots, lime juice, olive oil, cilantro, tabasco: In a bowl place the crab meat, 2 teaspoons of the cilantro, 1 teaspoon of the mint, the chopped shallot, a Tbsp of lime juice, 2 Tbsp of extra virgin olive oil, 10 drops of Tabasco sauce, and salt and pepper to taste. Mix carefully with a fork, to avoid breaking up the larger lumps of crab meat. Set aside.\n3 Combine mango, avocado, olive oil, lime juice, cilantro, mint, tabasco: In a separate bowl add diced mango from one whole mango, diced avocado, 1 Tbsp olive oil, 1/2 Tbsp of lime juice, the remaining cilantro and mint leaves, 10 drops of Tabasco, and salt and pepper to taste. Mix gently with a spoon, taking care not to mush the avocado pieces.\n4 Assemble the salad: Spoon some mango avocado mixture on to a chilled plate, gently mound some crab mixture over it. Garnish with cilantro leaves.\nFor a tasty added touch if you have them, arrange peeled sections of sweet ruby red grapefruit around the salads. The grapefruit provides a flavorful complement to the crab salad.\nAlternatively you can use small tureens or dessert bowls for individual molds, line the mold with plastic wrap, then layer the crab mixture and the mango avocado mixture. Chill in the refrigerator for 1 to 2 hours. When you are ready to serve, gently remove the salads from the molds onto individual plates.\nServe the sauce on the side.\nHello! b'Print\nAvocado Beet Salad with Citrus Vinaigrette Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 40 minutesYield: Serves 4\nINGREDIENTS\n4 medium-sized beets (any color), green tops removed, beets scrubbed clean\n1 just ripe avocado\n4 ounces mixed green lettuces\n2 tablespoons pistachios, chopped\nCitrus Vinaigrette:\n1 tablespoon minced shallot\n2 tablespoons rice vinegar (unseasoned)\n1 tablespoon fresh lemon juice\n1 tablespoon fresh orange juice\n2 teaspoons lemon zest\n1 teaspoon orange zest\nA Pinch of salt\n1/3 cup good quality extra virgin olive oil\nMETHOD\n1 Cook the beets: Place beets in a medium saucepan and cover with an inch of water. Bring to a boil and reduce heat to maintain a low simmer for 30 to 40 minutes, depending on the size of the beets, until easily pierced with the tines of a fork.\n2 Make the vinaigrette: Whisk together the citrus vinaigrette ingredients in a small bowl.\n3 Toss the beets in vinaigrette: When the beets are done, drain them, and peel off the outer skin. Cut the beets in half, and the halves into wedges.(Tip: use a plastic cutting board when cutting red beets. Red beets will stain wooden cutting boards.)\nPlace the beet wedges in a bowl and toss with a tablespoon of the vinaigrette.\n4 Cut and peel the avocado, cut the avocado into wedges (see how to peel and cut an avocado).\n5 Arrange the salad: Toss the salad greens with a half of the citrus vinaigrette. Arrange the dressed greens on serving plates.\nArrange the beet wedges and avocado wedges on top of the salad greens. Sprinkle with chopped pistachios. Drizzle remaining vinaigrette over the salads.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'
b'Print\nTomato, Onion, Avocado Salad Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesYield: Serves 6 to 8\nPro tip: slice the onion first and place in a bowl. Sprinkle with a little water and red wine vinegar. Then prep the other ingredients. Just a few minutes in a little vinegar water will help take the edge off of the onion slices.\nINGREDIENTS\n3-4 fresh large tomatoes, sliced\nKosher salt\n1/2 red onion, thinly sliced\n2 avocados, peeled and cut into bite-sized chunks\n1/4 cup chopped fresh parsley\n1 garlic clove, minced\n1 teaspoons crumbled dried oregano, or 1 Tbsp chopped fresh oregano\nRed wine vinegar (a good, strong red wine vinegar)\nExtra virgin olive oil (the best quality)\nFreshly ground black pepper\nMETHOD\n1 Layer tomatoes, onions, avocado, add parsley, garlic, oregano: Place a layer of sliced tomatoes on a large serving platter. Sprinkle with salt. Arrange the slivers of thinly sliced red onions and the chunks of avocado over the tomatoes.\nSprinkle with chopped fresh parsley, minced garlic, and crumbled dried oregano.\n2 Dress with red wine vinegar and olive oil, salt and pepper: Drizzle red wine vinegar and olive oil over the platter. Sprinkle with a little more salt and freshly ground black pepper.\nServe immediately or cover with plastic wrap and let sit at room temp for an hour or two before serving. Do not refrigerate.\nHello! b'Print\nBaked Salmon with Avocado Mango Salsa Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 10 minutesYield: Serves 4\nINGREDIENTS\nExtra virgin olive oil\n4 6-ounce salmon fillets\nSalt\nFreshly ground black pepper\n2 small or 1 large mango, not overly ripe (1 to 1 1/2 pounds of mango)\n2 just ripe avocados\n1/4 cup minced red onion\n1 serrano chile, minced (with seeds for more heat, without for less)\n2 limes, juiced (about 4 Tbsp lime juice)\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Preheat oven to 400\xc2\xb0F.\n2 Prep the mangos: While the oven is preheating, prep the mangos.  Either peel and then cut away the mango flesh from the core seed, and then cut the mango into 1/3-inch cubes, or follow the instructions here on How to Cut a Mango. Set the cut mango aside in a medium bowl.\n3 Bake the salmon fillets: Line a roasting pan with aluminum foil. Spread some olive oil on top of the foil. Coat the salmon fillets with olive oil and lay, skin side down, on the foil lined roasting pan.  Sprinkle with salt. Place in the 400\xc2\xb0F oven and cook for 10 minutes.\n4 Make the avocado mango salsa: While the salmon is cooking, prep the avocados. Cut the avocados in half. Remove the seeds. Score the inside of the avocados with a small knife in a cross hatch pattern. Scoop out the avocado pieces and add them to the bowl with the cut mango pieces. (See How to Cut and Peel and Avocado.)\nAdd the minced red onion, serrano chile, and lime juice to the bowl. Sprinkle with a little salt. Gently fold the ingredients together.\nServe the salmon fillets with a generous portion of avocado mango salsa.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'
b'Print\nSpicy Three-Chile Guacamole Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesYield: 6 servings\nINGREDIENTS\n2 poblano peppers (approx. 6\xe2\x80\x9d long)\n4 serrano peppers (3-4\xe2\x80\x9d long)\n2 jalape\xc3\xb1o peppers (3-4\xe2\x80\x9d long)\n4 ripe avocados\n1 1/2 teaspoons of lime juice\n1/4 cup diced red onion\n1/4 cup chopped cilantro\n1 teaspoon ground cumin\n3/4 teaspoon kosher salt\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Preheat your grill or broiler: Set your oven\xe2\x80\x99s broiler or your grill\xe2\x80\x99s searing compartment to high. Roast the peppers for 7-8 minutes until the skins are charred and blistered, turning the peppers as they begin to shake, and the seeds inside make snapping noises.\n2 Steam the peppers and remove the skins: Once the peppers have been charred, remove them from the heat. Put the peppers into a shallow dish or bowl and cover them with a towel to steam.\nAfter the peppers steam, their skins are easy to remove. Use the back of your knife to scrape the charred, papery skins from the peppers, then discard.\n3 Dice the peppers: Once the skins have been removed, slice off the stem end of each pepper. Cut the poblano and jalape\xc3\xb1os in half lengthwise, then scrape away the white membrane and the seeds with the back side of your knife (this helps prevent scraping away valuable pepper flesh).\nBecause serrano peppers are so skinny, rather than slice them in half, use the back of your knife blade and drag it down the length of the pepper to push the seeds out from the cut end.\nDice the peppers into 1/4-inch pieces.\n4 Mash the avocados: Cut the avocados in half and remove, then discard the pits. Scoop the avocado flesh into the mixing bowl and use a fork or potato masher to smash the avocado into a semi-chunky paste.\nGently stir in the lime juice to help delay the browning of the avocado. Try to avoid stirring too much as it will break up the avocado.\n5 Finish the guacamole: Fold in the chiles, red onion, cilantro, cumin, and salt until the ingredients are well incorporated. Taste the guacamole and adjust the salt to suit your preference.\n6 Allow the flavors to meld: Press a piece of plastic wrap against the surface of the guacamole and cover your bowl with a lid. Refrigerate the guacamole for at least 15 minutes to allow the flavors of the chiles and the cumin to meld and deepen.\nEnjoy the guacamole within 3 days. Store leftovers covered in the refrigerator. If the guacamole browns, scrape off the brown layer and discard before serving.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'
b'Save It Print\nSpaghetti Pasta Carbonara Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 20 minutesYield: Serves 4-6\nThis recipe uses raw eggs, which are essentially cooked by tossing with hot pasta. They are not cooked to the point of scrambled though, just enough to thicken the eggs into a sauce.\nThe garlic is optional. It is not usually included in pasta carbonara, but it tastes great so we\'ve included it. By the way, "guanciale", or pork jowl, is traditionally used in this dish, so if you can get it, by all means use it.\nINGREDIENTS\n1 tablespoon extra virgin olive oil or unsalted butter\n1/2 pound pancetta or thick cut bacon, diced\n1-2 garlic cloves, minced, about 1 teaspoon (optional)\n3-4 whole eggs\n1 cup grated parmesan or pecorino cheese\n1 pound spaghetti pasta (or bucatini or fettuccine)\nSalt and black pepper to taste\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Heat pasta water: Put a large pot of salted water on to boil (1 Tbsp salt for every 2 quarts of water.)\n2 Saut\xc3\xa9 pancetta/bacon and garlic: While the water is coming to a boil, heat the olive oil in a large saut\xc3\xa9 pan over medium heat. Add the bacon or pancetta and cook slowly until crispy.\nAdd the garlic (if using) and cook another minute, then turn off the heat and put the pancetta and garlic into a large bowl.\n3 Beat eggs and half of the cheese: In a small bowl, beat the eggs and mix in about half of the cheese.\n4 Cook pasta: Once the water has reached a rolling boil, add the dry pasta, and cook, uncovered, at a rolling boil.\n5 Toss pasta with pancetta/bacon: When the pasta is al dente (still a little firm, not mushy), use tongs to move it to the bowl with the bacon and garlic. Let it be dripping wet. Reserve some of the pasta water.\nMove the pasta from the pot to the bowl quickly, as you want the pasta to be hot. It\'s the heat of the pasta that will heat the eggs sufficiently to create a creamy sauce.\nToss everything to combine, allowing the pasta to cool just enough so that it doesn\'t make the eggs curdle when you mix them in. (That\'s the tricky part.)\n6 Add the beaten egg mixture: Add the beaten eggs with cheese and toss quickly to combine once more. Add salt to taste. Add some pasta water back to the pasta to keep it from drying out.\nServe at once with the rest of the parmesan and freshly ground black pepper.\nIf you want, sprinkle with a little fresh chopped parsley.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'
b'Print\nBacon-Wrapped Stuffed Pork Tenderloin Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 20 minutesYield: 4 servings\nINGREDIENTS\n2 tablespoons olive oil\n1 medium apple, peeled and cut into small dice (about 1 cup)\n1/4 medium yellow onion, finely chopped (about 1/3 cup)\n1 tablespoon chopped fresh rosemary\n1 tablespoon chopped fresh thyme\n1 to 2 thick slices bread (enough to make 1/2 cup coarse breadcrumbs)\n1 tablespoon Dijon mustard\n1/8 teaspoon salt, plus more to taste\n1/8 teaspoon pepper, plus more to taste\n1 pork tenderloin (1 to 1 1/4 pounds)\n8 to 10 strips of bacon (about 12 ounces), cut in half\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Heat the oven to 450F. Have on hand a rimmed baking sheet.\n2 Make the stuffing: In a skillet over medium heat, heat the oil. Add the apple, onion, rosemary, and thyme, and cook for 7 to 9 minutes, or until softened. Meanwhile, pulse the bread slices in a food processor until you make coarse crumbs. You should have about 1/2 cup of breadcrumbs.\nRemove the pan with the onions and apples from the heat, and stir in the breadcrumbs, mustard, salt, and pepper. Set aside to cool briefly.\n3 Butterfly the tenderloin: Cut a deep lengthwise slit down the center of the tenderloin, stopping about 1/2-inch from the bottom of the roast. Open it up like a book. Cover with a piece of plastic wrap, and with a mallet or rolling pin, gently pound it until it is of an even thickness.\n4 Stuff the tenderloin: Spread the stuffing in a line along the center of the meat. Bring the edges of the meat together to return it to its original shape. Secure with toothpicks.\n5 Wrap the bacon slices around the meat: Lay out the bacon slices on a cutting board, overlapping them slightly. Place the tenderloin on top with the toothpicks facing up. Removing the toothpicks as you work, wrap the bacon slices around the pork to form a log. Place the tenderloin, bacon seam side down, on the baking sheet. \n6 Roast the tenderloin: Roast for 20 to 25 minutes, or until an instant-read thermometer inserted into the center of the meat registers 145F to 150F and the bacon is brown and crisp. If the roast is ready before the bacon browns, place the tenderloin under the broiler for 3 to 5 minutes to brown the bacon.\n7 Let the tenderloin rest for 10 minutes before cutting into slices. Serve with the pan juices spooned over top if desired.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'
b"Save It Print\nBean and Bacon Soup Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 1 hour, 30 minutesBean soaking time: 8 hoursYield: Serves 6 to 8\nIn this recipe we are making the bean soup starting with dry beans that we soak overnight. If you don't have time to soak beans overnight, you can put the beans into a pot of water, bring the water to a boil, remove from heat, and let sit for hour, and then drain. Pre-soaking the beans will help them cook faster.\nIf you would rather work with canned beans, use 3 to 4 15-ounce cans of drained white beans and cook them in step 3 for only 15 minutes, not an hour.\nINGREDIENTS\n1 pound dry Great Northern white beans, covered with a couple inches of water and soaked overnight\n5 ounces of bacon, cut into 1/2-inch wide pieces\n2 cups chopped onion (1 large onion)\n3/4 cup chopped celery (about 2 ribs of celery)\n3/4 cup chopped carrots (1 large carrot)\n3 cloves garlic, minced (about 1 tablespoon)\n6 cups chicken stock\n2 bay leaves\n1 Tbsp fresh thyme\n2 1/2 teaspoons kosher salt\n1/4 teaspoon black pepper\n3 Tbsp tomato paste\n1/2 teaspoon paprika\n1 ounce bacon (1 to 2 slices), cooked and crumbled for garnish (optional)\n2 Tbsp chopped fresh parsley for garnish (optional)\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Drain the beans: Drain the beans that have been soaking in water. (If you haven't already soaked the beans, and you don't have time to do so overnight, you can put them in a large pot of water, bring to a boil, remove from heat and let sit for an hour, then drain.)\n2 Cook the bacon and vegetables: Put the bacon into a large (5 to 6 quart) thick-bottomed Dutch oven on medium high heat. Let the bacon cook for a minute or two to start rendering out some of its fat, then add the chopped onion, celery, and carrots.\nLower the heat to low, cover and cook for 12 to 15 minutes, until vegetables are completely cooked through and softened. Add the garlic and cook a minute more.\n3 Add beans, stock, seasonings, simmer: Add the drained beans to the pot. Add the stock, the bay leaves, thyme, salt and pepper.\nIncrease heat to high to bring to a simmer, then lower the heat to maintain a simmer, partially covered, for 1 hour or until the beans are very soft.\n4 Add tomato paste and paprika: Stir in the tomato paste and the paprika. Cook for 5 more minutes.\n5 Pur\xc3\xa9e half the soup: Remove the bay leaves. Using an immersion blender, pur\xc3\xa9e most of the soup. You don't want the soup to be perfectly smooth, but you want to pur\xc3\xa9e enough of it so that the beans create a creamy base.\nAdd more salt and pepper to taste.\nGarnish with crumbled cooked bacon and chopped parsley to serve.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b'Print\nSour Cream and Bacon Deviled Eggs Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 30 minutes\nI use granulated garlic in this recipe because it mixes better into the egg yolk mixture and it doesn\xe2\x80\x99t have the raw bite of freshly minced garlic. If you don\xe2\x80\x99t have granulated garlic or garlic powder on hand, I would mix in 1/2 to 1 full tablespoon of minced onions instead.\nINGREDIENTS\n12 large eggs\n1/2 cup full-fat sour cream\n1 to 2 teaspoons Dijon mustard\n1/2 teaspoon kosher salt\n1/4 to 1/2 teaspoon granulated garlic\n3 to 4 strips of bacon\n1 1/2 tablespoons chopped chives\nGround paprika, to garnish\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Steam the eggs: Fill a pot with 1 to 1 1/2 inches of water. Place a steamer basket inside and bring water to a boil. Once the water boils, turn off the heat. Carefully place 6 eggs into the steamer basket. Cover the pot and return the heat to medium-high. Let the eggs steam for 15 minutes.\nUsing a slotted spoon, remove the eggs and place them in a bowl of ice cold water. Repeat with steaming the remaining 6 eggs. (Get the step-by-step tutorial for making steam-cooked eggs here.)\n2 Let the eggs sit in the ice water for 30 minutes: You may need to add more ice cubes if the heat from the first batch of cooked eggs melts the ice cubes and warms the water.\n3 Peel the eggs and slice each egg in half. Scoop out the egg yolks and place them in a bowl.\n4 Make the deviled egg filling: Using a fork, smash the yolks into small pieces. Add the sour cream, mustard, salt and granulated garlic and mix until you get a smooth mixture. Taste the filling and adjust the seasonings to your liking. Set the filling aside as you cook the bacon.\n5 Cook the bacon: Heat a frying pan over medium heat and cook the bacon to your desired level of crispiness. I usually cook mine for 5 to 6 minutes, until I see some browning on the bacon strips.\nUse tongs to remove the bacon from pan and onto a plate lined with paper towels. Let the bacon cool for a few minutes. Once the bacon is cool enough to handle, chop or crumble bacon strips into small pieces.\n6 Fill the deviled eggs: Fill a zip-top sandwich bag with the egg yolk mixture. Snip off one of the bottom corners and pipe the egg yolk mixture into the egg white halves. If you don\xe2\x80\x99t have a sandwich or piping bag on hand, you can also just spoon in the egg yolk mixture into the egg white halves.\n7 Sprinkle each egg with chives, paprika, and bacon bits. Serve immediately. Deviled eggs can also be refrigerated for a few hours before serving, but are best served the day they are made.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'
b"Save It Print\nBacon-Wrapped Shrimp Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 10 minutesBrining time (optional) time: 30 minutesYield: Makes 12 pieces\nYou'll need about 1 strip of bacon for every 2 shrimp.\nI highly recommend brining the shrimp first. The brine will help keep the shrimp from drying out in the time it takes for the bacon to cook.\nIf grilling, I recommend using long, flat skewers which make turning the shrimp on the grill easier. If you don't have flat skewers, I've used two thin bamboo skewers (soaked in water for 30 minutes beforehand) to the same effect.\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the brine (optional, but recommended):\n1/4 cup (Diamond Crystal) kosher salt (if using Morton's kosher salt, use only 3 tablespoons)\n1/4 cup sugar\n4 cups water\n1 cup ice\nFor the bacon-wrapped shrimp:\n1 pound (12 to 20 count), raw, peeled and deveined shrimp (tail on)\n2 tablespoons extra virgin olive oil\nZest from 1 lime\n2 tablespoons lime juice\n1/2 teaspoon chipotle powder or chili powder (less or more to taste)\n6 to 10 strips thin bacon, cut in half (half as many pieces of bacon as there are shrimp)\nSpecial equipment:\nSkewers (for grilling) or toothpicks (for oven)\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Brine the shrimp (optional, but recommended): Whisk the salt, sugar, and water until the salt and sugar dissolve. Add the ice and the shrimp, and let sit for 30 minutes (no longer). Remove the shrimp from the brine.\n2 Prepare grill or preheat oven: Prepare grill on high, direct heat (if grilling) or preheat the oven to 400\xc2\xb0F. If grilling and using thin bamboo or wood skewers, soak them in water first for 30 minutes.\n3 Season the shrimp: Mix together in a small bowl the lime zest, lime juice, olive oil, and chipotle powder. Stir the shrimp into the lime chipotle mixture; make sure each piece is well coated.\n4 Partially cook the bacon: Spread the bacon pieces out over several layers of paper towels on a microwave-safe plate. Cover with another layer of paper towel. Microwave on high until the bacon fat begins to melt but the bacon is still somewhat pliable, about 1 1/2 to 2 minutes.\n5 Wrap the shrimp with bacon: Working one at a time, wrap a half piece of partially cooked bacon around each piece of shrimp.\n6 Prep the shrimp for cooking: If you are grilling, thread the shrimp onto skewers.\nIf you are using the oven, secure each the bacon onto the shrimp with toothpicks. Place the bacon-wrapped shrimp on a foil-lined baking pan. Brush remaining lime chipotle mixture on the outside of the bacon-wrapped shrimp.\n7 Grill or bake the shrimp: Grill uncovered for 3 minutes on each side (less or more time depending on the heat of your grill), or bake in the 400\xc2\xb0F oven for 8 to 11 minutes, or until the bacon is lightly browned and the shrimp is cooked through.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b'Save It Print\nGoat Cheese Bacon Pops Recipe\nPrep time: 25 minutesYield: 1 dozen pops\nRegular sliced bacon is better than thick-cut bacon for this recipe since it crumbles more easily, but thick-cut is also fine if that\'s what you normally buy.\nPackages of goat cheese sometimes go by the name "chevre" in the store. Either is fine.\nINGREDIENTS\n6 slices bacon\n4 ounces goat cheese\n4 ounces cream cheese (lower fat is fine here, if you prefer)\n1 tablespoon mild honey\nPinch dried chili flakes (optional)\n1/3 cup dried cherries (cranberries, blueberries, or other tart dried fruit works well, too)\n1/2 cup lightly packed fresh herbs (I used parsley and chives)\n1/2 cup unsalted pecan halves\nSpecial equipment:\nAppetizer skewers\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Cook the bacon: In a skillet over medium heat, cook the bacon until crispy. Drain on a paper towel. This can be done several days in advance; store in the fridge until needed.\n2 Make the cheese mix: In a food processor, combine goat cheese, cream cheese, honey, chili flakes (if using), a pinch of salt and a pinch of pepper. Blitz for about 30 seconds, then scrape down the sides of the bowl and pulse a few more times to fully combine. Transfer to a small bowl and freeze for 10 to 20 minutes, until firm but not frozen solid. (The cheese can be mixed up to 2 days in advance; store in the fridge.)\n3 Make the bacon topping: While the cheese mix is chilling, clean your food processor to make your filling. Place the dried cherries in the food processor and blend in 1-second pulses until they\xe2\x80\x99re chopped into tiny bits. Add herbs and pulse another 5 or so times. Add bacon and pecans and pulse until the mixture looks crumbly. Do not over-mix or you will end up with bacony nut butter. Transfer coating to a bowl.\n4 Roll the cheese into balls: Remove the cheese mixture from the freezer and roll into twelve little balls (a scant tablespoon each). Wetting your hands in cool water helps to cut down on the mess.\n5 Roll the cheese balls in the bacon topping: Gently press the coating into the cheese to make it stick.\n6 Stick a small stick or skewer into your cheese balls and store in the fridge until you\xe2\x80\x99re ready to serve. The pops are best the day they are made, but will keep just fine in the fridge for several hours before serving.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'
b"Print\nBaked Potato Soup Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 1 hour, 30 minutesYield: Serves 4 to 6\nPotatoes love salt, so if you are using homemade stock or low sodium stock that isn't well seasoned, you'll need to add more to this soup to make up the difference.\nINGREDIENTS\n4 pounds russet potatoes (about 7 medium potatoes)\n1/4 pound thick sliced bacon, cut crosswise into 1/8-inch slices (lardons)\n1 large onion, finely chopped (about 2 cups)\n2 ribs celery, finely chopped\n6 cups chicken stock\n1 teaspoon kosher salt (more to taste)\n1/8 teaspoon of ground white or black pepper\n2 to 4 tablespoons heavy cream (optional)\nGarnishes:\nGrated sharp cheddar cheese\nSour cream\nMinced chives\nCrumbled bacon (from step 2 in method)\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Bake the potatoes: Scrub the potatoes clean and poke them all over with the tines of a fork or paring knife (this is so they don't explode from internal pressure building up as they cook). Place on a foil lined baking sheet and bake at 400\xc2\xb0F for 1 hour, or until easily cut through with a knife.\nRemove and let cool enough to handle. (To speed up cooling, slice them in half lengthwise.)\n2 Cook the bacon: Place bacon lardons in a large, thick bottomed Dutch oven (about 5 to 6 quart pot). Heat on medium high until the bacon starts to brown then lower the heat to medium.\nCook until the bacon has rendered most of its fat and the lardons are browned and crispy. Remove the cooked bacon and set aside.\nRemove all but 1 tablespoon of bacon fat from the pan. (Do not discard bacon fat in your sink, it will clog the drain. Pour the fat into a jar and let it cool and solidify. Then either scoop it out and discard it or use it for another purpose.)\n3 Cook onion and celery in the bacon fat: Add the chopped onion and celery to the remaining bacon fat in the pot. Cook for 2 minutes on medium high, then lower the heat to low, and cover the pot. Let cook slowly on low heat for 15 to 20 minutes.\n4 Scoop out baked potatoes, add it and chicken stock to pot: When potatoes are cool enough to handle, scoop out the insides to a bowl. Then add it to the cooked onion and celery mixture along with 6 cups chicken stock. Add a teaspoon of kosher salt.\nBring the soup to a simmer and reduce the heat to low.\nUse a potato masher to mash the potatoes into the stock.\n5 Pur\xc3\xa9e some or all of the soup: Cook the potato soup for about 5 minutes, then use an immersion blender to pur\xc3\xa9e about half of the soup if you want a slightly chunky soup, or pur\xc3\xa9e all of it if you want a smoother soup.\n6 Add cream: Stir 2 to 4 tablespoons of heavy cream into the soup if you want a creamier soup. Add more salt and pepper to taste.\n7 Top with grated cheddar, sour cream, chives, bacon: Pour into bowls and top with grated cheddar, sour cream, chives, and crumbled crispy bacon.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint"

b'Save It Print\nBrussels Sprouts with Bacon and Chestnuts Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 15 minutesYield: Serves 6-8 as a side\nChestnuts are delicious, but a major pain to roast and shell (have you ever exploded chestnuts all over your kitchen? I have). Canned (jarred more like it) chestnuts actually work better in recipes than the kind you roast and peel yourself. The texture and moisture content is more consistent. So, we suggest using canned roasted chestnuts for this recipe. You can of course roast and shell your own if you prefer.\nINGREDIENTS\n1 pound Brussels sprouts\n1/3 pound thick-sliced bacon or slab bacon, cut into 1/4-inch pieces or batons\n1 red onion, chopped\n20-25 canned roasted chestnuts, quartered or roughly chopped\n1/4 cup chicken stock\nSalt and pepper to taste\nLemon wedges to serve\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Prep the Brussels sprouts: Cut the Brussels sprouts in half and slice thinly, starting at the top of the sprout and working back toward the stem. Discard the hard tip of the stem side.\n2 Cook the bacon: Cut the bacon into pieces about 1/4 inch wide and put them in a large saut\xc3\xa9 pan over medium heat.\nWhen the bacon is browned, remove with a slotted spoon and set aside.\n3 Cook the onions in bacon fat, add back the bacon:  Remove all but 1 tablespoon of the bacon fat (do not put down the drain, see how to render bacon fat). Turn up the heat to high, add the red onions. Cook until the onions begin to brown, add back the bacon.\n5 Add chestnuts, Brussels sprouts, stock: Add the chestnuts and Brussels sprouts to the saut\xc3\xa9 pan with the bacon and onions. Add the chicken stock and toss to combine. Stir in about 1 teaspoon of salt, more or less to taste. Cook over high heat for 3-4 minutes. Add pepper to taste.\nServe hot with lemon wedges. Squeeze a little lemon juice over the sprouts right before you eat them.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. b'Save It Print\nSpaghetti with Tomatoes, Bacon, and Eggs Recipe\nPrep time: 5 minutesCook time: 15 minutesYield: Serves 4\nWhile the water for the pasta and the eggs heats up, cook the bacon, garlic, and tomatoes. Then poach the eggs while the pasta is cooking. It all comes together in about 20 minutes.\nINGREDIENTS\n2 tablespoons white vinegar, for poaching the eggs\n12 ounces (3/4 box) spaghetti\n6 slices (about 5 ounces) thick cut bacon, cut into 1/2-inch dice\n2 cloves garlic, thinly sliced\n7 to 8 (12 ounces) small (1 1/2-inch) tomatoes, quartered\n4 large eggs\n1/2 cup freshly grated Parmesan\n1/2 cup packed basil leaves, torn into pieces\nFreshly ground black pepper, to taste\nOlive oil, for garnish\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Bring two pans of water to a boil: For the pasta, bring a large pot of salted water to a boil (at least 4 quarts of water and 2 tablespoons of salt). For the eggs, fill a wide saucepan with 2 inches of salted water and bring to a boil. Add the vinegar to the saucepan for the eggs.\n2 Cook the bacon, garlic, and tomatoes while the water heats: In a large (12-inch) skillet over medium-high heat, cook the bacon until browned. Transfer to plate.\nAdd the garlic and the tomatoes, and cook, stirring often, for 2 minutes, or just until the garlic turns pale golden and the tomatoes soften slightly. Remove the pan from the heat.\n3 Cook the spaghetti: Add the spaghetti to the large pot of boiling water, and cook for 8 to 9 minutes, or until al dente. Remove 1 cup of the pasta water with a measuring cup.\n4 Poach the eggs while the pasta cooks: Line a tray or plate with a paper towel. Adjust the heat under the saucepan so that the poaching water barely simmers.\nCrack 1 egg into a small bowl or cup and, holding the rim as close to the surface of the water as possible, drop the egg into the water.\nRapidly repeat with the remaining eggs.\nDrag a wooden spoon around the edge of the pot to stir the water and gently release the eggs from the bottom.\nAfter 2 minutes, lift 1 egg from the water with a slotted spoon and test for doneness by pressing on the egg. The white should feel firm and the yolk should still be soft. Return to the water if necessary to complete the cooking. With a slotted spoon, transfer the eggs to the paper towel lined plate to drain the water.\n5 Assemble the pasta: Set the skillet with the garlic and tomatoes back over low heat. With tongs, add the cooked spaghetti. Add the cooked bacon, Parmesan, basil, salt, and pepper and toss together. If the spaghetti looks dry, add some of the reserved pasta water a few tablespoons at a time.\n6 To serve: Divide the spaghetti among 4 plates or shallow bowls and top each with a poached egg. Drizzle with olive oil and sprinkle with freshly ground pepper, if you like.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'

b"Save It Print\nHow to Render Bacon Fat\nCook time: 10 minutes\nIf you make more bacon fat than you end up using, just throw out the whole jar and start a new one.\nNever pour bacon fat down the drain! It will solidify as it cools and clog your drain. Either soak it up with paper towels and discard or pour the rendered bacon fat into a jar to save.\nINGREDIENTS\nStrips of raw bacon\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Cook bacon on medium low heat: Heat a large skillet on medium-low heat. Lay out several strips of raw bacon. Let the strips cook for 10 or 15 minutes, turning them occasionally.\nWhen the bacon strips are nicely browned and crispy, use tongs or a fork to lift them out of the pan and place them on paper towels (to absorb the excess fat) on a plate.\n2 Pour remaining fat into a jar: Pour the remaining fat in the pan into a jar, and put the jar into your refrigerator. The bacon grease will solidify to a slightly off-color white. When you cook bacon again, pull out the jar and add more of the excess fat to it.\nIf you want, you can strain out the solid bacon bits before pouring the fat into a jar. I find that these bits have plenty of flavor, so I don't bother to strain them.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"

b"Save It Print\nGerman Potato Salad Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 25 minutesCooling time: 20 minutesYield: 4 to 6 servings\nThis salad can be made up to a day ahead. It can also be easily doubled or even tripled.\nVegetarian variation: Instead of bacon, saut\xc3\xa9 the onions in butter or oil. b"Save It Print\nBBQ Bacon Jalape\xc3\xb1o Poppers Recipe\nPrep time: 30 minutesCook time: 40 minutesYield: 6 to 8 servings\nBe sure to let your cream cheese soften at room temperature for a half hour or so before you plan to assemble your poppers. This helps make it easier to mix with the other ingredients.\nDepending on the size of your peppers and how much you stuff them, you may have some leftover filling. This makes a great spread for crackers or made into sandwiches! \nOven Directions: Arrange the poppers on a baking sheet and roast at 425F until the cheese filling is hot and bubbly and the jalape\xc3\xb1os are tender, 10 to 15 minutes.\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the bacon:\n12 ounces (8 to 12 slices) thick-cut smoked bacon\n1 1/2 tablespoons barbecue sauce\nFor the filling:\n8 ounces plain cream cheese, softened to room temperature\n1 cup (about 3 ounces) coarsely shredded sharp cheddar cheese\n1 1/2 tablespoons minced fresh chives\n1 large clove garlic, minced\n2 tablespoons barbecue sauce\n12 medium-sized jalape\xc3\xb1os\nExtra minced fresh chives to garnish\n1 cup sour cream, to serve (optional)\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Preheat oven to 375\xc2\xbaF. Line a baking sheet with aluminum foil. Lay a few layers of paper towels on top of a cooling rack and place near the oven.\n2 Glaze and bake the bacon until crispy: Arrange the bacon in a single layer on the baking sheet. Brush with 1 1/2 tablespoons of barbecue sauce.\nTransfer to the oven and bake until crisp and caramelized, 15 to 20 minutes (begin checking around 15 minutes; the bacon could take up to 20 minutes to fully crisp depending on the brand and thickness).\nRemove the bacon from oven and drain for a few minutes on paper towels, then transfer to a plate to finish cooling. The pieces will stick to the paper towels if left for too long.\n3 While bacon cooks, prepare the filling: Combine cream cheese, cheddar cheese, chives, garlic and barbecue sauce in a small mixing bowl.\n4 Prepare the jalape\xc3\xb1o peppers: Wear gloves for this step if you are sensitive to pepper heat. Cut the jalape\xc3\xb1os in half lengthwise. Use a spoon to scoop out the seeds. You can leave the stems on (they make nice handles for eating!) or trim them off.\nArrange all the jalape\xc3\xb1os cut-side up on a platter or baking sheet.\n5 Stuff the peppers: Chop or crumble the bacon into small bits, then fold into the cream cheese mixture. Using a spoon, fill each of the jalape\xc3\xb1o halves with a big dollop of the cream cheese mixture, mounding slightly.\nAt this point, the poppers can be covered and refrigerated until ready to grill, up to 24 hours.\n6 Prepare your grill: For gas grills, heat the grill with the burners set to high and preheat for 10 minutes. When ready to grill, reduce the burners to medium.\nFor charcoal grills, fill a grill chimney with charcoal and light it. When the coals are hot (they should be covered with a layer of fine gray ash) empty the coals into the grill and push them to one side of the grill to make higher heat and lower heat cooking zones. Set the grate in place and cover the grill. Preheat the grate for 5 minutes.\n7 Grill the poppers: Brush grill grates with oil to prevent sticking. If you're using a charcoal grill, cook over the low-heat cooking zone.\nUsing tongs, place the poppers on the grill so they lay across the grates and don't fall through. If any of the poppers is leaning to the side, prop it up against a neighbor so the cheese filling doesn't start to melt out as the poppers cook.\nGrill until the poppers are seared on the bottoms and the cheese filling is hot and bubbling around the edges, about 10 minutes. Be careful of overcooking or the peppers will become too soft.\n8 Serve the poppers right away: Using tongs and a spatula in tandem to scoop up the poppers, remove from the grill and transfer to a platter. Serve immediately alongside sour cream, if desired. Discard the stems as you eat.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. b"Save It Print\nGrilled Bacon-Wrapped Stuffed Hot Dogs Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 11 minutesYield: Makes 4 stuffed hot dogs\nRecipe adapted from Mastering the Grill: The Owner's Manual for Outdoor Cooking by Andrew Schloss and David Joachim.\nINGREDIENTS\n1 teaspoon ketchup\n1 teaspoon Dijon mustard\n4 large hot dogs, knockwurst, or kielbasa\n1/2 ounce cheddar cheese, cut into long sticks\n2 tablespoons chopped onions\n1 cup prepared sauerkraut, drained, roughly chopped\n4 slices bacon\nVegetable oil\n4 long hot dog buns\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Prepare your grill for direct medium high heat.\n2 Slice open the hot dogs: Mix together the ketchup and mustard in a small bowl. In a separate bowl, mix the sauerkraut with the chopped onion, set aside.\nSlice open the hot dogs, down the center, lengthwise, forming a deep pocket in each, but not cutting all the way through.\nCoat the inside of each hot dog with the mustard ketchup mixture.\n3 Stuff the hot dogs: Place a strip of cheese deep within the pocket of each hot dog. Top with sauerkraut and onions.\nEncapsulate the cheese at the ends with the sauerkraut mixture as well, so that no cheese is exposed (otherwise it will drip out when cooking).\n4 Wrap bacon around each hot dog: Wrap a strip of bacon around each stuffed hot dog, securing with toothpicks at each end.\nMake sure you wrap tight enough so that the stuffing stays in, but not so tight so that when the hot dog expands will cooking the bacon would tear.\n5 Grill the hot dogs: Brush the grates of your grill with vegetable oil so that the hot dogs don't stick. If you have a grill screen (a screen with smaller holes so that small pieces of whatever you're cooking don't fall through the grill), you can use it, just coat it with vegetable oil first and pre-heat for a couple of minutes.\nPlace the stuffed hot dogs on the grill, stuffing side down. Grill for 2 minutes, until the bacon on that side is cooked, turn the hot dogs a quarter turn and grill for a couple more minutes.\nContinue to grill for a few minutes each on all sides until the bacon is cooked. Cover the grill in between turnings to help with the cooking.\n6 Grill the buns: During the last minute of cooking, open up the hot dog buns and place them open-side down on the grill to lightly toast.\n7 Serve: Remove the hot dogs and buns from the grill. Remove the toothpicks from the hot dogs. Place the hot dogs in the buns and serve.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Add the onions and saut\xc3\xa9 until softened and translucent, about 3 more minutes.\n2 Stir in the rest of the ingredients and pressure cook: Add the green beans, diced tomatoes and their liquid, water, salt, pepper, cayenne, and thyme. Give everything a good stir so all of the green beans are coated with some of the cooking liquid.\nSecure the lid on the pressure cooker. Make sure that the pressure regulator is set to the \xe2\x80\x9cSealing\xe2\x80\x9d position. Set the cooking time to 7 minutes at high pressure. (For stovetop pressure cookers, cook for 6 minutes at high pressure.)\nIt will take about 10 minutes for your pressure cooker to come up to pressure, and then the 7 minutes of actual cooking will begin.\n3 Release the pressure: Perform a quick pressure release by immediately moving the vent from \xe2\x80\x9cSealing\xe2\x80\x9d to \xe2\x80\x9cVenting\xe2\x80\x9d (be careful of the steam!). The pot will take a couple minutes to fully release the pressure.\n4 Serve the green beans: Use a slotted spoon to gently transfer the green beans to a serving dish. b"Save It Print\nPasta with Butternut Squash, Bacon, and Brown Butter Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 30 minutesYield: 4 to 6 servings\nINGREDIENTS\n1 pound butternut squash, cut into 1/2-inch cubes (about 4 cups)\n2 tablespoons olive oil\n1 teaspoon Morton\xe2\x80\x99s kosher salt\n1/2 teaspoon freshly cracked black pepper\n1 pound pasta, such as penne, rigatoni, or other short-shaped pasta\n8 ounces bacon (7 to 8 slices, depending on how thickly they are cut)\n1/4 cup sliced shallots\n1 stick unsalted butter (4 ounces/8 tablespoons)\n4 to 5 sage leaves\n1/4 cup freshly grated Parmesan cheese\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Roast the squash: Preheat the oven to 425\xc2\xb0F. On a rimmed baking sheet, combine the squash with olive oil, salt, and pepper on a rimmed baking sheet, and toss to coat.\nRoast for 20 minutes, tossing half way through to evenly brown. When it\xe2\x80\x99s ready, the squash will be soft and some of the edges will have browned.\n2 Cook the pasta: Meanwhile, bring a large pot of salted water to boil and cook the pasta to al dente, or according to package directions. Drain well and set aside.\n3 Fry the bacon: In a large, deep skillet (I used cast iron), put the bacon in a cold pan and cook over medium heat until crispy. Remove from the skillet and drain on paper towels.\n4 Cook the shallots: Place the skillet back on the stove, but with the heat turned off. Drain all but about 2 tablespoons of the bacon grease.\nAdd the shallots and cook in the residual heat from the skillet; this helps prevent the shallots from burning. If they don\xe2\x80\x99t seem to be cooking fast enough, turn the heat to medium-low and cook for just a couple of minutes until they start to soften and become aromatic. Transfer the cooked shallots to a large bowl.\n  5 Combine the bacon, shallots, squash and pasta: After the bacon cools, cut it into small pieces using kitchen scissors (or using a chef's knife), and combine with the shallots in a large bowl\xe2\x80\x94or you can use the stockpot you cooked the pasta in (I like to do this if it's just me and the boys).\nAdd the pasta and toss to combine. When the squash comes out of the oven, add the squash to this bowl and toss gently together.\n  6 Brown the butter: In a small saucepan, melt the butter over medium heat. Stir it constantly and keep an eye on it so it does not burn. (See here for full instructions on how to brown butter.) It will start to crackle, foam, and smell nutty. The color will deepen to a caramel/amber hue.\nAround when the butter stops foaming\xe2\x80\x94or at least it starts to subside\xe2\x80\x94and the butter turns slightly brown, add the sage leaves.\nRemove the saucepan from the heat as soon as the sage leaves start to curl. Pour the butter and the sage leaves into the bowl with the rest of the ingredients.\n  7 Combine all ingredients and serve: Toss everything gently together with a wooden spoon. Taste and add salt and/or pepper if needed. Serve immediately with freshly grated cheese over the top.\nIf you are feeling extra decadent, add a chunk of unsalted butter or a splash of extra virgin olive oil on top when you toss, or some of the reserved bacon grease.\nLeftovers keep for about 2 to 3 days and reheat fairly well. I like to add a bit of olive oil or water to the pot when I reheat it over low heat. (I try to avoid microwaving leftover pasta because it just makes it gummy.)\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"

b'Save It Print\nRoasted Cabbage with Bacon Gremolata Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 1 hourYield: 4 to 6 servings\nFrom Andrea Bemis:\n"This is one of our favorite winter side dishes, and we get rave re\xc2\xadviews each time we serve it for company. I\'ve brought back the bacon gremolata yet again because it pairs so nicely with the roasted cabbage. I hope you and your guests find as much joy and pleasure in this simple recipe as we do."\nAdapted from Dishing Up the Dirt by Andrea Bemis, copyright \xc2\xa9 2017. Published by Harper Wave, an imprint of Harper Collins Publishers.\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the cabbage:\n1 medium-sized head of cabbage (about 1 1/2 pounds)\n2 tablespoons olive oil\n1/2 teaspoon salt\nFreshly ground black pepper\nFor the bacon gremolata:\n3/4 cup roasted unsalted almonds\n4 strips (about 1/4 pound) good-quality thick-cut bacon\n3 tablespoons minced fresh parsley\n1 teaspoon freshly grated lemon zest\nPinch of kosher salt\nTo serve:\nFreshly grated Parmesan cheese\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Heat the oven to 400F. Arrange two oven racks in the upper and lower third of the oven.\n2 Slice the cabbage: Peel off one or two of the thin, limp outer layers of the cabbage. Trim the stem so that it is flush with the bottom of the cabbage (if it isn\'t already).\nSet the cabbage upright and slice into 1-inch thick slices. Don\'t worry if a few of the outer layers unfurl or fall away.\n3 Brush the cabbage slices with olive oil: Use a pastry brush to cover both sides of the cabbage slices with olive oil, or use your fingers to rub the oil in. Season both sides with a little salt and pepper.\n4 Roast the cabbage: Arrange the cabbage slices in a single layer on a baking sheet. Roast on the lower oven rack for 35 to 45 minutes, flipping the slices halfway through cooking.\nWhen done, both sides should be seared an even golden-brown with crispy edges and the center of the slices should be tender.\n5 While the cabbage is roasting, prepare the bacon gremolata. If using unroasted almonds, arrange them on another sheet pan and roast in the upper part of the oven for about 10 minutes, until toasted and fragrant. Remove from the oven, cool briefly, then finely chop using a chef\'s knife (or pulse a few times in a food processor, but be careful not to over process or you\'ll make almond butter!)\nCook the bacon in a skillet over medium heat until very crispy. Transfer to a plate lined with paper towels to drain. When cool, roughly chop.\nCombine the chopped almonds, chopped bacon, minced parsley, lemon zest, and a pinch of kosher salt in a small mixing bowl. Toss to combine and set aside. (This bacon gremolata can be prepared ahead and kept refrigerated in an airtight container for about a week.)\n6 To serve: As soon as the cabbage slices are done roasting, transfer to a serving platter or individual plates. Sprinkle with a few spoonfuls of bacon gremolata and grated Parmesan cheese. Serve warm.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'
b'Save It Print\nBLT with Arugula Recipe\nCook time: 15 minutesYield: Makes one BLT sandwich\nINGREDIENTS\n2-3 slices thick smoked bacon\n1-2 thin slices of a fresh, large tomato\n1-2 ounces (a couple handfuls) fresh baby arugula (can substitute watercress)\n2 slices of bread\nMayonnaise\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Cook the bacon: Heat a large saut\xc3\xa9 pan or cast iron pan on medium low heat. Lay the strips of bacon in a single layer on the pan. Slowly cook the bacon, rendering out the fat, until lightly browned on one side. Using a fork or tongs, turn the strips of bacon over to cook the other side.\nWhen the bacon strips are sufficiently cooked remove from pan and place on a plate lined with a paper towel to absorb the excess fat.\nPour out excess fat from the pan (leaving about half a teaspoon in the pan) into a jar or a container to either dispose of or to store. (Never pour bacon grease down the sink, it will clog your pipes.)\n2 Wilt the arugula: In the same pan, add handfuls of fresh baby arugula or watercress. Toss in the remaining remaining fat. As soon as the greens start to wilt, remove from heat and remove from the pan to stop the cooking.\n3 Toast bread, build sandwich: Toast bread slices in a toaster. Spread mayonnaise (or your favorite spread, butter will do too) over the slices. Layer the sandwich with bacon, sliced tomato, and lightly wilted arugula. Cut on the diagonal.\nEat immediately.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'

b"Save It Print\nOven-Baked Bacon\nPrep time: 5 minutesCook time: 20 minutesYield: 12 strips\nIf you use thick-cut bacon, plan to cook for an extra 5 to 10 minutes.\nINGREDIENTS\n12 strips bacon\n1/2 teaspoon ground black pepper (optional)\nSpecial equipment:\nWire baking rack\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Prep the bacon: If you have an oven-safe baking rack, place it inside a sheet pan. (For even easier clean-up, you can also line the sheet pan with foil.)\nLay out the bacon strips on the wire rack. Make sure they don\xe2\x80\x99t overlap. Sprinkle bacon strips with black pepper, if you want.\n2 Bake the bacon: Place the bacon in a cold oven, and set the oven temperature to 375\xc2\xb0F. Bake the bacon in the oven for 15-20 minutes total.\nIf you are doing more than one pan of bacon, rotate sheet pans from top to bottom halfway through. If you are not using a baking rack, flip the bacon strips halfway through cooking.\nStart checking the bacon around 18 minutes, as some bacon cooks faster depending on the fat content. The bacon is done when it turns a dark tan color. Remember that the bacon crisps up as it cools, so don't worry if it's not completely crispy when you take it out of the oven.\n3 Drain and cool: When the bacon comes out of the oven, place it on a few paper towels to drain and cool. If you like, pour off the bacon grease from the pan and save it for cooking. (I love to cook eggs in my bacon grease!)\n4 Store the bacon: Bacon can be kept in the fridge for a few days and reheats well in a skillet over low heat. You can also freeze the bacon if you made a big batch. Just make sure to freeze the strips individually, or in between pieces of parchment paper, so they don't stick together.\nHello! b"Print\nHow to Make Candied Bacon\nPrep time: 5 minutesCook time: 25 minutesYield: 12 strips, serves 4 to 6\nThis recipe is easily doubled. Space the bacon as closely together as you can on the two baking sheets. It's okay if they touch in places, but don't let them overlap.\nMAPLE BACON ALTERNATIVE: As an alternative to the standard recipe, stir two tablespoons of maple syrup into the brown sugar and brush this onto the bacon before baking. Bake just as you would the normal version.\nINGREDIENTS\n12 strips bacon (not thick-cut, about one pound)\n1/4 cup light brown sugar\n1/2 teaspoon freshly ground black pepper (optional)\nSpecial equipment:\n2 baking sheets\n2 oven-safe wire racks\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Prep the bacon: Preheat oven to 375\xc2\xb0 F with one rack in the top third and another rack in the bottom third of the oven. Line two baking sheets with foil, and place an oven-safe wire rack on each. Lay out the bacon strips perpendicular to the lines on the wire rack, divided between the two pans and making sure they don\xe2\x80\x99t overlap. (If you lay them out parallel to the rack, the bacon may fall through the cracks while cooking!)\nSprinkle the bacon strips with brown sugar and (optionally) add some freshly ground black pepper. I like to use about 1 teaspoon of brown sugar per bacon strip, spreading it out along the length of the strip.\n2 Bake the candied bacon: Bake the bacon in the oven for 20 to 25 minutes. I recommend rotating the pans once during baking to ensure the bacon is cooking evenly. Start checking the bacon around 18 minutes, as some slices will cook faster, depending on the fat content and thickness of the slices.\nThe bacon is done when the brown sugar is melted and the bacon is a deep brown color. Remember that the bacon will continue to crisp up as it cools, so don\xe2\x80\x99t worry if it\xe2\x80\x99s not completely crispy now.\n3 Cool the bacon: Let the bacon cool right on the wire rack for a few minutes. (If you eat it right away, you'll burn your mouth on the molten sugar.) The bacon will crisp up as it cools and as the melted sugar hardens. Then serve!\n4 Store the bacon: Candied bacon can be kept in the fridge for a few days and reheats well in a skillet over low heat.\nI don\xe2\x80\x99t think candied bacon is worth freezing, although if you made a huge batch you absolutely could. You could just want to make sure to freeze the strips individually so they didn\xe2\x80\x99t stick together.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint"

b'Print\nEasy Potato Soup with Bacon Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 30 minutesYield: Serves 4-6\nINGREDIENTS\n6 strips bacon, chopped\n1 small yellow onion, diced\n2 stalks celery, diced\n2 medium carrots, peeled and diced\n1 parsnip, peeled and diced\n1/2 teaspoon salt\n1/4 teaspoon black pepper\n1/4 cup all-purpose flour\n2 cups whole milk\n2 cups vegetable or chicken broth\n1 1/2 pounds (3 cups) peeled and chopped Yukon Gold potatoes\nFresh chives, garnish\nFor the Crispy Skillet Croutons (Dad Add) \n2 cups chopped bread, cut into 1/4-inch cubes\n2 tablespoons olive oil\n1/4 teaspoon dried thyme\nPinch of salt and pepper\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Make the skillet croutons: In a small bowl, toss chopped bread with olive oil, dried thyme, and a pinch of salt and pepper. Toast croutons in a nonstick skillet over medium heat for 4 to 5 minutes, stirring occasionally. It\xe2\x80\x99s okay if the char on them becomes uneven. Some sides should be crunchy and some soft still. Remove and set aside.\n2 Cook the bacon: Add chopped bacon to a large pot over medium heat. Cook until fat renders out and bacon is crispy. Transfer the bacon to a plate lined with a paper towel and set aside as a topping for the soup. Reserve the bacon grease in the pot.\n3 Make the soup: Add onions, celery, carrots, and parsnips to pot. Season with salt and pepper and cook until vegetables soften, 3 to 4 minutes.\nStir in flour, cook for another minute, then add broth and milk. Slowly stir. Bring to a slight simmer, then add potatoes and simmer for about 15 minutes, or until potatoes are very tender.\n4 Blend half of the soup: When potatoes are very tender, remove half of the soup from the pot and let cool briefly. Blend until smooth and return to the pot, stirring it into the non-blended soup base.\nAlternatively, blend half the soup directly in the pot with an immersion blender; be careful not to over-blend! Some chunks are good. Taste the soup and adjust seasoning to your liking. Keep warm until serving.\n5 Serve: Serve the soup topped with fresh chives, crispy reserved bacon, and skillet croutons.\nLeftover soup keeps well in the fridge for up to a week, or you can freeze it for 3 months. Reheat gently on the stove with a splash of water.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'

Sprinkle the broccoli with more cheese and more broccoli or bacon depending on the size of the potato and the size of your appetite!\n6 Reheat the potatoes: Place the stuffed potato back in the oven for 5-10 minutes to really melt the cheese and warm the fillings.\n7 Serve: Top the warm potatoes with sour cream and chives and serve.\nLeftovers: Store any extra potatoes before filling them. Leftover potatoes can be used within a week for baked potatoes, loaded potatoes, or quick Dad Add home fries!\n8 How to Make Dad Add Home Fries: Cut a leftover potato into about 1/4-inch cubes. Into a medium skillet set over medium heat, add the olive oil. When the oil starts to shimmer, add the potato cubes and seasoned salt. Cook for 10-12 minutes, stirring occasionally, until the potatoes are crispy and browned on the edges. Remove from skillet and serve with eggs.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. b'Save It Print\nEasy Breakfast Casserole with Prosciutto Recipe\nPrep time: 25 minutesCook time: 45 minutesYield: 6 to 8\nYou can make and bake this savory strata all in one fell swoop, or assemble and refrigerate it the night before (but leave the cheese off until morning). Pull it out of the fridge 30 minutes before baking; add the cheese, and pop it into the oven.\nIf you have vegetarians at your table, feel free to skip the prosciutto and add one teaspoon of smoked paprika instead.\nThe strata holds up well as a leftover, so enjoy it for breakfast the next day, or pack up a slice for your desk lunch.\nINGREDIENTS\n1 tablespoon extra-virgin olive oil\n1 medium yellow onion, chopped\n2 big handfuls tender greens, such as arugula, dandelion greens, baby kale, or spinach (tough stems removed)\n1 1/2 cups asparagus, cut into 3/4-inch pieces\n1 teaspoon kosher salt, divided\n3 ounces thinly sliced prosciutto\n2 packed cups cubed crusty bread, such as levain, baguette, or Italian bread (slightly stale is ok)\n8 large eggs\n1 cup low fat cottage cheese\n1 cup 2% milk (or whatever kind you have in the fridge)\nFreshly ground black pepper\n1 1/2 cups (3 oz) grated cheddar, divided\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Preheat the oven to 350\xc2\xb0F.\n2 Saut\xc3\xa9 the vegetables: Add oil to a 12-inch ovenproof skillet set over medium heat. b"Save It Print\nSlow Cooked Boston Baked Beans Recipe\nCook time: 8 hoursYield: Serves 5-6 as a main dish or 10-12 as a side\nWhy pre-soak the beans? You don't have to (see this great Russ Parsons article in the LA Times about why you don't need to soak beans), but not doing so in this recipe will increase the cooking time. With the beans pre-soaked, they'll still take 8 hours to cook and soften in a slow-cooker. Once beans come in contact with the molasses, the sugar in the molasses will keep the beans firm. That's why they take so long to cook.\nINGREDIENTS\n1 pound (2 to 2 1/4 cups) dry white beans such as Navy beans or Great Northern beans (can also use kidney beans)\n1/3 cup molasses\n1/3 cup brown sugar\n3-4 Tbsp Dijon mustard\n1/8 teaspoon ground cloves\n3 cups hot water\n1/2 pound salt pork (can sub bacon), cut into 1/2-inch to 1-inch pieces\n1 medium onion, (1 1/2 cups) chopped\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Soak beans in water: Place beans in a large pot and cover with 2 inches of water. Soak overnight and drain. Alternatively, bring a pot with the beans covered with 2 inches of water to a boil, remove from heat and let soak for a hour, then drain.\n2 Mix molasses, brown sugar, mustard, ground cloves with water: Whisk together the molasses, brown sugar, mustard, and ground cloves with 3 cups of hot water.\n3 Add ingredients to slow-cooker, layering them, starting with the salt pork: Line the bottom of a slow-cooker (or a Dutch oven if you are cooking in the oven) with half of the salt pork (pick the fattiest pieces). Layer over with half of the drained beans. Add all of the chopped onion in a layer.\nTop with another layer of beans and the remaining salt pork. Pour the molasses water mixture over the beans to just cover the beans.\n4 Slow cook until beans are tender: Cover and cook in a slow-cooker on the low setting for 8 hours (or in a 250\xc2\xb0F oven), until the beans are tender. Check the water level a few hours in, and if the beans need more water, add some. Add additional salt to taste if needed.\nNote that fresher beans will cook faster than older beans. Your beans may be ready in less than 8 hours, or they may take longer. Best the next day.\nServe with Boston brown bread.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b'Save It Print\nBaked Beans in Tomato Sauce Recipe\nPrep time: 1 hourCook time: 2 hours, 45 minutesYield: Serves 8-10 as a side\nIf you want to save time, you can used canned beans instead of dry. Use 3 or 4 15-ounce cans, drained and rinsed and proceed to step 3. If you want a vegetarian version, skip the bacon, increase the olive oil, and use vegetable stock.\nINGREDIENTS\n1 pound dry cannellini, borlotti or Great Northern beans\n1 tablespoon extra virgin olive oil\n1/4 pound bacon or pancetta, roughly chopped\n1/2 medium onion, chopped\n4 garlic cloves, chopped\n1 tablespoon fresh sage, minced (can sub fresh rosemary)\n1/2 to 1 teaspoon chile flakes (depending on how spicy you want it)\n2 tablespoons honey\n1/4 cup tomato paste\n1 15-ounce can crushed tomatoes or tomato sauce\n2 cups beef or chicken stock (use gluten-free stock for gluten-free version)\nSalt\n1/2 cup chopped fresh parsley\n2 tablespoons balsamic vinegar\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Soak the beans in water: Pre-soak the beans, either by covering with two inches of water and soaking overnight, or by pouring boiling water over them and soaking them for an hour.\n2 Drain beans, cover with water, cook until tender: Drain the beans and put them in a medium-sized pot and cover with 2 inches of water. Bring to a simmer, cover, reduce the heat to a low simmer and cook until the beans are just soft enough to eat, about 1 hour, give or take 15 minutes or so, depending on how old the beans are (older beans will take longer to cook).\n3 Cook bacon or pancetta: Preheat the oven to 325\xc2\xb0F. In a 3 or 4 quart heavy-bottomed, oven-proof, lidded pot such as a Dutch oven, heat the olive oil over medium heat. Add the bacon or pancetta and cook slowly until lightly browned and crispy.\n4 Saut\xc3\xa9 onions: Add the chopped onions and increase the heat to medium-high. Cook, stirring often, until the onions begin to brown. Use a wooden spoon to scrape any browned bits off the bottom of the pot.\n5 Add garlic, chili flakes, sage, then add tomatoes and stock: Add the garlic, chile flakes and sage and cook for 1-2 minutes, then add the honey and tomato paste. Stir well to combine.\nAdd the tomatoes or tomato sauce and the stock. Bring to a simmer. Taste for salt and add some if needed.\n6 Add the beans, cover, cook in oven: Drain the beans and add them to the pot. Stir well.\nCover the pot and cook in a 325\xc2\xb0F oven for 1 hour and 15 minutes.\nIf still a bit wet, remove the cover and cook for 15 minutes more.\nNote that the cooking time will depend on several things, the most important being how thoroughly the beans were cooked to begin with when they were simmered.\nIf the beans are still a bit hard when they go in the oven, it may take several hours to soften them, once the tomato and honey have been added.\n7 Stir in parsley and balsamic vinegar: Right before serving, gently stir in the chopped parsley and balsamic vinegar. Taste for salt, add more if needed to taste.\nServe either hot or at room temperature.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'
b'Save It Print\nPressure Cooker Baked Beans Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCooking (including pressure release) time: 2 hoursYield: 8 to 10 servings\nThis recipe uses an electric pressure cooker. Pressure cooking times will be slightly less if you\'re using a stovetop pressure cooker.\nINGREDIENTS\n1 pound dried Great Northern beans\n1/3 cup molasses\n1/3 cup brown sugar\n3 tablespoons Dijon mustard\n1/8 teaspoon ground cloves\n8 ounces bacon, cut into 1/2-inch pieces\n1 medium onion, diced\nSpecial equipment:\n6-quart electric pressure cooker\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Par-cook the beans: Combine the dried beans and 8 cups of the water in an electric pressure cooker. Secure the lid on the pressure cooker. Make sure that the pressure regulator is set to the \xe2\x80\x9cSealing\xe2\x80\x9d position.\nIf you are using an Instant Pot, select the \xe2\x80\x9cBean/Chili\xe2\x80\x9d program, then adjust the time to 15 minutes. If your pressure does not have a \xe2\x80\x9cBean/Chili\xe2\x80\x9d program, set it manually to \xe2\x80\x9cHigh Pressure\xe2\x80\x9d for 15 minutes.\nIt will take about 20 minutes for your pressure cooker to come up to pressure, and then the 15 minutes of actual cooking will begin. \n2 Naturally release the pressure and drain the beans: When the timer goes off, wait for the pressure to release naturally for 15 minutes, then release the rest of the pressure by moving the pressure release knob from \xe2\x80\x9cSealing\xe2\x80\x9d to \xe2\x80\x9cVenting.\xe2\x80\x9d It will take a minute or two for the pressure to release completely.\nAt this point, the beans should be mostly cooked through, but still firm. It\'s fine if there\'s still a little bit of white at the center. If you\'d like to use some of the bean cooking liquid to make your baked beans, scoop out 1 1/2 cups of liquid and set it aside.\nWearing a pair of heat-proof mitts, lift the inner pot out of the pressure cooker and drain the beans into a colander in the sink. Wash out the pot and return it to the pressure cooker.\n3 Prepare the cooking liquid: In a small bowl, whisk together the molasses, sugar, mustard, ground cloves, and 1 1/2 cups water or reserved bean cooking liquid. Set aside.\n4 Saut\xc3\xa9 the bacon and onions: Reset the electric pressure cooker, then select its \xe2\x80\x9cSaut\xc3\xa9\xe2\x80\x9d program. Add the bacon to the pot and saut\xc3\xa9 it until it begins to render some fat, about 5 minutes.\nAdd the onions and saut\xc3\xa9 until they are translucent, about 5 more minutes. When done, hit "Cancel" to stop saut\xc3\xa9ing.\n5 Finish cooking the beans: Gently stir the beans and the cooking liquid into the pot with the bacon and onions. Secure the lid on the pressure cooker, again making sure that the pressure regulator is set to the \xe2\x80\x9cSealing\xe2\x80\x9d position.\nIf you are using an Instant Pot, select the \xe2\x80\x9cBean/Chili\xe2\x80\x9d program, then adjust the time to 15 minutes. If your pressure does not have a \xe2\x80\x9cBean/Chili\xe2\x80\x9d program, set it manually to \xe2\x80\x9cHigh Pressure\xe2\x80\x9d for 15 minutes.\nIt will take about 15 minutes for your pressure cooker to come up to pressure, and then the 15 minutes of actual cooking will begin.\n6 Let the pressure release naturally: When the cooking program finishes, let the pressure cooker completely release its pressure naturally. This will take about 30 minutes.\nDon\xe2\x80\x99t perform a quick release, as the thick cooking liquid will sputter out of the pressure release valve.\n7 Serve the beans warm: They are very good straight out of the pot, and taste even better the next day. Reheat beans over low temperature on the stovetop, in a low oven, or in the microwave.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'
b'Print\nThree Bean Baked Beans Recipe\nPrep time: 7 minutesCook time: 1 hour, 15 minutesYield: Serves 4 to 6\nINGREDIENTS\n1/4 pound sliced bacon\n2 cups chopped onion\n1 Tbsp dry mustard\n1 teaspoon minced fresh thyme (or 1/2 teaspoons dry thyme)\n3/4 cup ketchup\n3 tablespoons apple cider vinegar\n1/4 cup dark molasses\n1/3 cup water\n1 bay leaf\n1 15-ounce can red kidney beans, rinsed, drained\n1 15-ounce can black beans, rinsed, drained\n1 15-ounce can cannellini (white kidney beans), rinsed, drained\n1 teaspoon Tabasco\nSalt\nFreshly ground black pepper\nMETHOD\n1 Preheat oven to 350\xc2\xb0F.\n2 Cook and crumble the bacon: Cook the bacon in a large Dutch oven over medium heat until browned and crisp. Remove bacon and place on paper towels to soak up excess fat. Crumble up the bacon and set aside.\n3 Saut\xc3\xa9 the onions: Remove all but a tablespoon of the bacon drippings from the pot. Add the chopped onions and cook on medium high heat until translucent, about 5 minutes.\n4 Add the rest of the ingredients: Sprinkle the onions with dry mustard and thyme. Stir in the ketchup, vinegar, molasses, bay leaf, beans, Tabasco, and water. Add salt and pepper to taste.\n5 Cover and bake: Cover the pot and put into a 350\xc2\xb0F oven. Bake for 1 hour, checking every 15 minutes to stir and add more water if needed. Stir in the bacon the last 15 minutes of cooking.\nAlternatively, cook in a slow cooker 4 hours on high, or 8 on low.\nDiscard bay leaf before serving.\nHello!
