b'Save It Print\nRoasted Beets with Balsamic Glaze Recipe\nCook time: 1 hour, 15 minutesYield: Serves 6 to 8\nINGREDIENTS\n2 pounds red beets, medium sized, scrubbed clean, green tops removed (see beet greens recipe for what to do with beet greens)\n2 teaspoons extra virgin olive oil\nSalt\n1/2 cup balsamic vinegar\n2 teaspoons sugar\n1 teaspoon grated orange zest\nFreshly ground black pepper\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Preheat oven to 400\xc2\xb0F and line pan with aluminum foil.\n2 Prepare the beets: Place the beets in the pan. Rub olive oil over the beets, and sprinkle with salt. Cover the beets with another sheet of aluminum foil.\n3 Roast the beets: Roast for 1 to 2 hours, depending on the size of the beets and how old they are. After 1 hour, test every fifteen minutes by poking a beet with the tines of a fork. Once the fork tines go in easily, the beets are tender and cooked. Remove from the oven.\n4 Prepare balsamic glaze: While the beets are cooling, prepare the balsamic glaze. In a small, shallow saut\xc3\xa9 pan, add the balsamic vinegar and sugar. Heat on high until the vinegar has reduced to a syrup consistency. Remove from heat.\n5 Peel and cut cooked beets: After the beets have cooled for several minutes, but are still warm to the touch, peel off the outer skins and discard. Cut the beets into quarters or more bite-sized pieces.\n6 Pour glaze over beets: Place beets in a serving bowl. Pour balsamic glaze over the beets. Stir in grated orange zest, and add salt and pepper to taste.\nGarnish with a little orange zest to serve.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'
b'Save It Print\nKale Salad with Balsamic Dressing Recipe\nPrep time: 25 minutesRest in dressing time: 30 minutesYield: Serves 6 to 8\nSlightly adapted from a Dan Barber recipe that appeared in Bon Appetit in 2009.\nFeel free to sub out the pine nuts with toasted slivered almonds, and the dried sweetened cranberries with golden raisins. We use both interchangeably in this salad.\nIf you are using regular kale instead of dinosaur kale, you might want to let the salad marinate a bit longer, two hours or more, before serving.\nINGREDIENTS\n1/4 cup dried sweetened cranberries, chopped (or whole golden raisins or currants)\n1/3 cup pine nuts (can substitute slivered almonds)\n1 pound fresh Lacinato kale (also called Tuscan kale or dinosaur kale), about 2-3 bunches, rinsed and patted dry\n1/4 cup balsamic vinegar\n3 tablespoons olive oil\n1 tablespoon seasoned rice vinegar\n1 tablespoon honey\n1 teaspoon salt\n1/2 teaspoon pepper\n1/4 cup grated Parmesan cheese, packed\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Toast the pine nuts: Heat a small skillet on medium high heat. Spread the pine nuts in an even layer on the bottom of the pan. Cook, stirring occasionally, until lightly browned. Then remove to a bowl to allow to cool.\nHint when toasting nuts: do not take your eyes off of them! Nuts can go from browned to burned very quickly.\n2 Prep the kale: Use a sharp knife to cut out the tough midrib of each kale leaf, and discard or compost. Slice the leaves crosswise into thin, 1/4 inch wide, slices.\nThe easiest way to do this is to work with a small bunch of leaves at a time, stack the leaves and roll them into a loose cigar shape. Then using a sharp knife, work from one end of the "cigar" to the other, slicing a 1/4 inch off from the end.\nPlace the kale slices into a large bowl.\n3 Make the dressing: In a smaller bowl, whisk together the balsamic vinegar, olive oil, rice vinegar, honey, salt, and pepper.\n4 Dress the kale and toss with nuts and cranberries: A half hour to an hour or two before serving, toss the kale together with the toasted pine nuts, the dried cranberries, and the dressing, allowing the kale to marinate a bit.\n5 Right before serving, stir in the grated Parmesan cheese.\nHello! b'Print\nRoasted Brussels Sprouts with Pomegranate-Balsamic Glaze Recipe\nPrep time: 30 minutesCook time: 25 minutesYield: 6 servings\nThe pomegranate-balsamic glaze can be made ahead and will keep in the refrigerator for up to a month.\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the glaze:\n1 cup pomegranate juice\n2/3 cup balsamic vinegar\n2 tablespoons brown sugar\nFor the Brussels sprouts:\n1 1/2 pounds Brussels sprouts\n3 tablespoons olive oil\n1/2 to 2/3 cup pomegranate arils\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Make the glaze: Combine the pomegranate juice, balsamic vinegar, and brown sugar in a saucepan and bring to boil over medium heat. Reduce the heat to medium-low and let the liquid simmer for 25 to 30 minutes, until reduced to a syrupy glaze that coats the spoon. Stir occasionally. You should have about 2/3 cup of pomegranate balsamic glaze when done. (Once cool, store the glaze in the refrigerator for up to a month.)\n2 Preheat oven to 375F. Move the oven racks to the upper third and lower third positions. Line 2 baking sheets with parchment paper.\n3 Roast the Brussels sprouts: Trim the ends of the Brussels sprouts and slice them in half. Chop very large sprouts into quarters. Toss with the olive oil and a good pinch of salt. Divide the sprouts between 2 baking sheets and roast for 20 to 25 minutes, stirring halfway through.\n4 Toss the sprouts with the glaze: Let the Brussels sprouts cool for a few minutes before tossing them with 2 to 3 tablespoons of the pomegranate balsamic reduction and the pomegranate arils. Taste and add more glaze if you like. Serve immediately.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint'
b"Save It Print\nBalsamic-Glazed Red Onions Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 1 hour, 10 minutesYield: Serves 4\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the onions:\n4 medium red onions (1 1/2 to 2 pounds total)\n2 tablespoons olive oil\n2 tablespoons balsamic vinegar (See our Guide to Balsamic Vinegar)\n1 tablespoon plus 1 teaspoon chopped fresh oregano\n1/8 teaspoon salt\n1/8 teaspoon ground black pepper\nFor the glaze:\n1 tablespoon balsamic vinegar\n1 teaspoon Dijon mustard\n2 tablespoons olive oil\n1/8 teaspoon salt\n1/8 teaspoon ground black pepper\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Prepare the onions: Preheat the oven to 400F. Slice off any straggly roots from the onions, leaving the firm root centers intact. Cut the onions in half from tip to root. Peel off the skins until all the papery layers are removed. Cut each half into 4 wedges, slicing through the root so that the wedges stay intact.\n2 Pack onions into baking dish: Pack the onions as tightly as you can into a 1 to 1 1/2 quart baking dish (9-inch round or oval, 8-inch square).\nSprinkle the olive oil, balsamic, 1 tablespoon of the oregano, salt, pepper evenly over the top. (No need to stir or you'll disturb the pretty arrangement!)\n3 Roast the onions: Cover the baking dish with foil and roast the onions for 30 minutes. Remove the foil and continue roasting the onions uncovered for 30 minutes more.\n4 Make the glaze: In a bowl, whisk the balsamic, mustard, salt, and pepper. Gradually whisk in the olive oil.\n5 Pour the glaze over the roasted onions and return the dish to the oven. Continue cooking another 10 minutes, or until the onions are very tender when pierced with the tip of a knife.\n6 Sprinkle the onions with the remaining 1 teaspoon oregano before serving.\nHello! Add the shallots, spread them out in an even layer, lower the heat to medium low, and let them cook for 6 to 8 minutes, until softened and lightly browned.\n2 Add Brussels sprouts, garlic, balsamic: Preheat oven to 425\xc2\xb0F. Add the Brussels sprouts and the garlic to the shallots. Cook for 5 to 6 minutes more, until the sprouts begin to brown.\nDrizzle with 2 tablespoons of balsamic vinegar. Sprinkle with salt and pepper. Toss to coat.\n3 Bake in oven: Place in oven, uncovered. Roast at 425\xc2\xb0F for 15 to 20 minutes, until cooked through and caramelized on the edges.\n4 Sprinkle with balsamic, thyme, walnuts, salt, pepper: Remove from oven. Sprinkle with remaining 2 teaspoons of balsamic vinegar, the thyme, and toasted walnuts (if using). Stir to combine. Add more salt and pepper to taste.\nHello! b"Save It Print\nRoast Quail with Balsamic Reduction Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 20 minutesYield: Serves 2\nQuail, properly cooked, still have a blush of pink inside. They are delicate-tasting birds and need this delicate treatment to truly shine. If you are aiming for a temperature, 150\xc2\xb0F in either the leg or breast is ideal; quail are so small the whole bird will likely be the same temperature throughout.\nINGREDIENTS\n4 whole quail\n1 tablespoon extra virgin olive oil\nSalt\n1 celery stick\n1/2 cup chicken stock\n1/2 cup inexpensive balsamic vinegar\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Defrost frozen quail: If you are working with frozen quail, either defrost overnight in the refrigerator, or place the package in a large bowl and cover with a couple inches of room temperature water for 20 minutes.\n2 Truss the quail: Pre-heat the oven to 500\xc2\xb0F. Truss the quail with kitchen string. Cut off a length of string about 18 inches long. Cross the middle of the string over the quail's legs and bring the string around to the front of the bird, making sure it holds the wings close to the bird's flanks. Tie the string tightly around the neck.\n(Chowhound has an excellent video on how to truss a chicken, and quail are the same, only smaller.)\nAllow the quail to come to room temperature for at least 20 minutes.\n3 Arrange quail in roasting pan: Pat the quail dry with paper towels. Coat the quail with the olive oil and salt well. When the oven is hot, arrange the quail, breast side up, in a small roasting pan. Use pieces of the celery stick to keep the birds upright while they roast.\n4 Roast quail: Roast quail for 10-12 minutes in a 500\xc2\xb0F oven. Remove the birds from the pan and set aside on a plate to rest for 10 minutes, loosely tented with foil.\n5 Make balsamic reduction: As the quail are resting, make the sauce by putting the roasting pan on a burner set to medium heat. Discard the celery sticks.\nAdd the chicken stock and deglaze the pan by scraping all the browned bits off the bottom. Bring this to a simmer and pour into a small pot or saut\xc3\xa9 pan.\nAdd the balsamic vinegar, increase the heat to high and boil down to a syrup. Halfway through the boil, pour any accumulated juice from the resting quail into the sauce. When the sauce thickens and will coat the back of a spoon, it's ready.\n6 Serve: Serve the quail with the sauce drizzled over everything. Serve with a side of polenta, or rice pilaf.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b'Save It Print\nBalsamic Risotto with Tomatoes and Basil Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 35 minutesYield: Serves 3 to 4\nINGREDIENTS\n4 cups of stock (I use homemade vegetable stock or Better Than Bouillon)\n1 Tbsp butter\n1/2 cup chopped shallots\n1 clove garlic, minced\n1 cup (200 g) risotto rice (arborio, carnaroli, or vialone nano)\n1/3 cup dry white wine (I recommend a New Zealand Sauvignon Blanc)\n1/2 cup grated or shredded Parmesan cheese\n1 to 2 Tbsp balsamic vinegar\nWhite pepper\n1/4 teaspoon fresh thyme or a pinch of dried thyme\n1 1/2 cups cherry tomatoes, halved\n4 basil leaves, thinly sliced\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Heat the stock: Bring 4 cups of stock to a low simmer in a small pot. Keep the stock warm while making the risotto.\n2 Cook shallots and garlic: Melt a tablespoon of butter in a wide saucepan on medium heat. Add the chopped shallots and cook until translucent, a couple of minutes.\nAdd the minced garlic and cook until fragrant, a half minute more.\n3 Lightly brown the rice: Add the risotto rice to the pan and toss to coat with the shallots. Increase the heat to medium high and let the rice start to brown.\n4 Add the white wine: Stir in the white wine. The pan will steam up. Let the rice absorb the wine.\n5 Start adding the stock, 1/2 cup at a time: Here is the real process of making risotto. Add the stock, a half cup or ladleful at a time, slowly stirring the rice, and allowing the rice to absorb the stock for a minute or two, before adding another ladleful of stock.\nYou\'ll want to stop adding the stock when the rice is cooked through, but still a little firm to the bite, "al dente". Note that you may not need all of the stock you have heated for this recipe.\n6 Add balsamic, tomatoes, thyme with last 1/2 cup of stock: When it comes time for that last 1/2 cup of stock to add to the risotto, add it, as well as the balsamic vinegar. Balsamic vinegar can vary in its acidity and intensity. So, add 1 tablespoon to start, and add another tablespoon if you want more of the balsamic flavor.\nAdd half of the cherry tomatoes and add the thyme. Let the tomatoes soften with the cooking of the risotto in those last few minutes.\n7 Remove from heat, stir in Parm: When the risotto has reached it\'s "al dente" stage, remove it from heat. Stir in the shredded Parmesan cheese. Sprinkle with pepper.\n8 Serve: Serve with remaining halved fresh cherry tomatoes and thinly sliced basil on top.\n  Hello! b"Save It Print\nRicotta-Mascarpone Mousse with Balsamic Strawberries Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesChilling time: 2 hoursYield: Serves 8\nINGREDIENTS\n1 cup heavy whipping cream\n1 pound whole milk ricotta cheese\n8 ounces mascarpone cheese\n3/4 cup granulated sugar\nGrated zest of one lemon\n2 pounds strawberries, hulled and cut into quarters\n1/4 cup balsamic vinegar, or to taste\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Whip cream to soft peaks: In a medium bowl, beat the cream until soft peaks form.\n\n2 Beat ricotta mascarpone mixture: In a large bowl combine the ricotta, mascarpone, 1/2 cup of the sugar, and lemon zest. Half an hour before serving gently mix in the remaining sugar and balsamic vinegar. Make sure you don't let the strawberries sit in the balsamic vinegar much longer than 30 minutes before serving or the acidity of the vinegar will cook the strawberries.\n5 Assemble: When you are ready to serve, fill glass bowls halfway with the strawberries and their juices. b'Save It Print\nEasy Broiled Steak\nPrep time: 5 minutesCook time: 8 minutesMarinating time: 2 - 24 hoursYield: Serves 4\nIf your balsamic vinegar is very aged and thick, replace the 2 tablespoons balsamic vinegar with 1 tablespoon balsamic and 1 tablespoon red wine vinegar.\nINGREDIENTS\n2 tablespoons balsamic vinegar\n2 tablespoons soy sauce\n2 tablespoons extra virgin olive oil\n1 teaspoon kosher salt\n1 teaspoon ground black pepper\n1 teaspoon ground coriander\n1 teaspoon garlic powder\n1/2 teaspoon smoked paprika\n1 1/2 pounds (four 6-ounce) sirloin, ribeye, or strip steaks, about 1 inch thick\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Combine the marinade ingredients: In a small bowl or jar, stir together the vinegar, soy sauce, olive oil, salt, pepper, coriander, garlic powder, and smoked paprika.\n2 Marinate the steaks: Place the steaks in a gallon zip-top bag or a lidded container that just fits the steaks\xe2\x80\x94you want them to get cozy with the marinade. Pour the marinade over the steaks, turning them to coat the steaks on all sides. Close the bag or container, pushing as much air out as possible. Refrigerate and marinate the steaks for at least 2 hours, or up to 24 hours.\n3 Heat your broiler: Preheat your oven broiler to 550\xc2\xbaF (or as high as your broiler goes) with the oven rack in its highest position (about 4 to 6 inches from the broiler element), and line a baking sheet with aluminum foil.\n4 Dry the steaks: Pat the steaks dry with paper towels and place them on the lined baking sheet. Patting the steaks dry is very important\xe2\x80\x94you don\xe2\x80\x99t want a bunch of extra marinade on the steaks and the sheet pan, as it will just burn under the broiler.\n5 Broil the steaks: Broil the steaks for 4 minutes on the first side, then use a pair of tongs to flip them and broil for 4 minutes more on the second side. Use a digital thermometer to test for doneness.\nI aim for around 130\xc2\xbaF in the center for medium-rare to medium steaks\xe2\x80\x94they\xe2\x80\x99ll continue to cook a bit after you take them out of the oven. If the steaks are not yet done, flip and broil for an additional minute, and test again. (I usually end up broiling my steaks for 4 to 6 minutes per side, depending on their thickness.)\nIf the steaks are already charred after 4 minutes per side, but still undercooked in the middle, lower the oven rack a rung for the remainder of cooking, or even just turn the oven off and use the carryover heat to finish cooking the steaks for another minute or two.\n6 Rest and Serve: Transfer the steaks to a cutting board. Let them rest for about 5-7 minutes. Then plate and serve with your favorite side.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'
b"Save It Print\nInstant Pot Pot Roast with Balsamic and Rosemary Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 1 hour, 45 minutesYield: 4 to 6 servings\nStovetop Pressure Cooker Instructions:\nFollow the recipe as written, but lower the cooking time for the pot roast to 50 minutes at high pressure. Lower the cooking time for the potatoes and carrots to 4 minutes at high pressure.\nStovetop/Oven Instructions:\nPreheat the oven to 300\xc2\xb0F. Season the roast with the salt and pepper, then sear in a Dutch oven on the stovetop over medium-high heat. Remove it to a dish, then saut\xc3\xa9 the onions, garlic, and rosemary, then add the broth and vinegar as in the recipe below.\nAdd the pot roast back to the Dutch oven, then add enough water to come about a third of the way up the roast. Cover the Dutch oven with its lid and place in the oven.\nRoast the pot roast for 3 hours, or until it is tender, adding the carrots and potatoes during the last 1 1/2 hours of cooking. Check the pot roast every 45 minutes or so\xe2\x80\x94if too much liquid has evaporated, add an extra splash of water.\nINGREDIENTS\nOne (2 1/2 to 3-pound) boneless beef chuck pot roast\n2 teaspoons salt\n1 teaspoon ground black pepper\n1 tablespoon vegetable oil\n1 jumbo (12-ounce) onion, sliced\n4 cloves garlic, chopped\n2 (4-inch) sprigs fresh rosemary\n3/4 cup beef broth or vegetable broth\n1/4 cup aged balsamic vinegar\n1 1/2 pounds new potatoes (halved if over 1 1/2 inches in diameter, quartered if even larger)\n1 pound baby carrots (or regular carrots, peeled and cut into 1/2-inch rounds)\n1 tablespoon chopped fresh parsley, for serving (optional)\nSpecial equipment:\n6-quart electric pressure cooker, such as the Instant Pot\nFat separator\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Dry and season the roast: Place the roast on a dish and pat it dry with a paper towel. Season it all over with the 1 1/2 teaspoons of salt and pepper.\n2 Sear the pot roast on the top and bottom: Select the Saut\xc3\xa9 setting on your electric pressure cooker and heat the oil for 3 minutes, until the oil is shimmering. Using a pair of tongs, lower the pot roast into the pot and sear it for 4 minutes on top and bottom (8 minutes total), until browned. Transfer the pot roast back to the dish.\n3 Cook the onions and seasonings: Add onions and 1/2 teaspoon of salt to pot and saut\xc3\xa9 them for about 3 minutes, until they are a bit softened. Add the garlic and rosemary and saut\xc3\xa9 1 minute more, until the garlic is no longer raw. Add the beef broth and balsamic vinegar, then use a wooden spoon to nudge any browned bits from the bottom of the pot.\n4 Pressure cook the roast: Use the tongs to lower the pot roast back into the pot, and spoon some of the cooking liquid over the top of the roast.\nSecure the lid on your pressure cooker in its Sealing position. Cancel the Saut\xc3\xa9 program, then select the Manual or Pressure Cook program for 55 minutes at high pressure. (It will take about 5 minutes for the pot to come up to pressure before the cooking program begins.)\n5 Release the pressure: When the cooking program ends, let the pressure release naturally for at least 15 minutes, then move the pressure release valve from to Venting to release any remaining steam. \nYou can also leave the pot roast on the Keep Warm setting for up to 10 hours. You do not need to vent the steam.\n6 Rest the pot roast: Open the pot and use the tongs to transfer the roast to a cutting board. Cover the roast with aluminum foil to keep it warm.\n7 Strain the cooking liquid: Set a strainer over a fat separator in the sink. Wearing heat-resistant mitts, lift the inner pot out of the pressure cooker housing and pour the cooking liquid through the strainer and into the fat separator. (If you don't have a fat separator, you can pour the liquid into a ziplock bag, tilt it, let the fat rise to the top. Then, cut a hole in the bottom corner of the bag to let the liquid strain out, stopping before you get to the fat.)\nDiscard the rosemary stems, then add the strained onions, garlic, and rosemary leaves back to pot. Pour the liquid from fat separator back into the pot as well. Discard the fat.\n8 Pressure cook the vegetables: Add the potatoes and carrots to the pot and place it back in its housing. Secure the lid in its Sealing position.\nCancel the cooking program, then select the Manual or Pressure Cook program for 5 minutes at high pressure. (It will take about 15 minutes for the pot to come up to pressure before the cooking program begins.)\n9 Release the pressure: When the cooking program ends, perform a quick pressure release by moving the pressure release valve to Venting to release the steam.\n10 Serve: Open the pot, then use a slotted spoon to transfer vegetables to serving dish. Taste the cooking liquid for seasoning, adding salt and/or pepper if needed.\nRemove any string from the pot roast, then carve it into 1/2-inch thick slices. Arrange the pot roast on the serving plate with the vegetables. Ladle some of the cooking liquid over the meat and vegetables, garnish with parsley (if using), and serve.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b"Save It Print\nChocolate Banana Bread Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 1 hourYield: Makes one 9x5-inch loaf\nUse very ripe or over-ripe bananas. The peels should be at least half browned, and the bananas inside squishy and browning.\nDo not use Dutch processed cocoa for this recipe, only natural unsweetened.\nMelted coconut oil can be used in place of the butter. The flavor will change a little and you may get a hint of coconut in the result.\nThere is only 1 egg and 1 teaspoon of baking soda in this recipe for leavening, so make sure your baking soda is still good! (See more info on baking soda and baking powder.)\nINGREDIENTS\n3 large ripe bananas (easily mashable)\n1/3 cup melted butter\n3/4 cup brown sugar (packed, light or dark)\n1 teaspoon salt (1/2 a teaspoon if using salted butter)\n1 large egg, beaten\n1 teaspoon vanilla extract\n1 1/4 cup all purpose flour\n1/4 cup natural unsweetened cocoa powder\n1 teaspoon baking soda\n1/4 teaspoon ground allspice\n1/2 cup semi-sweet chocolate chips\nSpecial equipment:\n1 5x9-inch loaf pan\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Prepare pan and preheat oven:  Butter or spray with cooking spray the inside of a 5x9-inch loaf pan. Preheat oven to 350\xc2\xb0F (175\xc2\xb0C) with a rack in the middle.\n2 Pur\xc3\xa9e bananas: Using a blender, food processor, or a fork, pur\xc3\xa9e the peeled ripe bananas until smooth. You should have 1 1/2 to 1 3/4 cups of banana pur\xc3\xa9e.\n3 Mix wet ingredients and sugar: Place the banana pur\xc3\xa9e into a large mixing bowl. Stir the melted butter. Stir in the brown sugar and salt. Whisk to break up any clumps of brown sugar. Stir in the beaten egg and vanilla extract.\n4 Mix dry ingredients: In a separate bowl, vigorously whisk together the flour, cocoa, baking soda, and allspice.\n5 Add the flour mixture to the banana mixture and stir until just incorporated.\nStir in the chocolate chips.\n6 Bake: Pour batter into a buttered loaf pan. Place in a 350\xc2\xb0F (175\xc2\xb0C) oven and bake for 1 hour.\nNote that because of the chocolate chips that melt in the bread as it cooks, it's hard to check for doneness using a tester that you insert.\nOne way to test is to gently push the center top of the chocolate banana bread down with your finger. If it feels relatively firm and bounces back when you release your finger, that's a good sign that it's done.\n7 Let cool: Remove from oven and let cool for 10 minutes in the pan.\nGently remove the loaf from the pan and place on a rack to cool completely.\nSlice with a serrated bread knife to serve.\nHello! b"Save It Print\nBanana Sheet Cake Recipe\nPrep time: 20 minutesCook time: 20 minutesYield: Makes 30 pieces\nHere's a tip, leave the cream cheese and butter for the frosting out while you make the banana cake, that way they will be softened by the time the cake is cooled and ready to frost. This banana cake is on the sweet side (it is a cake after all).\nIf you are trying to cut sugars, you may want to experiment dropping the sugar in the cake mixture by a half cup and cutting the amount of frosting in half.\nINGREDIENTS\nCake\n2 cups all purpose flour\n1 teaspoon baking soda\n1 teaspoon cinnamon\n1/2 teaspoon salt\n1/2 cup (1 stick) unsalted butter\n1 cup white granulated sugar\n1/2 cup brown sugar\n2 eggs\nThe scraped insides of one vanilla bean, or 1 teaspoon of vanilla extract\n1 cup of mashed ripe bananas (2 large or 3 medium bananas)\n1/2 cup full fat sour cream\nFrosting\n6 ounces cream cheese, room temp\n4 Tbsp (1/4 cup) unsalted butter, room temp\n2 cups powdered sugar\n1 teaspoon vanilla extract\n1 teaspoon lemon juice\nMETHOD\n1 Preheat the oven to 350\xc2\xb0F (175\xc2\xb0C) . In a medium bowl, whisk together the flour, baking soda, cinnamon, and salt.\n2 Beat together in a mixer the butter and sugars. Beat in the eggs one at a time. Mix in the vanilla and mashed bananas.\n3 Mix in half of the flour mixture, then the sour cream, then the other half of the flour mixture.\n4 Spread batter evenly in a greased 10x15 baking pan. Bake at 350\xc2\xb0F (175\xc2\xb0C) for 20 minutes, or until nicely browned and the surface bounces back when you press it with your finger. Cool completely before frosting.\n5 To make the frosting, mix all of the ingredients together with an electric mixer. If too stiff to spread, add a teaspoon or two of water. Spread the frosting evenly over the cake and slice to serve.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. b"Print\nHummingbird Cake Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 50 minutesYield: Serves 12 to 16\nThe cream cheese frosting recipe can be cut in half if you prefer less frosting. If so, apply sparingly so there is enough to cover the entire cake.\nFeel free to use any favorite liquor, such as Grand Marnier, Triple Sec, Cognac, Armagnac, Brandy or even Bourbon. Or, simply omit the liquor and use 2 tsp vanilla extract.\n  INGREDIENTS\nFor the cake:\n3 cups all-purpose flour\n2 teaspoons baking powder (make sure your baking powder is still fresh!)\n1/2 teaspoon baking soda\n1 teaspoon salt\n1 teaspoon ground cinnamon\n1/2 teaspoon ground nutmeg (optional)\n3 large eggs\n2 cups granulated white sugar\n1 cup canola oil\n2 teaspoons vanilla extract\n1 (8 ounce) can crushed pineapple, with juice\n2 cups mashed bananas (from 3 to 5 bananas)\n1 cup finely chopped pecans\nFor the cream cheese frosting:\n1 pound cream cheese, softened\n1 cup (2 sticks) unsalted butter, softened\n2 pounds (32-ounces) powdered sugar\n1 teaspoon vanilla extract\n1 tablespoon Cointreau or other liquor (see Recipe Note)\n1 cup roughly chopped pecans, for topping (optional, toasted)\nEdible flowers for garnish (optional)\nSpecial equipment:\n3 9-inch cake pans\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Preheat the oven to 350\xc2\xb0 F. Butter and flour three 9-inch round cake pans.\n2 Whisk together dry ingredients: In a large bowl, vigorously whisk together the dry ingredients: flour, baking soda, baking powder, salt, cinnamon, and nutmeg (optional).\n3 Whisk together oil, sugar, eggs, then stir in pineapple, bananas, vanilla, 1 cup of pecans: In a separate bowl, whisk the canola oil, sugar, and eggs together until combined. Stir the pineapple, bananas, vanilla and one cup of the chopped pecans into the egg mixture and mix (do not beat).\n4 Fold wet ingredients into dry: Using a wooden spoon or spatula, fold the wet ingredients into the dry ingredients until just combined (do not over-mix).\n5 Pour into cake pans and bake: Pour the batter into the three prepared cake pans, taking care to divide evenly. Bake at 350\xc2\xb0F on center racks of oven for 20 to 25 minutes, or until a toothpick or knife inserted in the center comes out clean.\n6 Cool: Allow the cakes to cool in the pan on wire racks for 10 minutes.  After 10 minutes, run a knife around the edges and remove the cakes from the pans.  Cool completely on wire racks before frosting.\n7 Make the frosting: Beat the softened butter and cream cheese in a large bowl with an electric mixer. With the mixer on low speed, add the powdered sugar in small amounts until all is incorporated, then add the Cointreau and vanilla and beat until the frosting is light and fluffy.\nNote: Do not add the powdered sugar while the mixer is set on a high speed, or you will create a snowy mess of sugar all over your kitchen. (Please do not ask me how I know this.)\n8 Frost the cake: Place one layer, top down, on a large plate or cake stand (this creates a smooth surface on the top and results in a more level cake). Spread frosting evenly over the first layer, then repeat with the second and third layers, then frost the sides.\n3 Sprinkle with chopped pecans: Sprinkle the top completely with the remaining cup of chopped pecans (toasted or un-toasted). Alternatively, press the chopped pecans onto the sides of the cake and leave the top simply frosted.\nThis cake is best served the day it's made and can be kept, assembled and frosted, for a few hours before servings. If you need to serve it the next day or if you have leftovers, cover the cake as well as possible and refrigerate it. Remove it from the fridge and let it come up to room temperature for an hour or two before serving.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nPrint"
b'Save It Print\nCrunchy Banana Nut Granola Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 45 minutesYield: About 4 cups of granola\nI call for raw walnuts because they toast in the oven along with the granola, and nuts that have already been toasted can burn. If you can\xe2\x80\x99t find raw walnuts, you can sub raw almonds or pecans, or simply add toasted walnuts in the last 10 minutes of cooking.\nIf you like your granola in big clusters, spread the granola in a single, even layer on the baking sheets and do not stir during baking. This way, the granola will bake into one solid piece and you can break it up to clusters once cool.\nYou can store this granola in airtight containers for about a week, though it rarely lasts so long in our house.\nINGREDIENTS\n1/4 cup unsalted butter (If using salted butter, taste your mixture before adding salt)\n1/3 cup lightly packed light brown sugar\n1 tablespoon vanilla extract\n1 tablespoon water\n3 cups old-fashioned rolled oats (Certified gluten-free, if needed)\n3/4 cup chopped raw walnuts (See recipe notes)\n1/4 cup chia seeds\n1 tablespoon cinnamon\n1/2 teaspoon salt\n2 medium ripe bananas, diced\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Preheat the oven to 275F with two racks placed in the upper and lower halves. Line two baking sheets with parchment paper.\n2 Brown the butter: Slice the butter into small pats. In a small saucepan, melt the butter over medium heat. Once melted, the butter will start foam a bit, then it will begin to turn amber-colored and smell fragrant and nutty.\nWatch closely, as the butter can go from browned to blackened fairly quickly. This whole process should only take about 3 minutes.\nRemove the pan from heat immediately, and pour the melted butter into a small heatproof bowl.\n3 Melt the brown sugar: In the same saucepan used to brown the butter, add the brown sugar, vanilla, and water.\nStir over medium-low heat until combined, then cook until the brown sugar is thoroughly melted, 2 to 3 minutes. Remove from heat.\n4 Mix the granola: In a large bowl, mix the oats, walnuts, chia seeds, cinnamon, and salt until they are combined and the ingredients look well-distributed.\nAdd the melted brown butter and brown sugar mix and stir to combine. Then add the diced bananas and stir very gently.\n5 Bake the granola: Divide the granola between two baking sheets and spread into an even layer. Place into the warm oven and bake the granola for 45 minutes.\nHalf way through baking, stir the granola, then swap the top and bottom baking sheets and rotate the pans to avoid any hotspots. (If you want big clusters of granola, do not stir the granola.)\n6 Cool the granola: Remove the granola from oven and allow to cool for 20 to 30 minutes before stirring and serving. Store in airtight containers for up to a week.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'

Chill in the refrigerator until firm, 3 hours.\n5 Un-mold: To un-mold, fill a basin half-way with hot water. Carefully lower the bottom of the loaf pan into the hot water and hold for 5 to 8 seconds. This will melt the gelatin at the edge of the pan, helping it to release.\nRun a dull knife around the edge of the pan as well.\nPlace a serving platter topside down on top of the loaf pan and turn the whole thing over. b"Save It Print\nCoconut Banana Cream Pie Recipe\nPrep time: 1 hourCook time: 10 minutesChilling time: at least 4 hours or up to 24 hoursYield: 1 9-inch pie, serves 8 to 10 people\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the crust:\n12 whole graham crackers (about 200 g)\n6 tablespoons (85 g) unsalted butter\n3 tablespoons sugar\nPinch of kosher salt\nFor the custard:\n1/3 cup (66 g) sugar\n3 large egg yolks\n3 tablespoons cornstarch\n1 1/4 cup (295 ml) whole milk\n1 1/4 cup (295 ml) full-fat coconut milk\nPinch of kosher salt\n1 teaspoon vanilla\n1 1/2 cups sweetened shredded coconut, plus additional for the top\n2 medium ripe bananas\nFor the whipped cream topping:\n2 cups heavy whipping cream\n3 tablespoons powdered sugar\nSpecial equipment:\nFood processor\n9-inch pie plate\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Heat the oven to 350\xc2\xb0F.\n2 Make the graham cracker crust: Heat the oven to 350\xc2\xb0F. Break the graham crackers into a few pieces and place in the bowl of a food processor. Process the crackers until there are no large chunks left. The mixture should be sandy but not powdery.\nPour the crumbs into a bowl and stir in the melted butter, sugar, and salt. The mixture should be like wet sand and clump together when pinched.\nPress the crumbs firmly into the bottom and sides of a 9-inch pie plate to form a crust, using a measuring cup or glass to help you press firmly.\n3 Bake the graham cracker crust: Bake for 10 to 12 minutes or until the crust has started to turn a slightly darker brown color and smells fragrant. Remove from the oven and set aside to cool completely.\n4 Make the cream pie filling: Combine the sugar, egg yolks, and cornstarch in a medium saucepan. Whisk off the heat until they gain a little volume and turn a light yellow. Whisk in the milks and salt.\nPlace the pan over medium heat and whisk constantly until thickened, 15 to 20 minutes. (If this seems to be going really slowly, it's ok to nudge the heat up a little.)\nWhen the filling ready, the whisk should momentarily leave some visible trails on the surface before disappearing. Stir in the vanilla and shredded coconut.\n5 Transfer to pie crust: Spread half of the cream filling mixture into the cooled graham cracker crust. Slice the bananas and layer them on top, then cover with the remaining custard. Make sure to cover all the bananas (so they don\xe2\x80\x99t brown!).\nSmooth the surface and press plastic wrap directly on top.\n6 Refrigerate the pie at least 4 hours or up to 24 hours to set.\n7 Make the whipped cream topping: When ready to serve the pie, use a stand mixer or hand mixer to whip the cream until it holds soft peaks. Whisk in the sugar, and continue beating until the cream holds a medium peak. Generously dollop the cream over the top of the chilled pie. Sprinkle the top with extra shredded coconut.\nOnce assembled, the pie can be kept refrigerated for a few hours before serving. (Longer than a few hours, however, and the whipped cream can start to weep. It still tastes good, but is less visually appealing!)\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"

b'Save It Print\nVegan French Toast with Caramelized Bananas Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 30 minutesYield: 4 servings\nReprinted with permission from The Perfect Blend, copyright 2016 Tess Masters. Published by Ten Speed Press, an imprint of Penguin Random House LLC. (Photography copyright 2016 by Anson Smart.)\nINGREDIENTS\nFor the French toast:\n1 cup (240ml) unsweetened almond or macadamia milk (strained if homemade)\n1 ripe medium banana\n2 tablespoons pure maple syrup, plus more to serve\n1 teaspoon natural vanilla extract\n1 tablespoon white (or black) chia seeds\n1 teaspoon ground cinnamon\n1\xe2\x81\x844 teaspoon natural salt\n8 slices gluten-free sandwich bread\n1\xe2\x81\x844 cup (60ml) coconut oil (in liquid form), plus more as needed\nFor the caramelized bananas:\n2 medium bananas, thickly sliced on the diagonal\n1\xe2\x81\x844 cup (37g) coconut sugar\n1 to 2 tablespoons coconut oil (in liquid form)\nPure maple syrup, to serve\nOptional boosters:\n1\xe2\x81\x844 cup (60ml) bourbon or rum\n2 tablespoons crushed raw pecans or walnuts\n1 tablespoon unsweetened dried shredded coconut\nSpecial equipment:\nBlender\nMETHOD\n1 Set the oven to its lowest temperature or the \xe2\x80\x9cwarm\xe2\x80\x9d setting.\n2 Make the French toast batter: Combine the milk, banana, maple syrup, vanilla, chia seeds, cinnamon, and salt into your blender and blast on high for about 30 seconds, until well combined. Pour the mixture into a large shallow baking dish and let rest for about 5 minutes to thicken slightly.\n3 Soak the bread in the batter: In batches, place slices of the bread in the baking dish and let soak on one side for 8 to 10 seconds. Flip the slices and let soak for another 8 to 10 seconds, until evenly moistened.\n4 Cook the French toast: In a medium skillet (that fits two slices of bread) or on a large griddle (that holds all of the slices) over medium heat, warm 1 to 2 tablespoons of coconut oil per two slices of bread. (Resist the urge to use less coconut oil, or the bread won\xe2\x80\x99t get crispy.)\nAdd the bread and fry for 4 to 6 minutes on each side, until golden brown and crispy on the edges; you may need to add more coconut oil after you flip the bread. If cooking in batches, transfer the French toast to a lined baking sheet and place in the oven to keep warm, and repeat to fry the remaining bread, adding more coconut oil to cook each batch.\n5 While the last pieces of toast are cooking, make the caramelized bananas. Combine the banana slices and the coconut sugar in a zipper-lock bag, seal, and shake to coat evenly. In a skillet over medium-high heat, warm the coconut oil, add the coated bananas and the bourbon booster (if using), and fry for about 2 minutes on each side until nicely caramelized.\n6 To serve: Serve two slices of French toast on each plate, topped with one-quarter of the caramelized bananas, one-quarter of the crushed nut boosters, and one-quarter of the coconut booster. Pass maple syrup at the table.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print'

b'Save It Print\nVegan Banana Bread Recipe\nPrep time: 10 minutesCook time: 1 hourYield: 1 loaf (6 to 8 slices)\nIf you would like to make this recipe gluten free, swap out the all-purpose flour for equal amounts of a gluten-free flour blend.\nINGREDIENTS\n2 tablespoons flaxseed meal\n1/2 cup plus 2 tablespoons almond milk\n2 to 3 very ripe bananas, peeled\n1/3 cup walnut, coconut or avocado oil\n3/4 cup sugar (1/2 cup if you would like it less sweet, 1 cup if more sweet)\n1 teaspoon vanilla extract\n1 1/2 cups all-purpose flour\n1 teaspoon baking soda\nPinch of salt\nSpecial equipment:\n4x8 inch loaf pan\nMETHOD\n1 Preheat the oven to 350\xc2\xb0F. Line a 4x8-inch loaf pan with parchment paper, long enough so that it hangs over the edges and creates a sling. (This will help facilitate easy removal.)\n2 Make the flax egg: In a small bowl, combine the flaxseed meal with the almond milk. Let rest until thickened while you measure everything else.\n3 Make the batter: In a large mixing bowl, mash the ripe bananas with a fork until completely smooth. Stir the oil into the mashed bananas. Add the sugar, flax egg, and vanilla. Finally, stir in the flour, baking soda, and salt.\n4 Bake the bread: Pour the batter into your prepared loaf pan. Bake for 50 minutes to 1 hour, until a toothpick or cake tester inserted into the center comes out clean.\n5 Cool and serve: Remove the bread from the oven and let cool in the pan for a few minutes. Then, using the excess parchment hanging over the edges as handles, remove the banana bread from the pan, and let cool completely before serving. Slice and serve.\nHello! b"Save It Print\nChocolate Banana Bread Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 1 hourYield: Makes one 9x5-inch loaf\nUse very ripe or over-ripe bananas. The peels should be at least half browned, and the bananas inside squishy and browning.\nDo not use Dutch processed cocoa for this recipe, only natural unsweetened.\nMelted coconut oil can be used in place of the butter. The flavor will change a little and you may get a hint of coconut in the result.\nThere is only 1 egg and 1 teaspoon of baking soda in this recipe for leavening, so make sure your baking soda is still good! (See more info on baking soda and baking powder.)\nINGREDIENTS\n3 large ripe bananas (easily mashable)\n1/3 cup melted butter\n3/4 cup brown sugar (packed, light or dark)\n1 teaspoon salt (1/2 a teaspoon if using salted butter)\n1 large egg, beaten\n1 teaspoon vanilla extract\n1 1/4 cup all purpose flour\n1/4 cup natural unsweetened cocoa powder\n1 teaspoon baking soda\n1/4 teaspoon ground allspice\n1/2 cup semi-sweet chocolate chips\nSpecial equipment:\n1 5x9-inch loaf pan\nMETHODHIDE PHOTOS\n1 Prepare pan and preheat oven:  Butter or spray with cooking spray the inside of a 5x9-inch loaf pan. Preheat oven to 350\xc2\xb0F (175\xc2\xb0C) with a rack in the middle.\n2 Pur\xc3\xa9e bananas: Using a blender, food processor, or a fork, pur\xc3\xa9e the peeled ripe bananas until smooth. You should have 1 1/2 to 1 3/4 cups of banana pur\xc3\xa9e.\n3 Mix wet ingredients and sugar: Place the banana pur\xc3\xa9e into a large mixing bowl. Stir the melted butter. Stir in the brown sugar and salt. Whisk to break up any clumps of brown sugar. Stir in the beaten egg and vanilla extract.\n4 Mix dry ingredients: In a separate bowl, vigorously whisk together the flour, cocoa, baking soda, and allspice.\n5 Add the flour mixture to the banana mixture and stir until just incorporated.\nStir in the chocolate chips.\n6 Bake: Pour batter into a buttered loaf pan. Place in a 350\xc2\xb0F (175\xc2\xb0C) oven and bake for 1 hour.\nNote that because of the chocolate chips that melt in the bread as it cooks, it's hard to check for doneness using a tester that you insert.\nOne way to test is to gently push the center top of the chocolate banana bread down with your finger. If it feels relatively firm and bounces back when you release your finger, that's a good sign that it's done.\n7 Let cool: Remove from oven and let cool for 10 minutes in the pan.\nGently remove the loaf from the pan and place on a rack to cool completely.\nSlice with a serrated bread knife to serve.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
b"Save It Print\nBanana Nut Muffins Recipe\nPrep time: 15 minutesCook time: 25 minutesYield: Makes 12 muffins\nNo need for a mixer with this recipe.\nDon't want the nuts? Feel free to leave out or swap with chocolate chips.\nINGREDIENTS\n2 to 3 ripe bananas, thoroughly mashed (about 1 1/4 cup mashed)\n1/3 cup melted butter (salted or unsalted)\n3/4 cup sugar\n1 large egg, beaten\n1 teaspoon vanilla extract\n1 Tbsp strong brewed coffee or espresso, or a pinch of instant coffee granules mixed with a Tbsp of water (optional)\n1 teaspoon baking soda\nPinch of salt\n1 1/2 cup of flour\n1 cup chopped walnuts or pecans (toasted or raw)\nMETHOD\n1 Preheat oven, prepare muffin pan: Preheat the oven to 350\xc2\xb0F. Line a muffin pan with paper liners.\n2 Combine wet ingredients and sugar: Thoroughly mash the bananas in a large bowl. Stir the melted butter into the bananas. Mix in the sugar, egg, coffee and vanilla extract.\n3 Combine dry ingredients: Whisk together the flour, baking soda, and salt.\n4 Add dry ingredients into wet, add nuts: Add the flour mixture to the banana mixture, a third at a time, stirring until it is just incorporated. (Do not over-mix! Over-mixing will result in dense, tough muffins.)\nFold in the chopped walnuts or pecans.\n5 Fill muffin cups, and bake: Lightly spoon the mixture into a prepared muffin tin. Bake at 350\xc2\xb0F for 20-25 minutes.\nCheck for doneness by pressing down on the top of the muffin. If it bounces back, it's done. You can also test by inserting a skewer or other tester into the center of a muffin. If it comes out clean, it's done.\nCool on a rack.\nHello! All photos and content are copyright protected. Please do not use our photos without prior written permission. Thank you!\nSave It Print"
